Judge Accepting Private vs Public Invitations
Ruling on judge's acceptance of invitations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a judge accepting invitations, distinguish private from public invitations using the given criteria, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding relatives.

Core Idea
A judge must avoid private invitations to prevent suspicion; public gatherings are safe.

In this passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah, we examine the delicate matter of a judge accepting invitations. The rule is nuanced: public invitations like weddings are permissible, but private invitations create suspicion and are prohibited. An intra-Hanafi dispute arises regarding close relatives. By analyzing this passage, you will understand the governing principles and the criteria used to distinguish between private and public invitations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central ruling and its basis
Determine the general ruling for private vs public invitations and the underlying reason (suspicion).
The author states that private invitations are prohibited due to suspicion of partiality.
2
Distinguish between private and public invitations
Review the three definitions: (1) inviter's behavior, (2) number of invitees, (3) occasion type.
These definitions are provided by different mashayikh; the passage does not prefer one.
3
Locate the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf regarding relatives
Identify the positions of the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) and Imam Muhammad on a relative's private invitation.
The two shaykhs extend the prohibition to all relatives; Imam Muhammad allows it by analogy to gifts.
4
Evaluate the proofs of each position
Consider the dalil: the two shaykhs rely on the principle of avoiding suspicion, Imam Muhammad relies on qiyas to permissible gifts.
The text sides with the two shaykhs as the relied-upon view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ قاضی خصوصی دعوت قبول نہ کرے البتہ عمومی دعوت قبول کر سکتا ہے۔ کیونکہ خصوصی دعوت قاضی ہونے کی وجہ سے ہوگی ۔ اور اس کو قبول کرنے میں متہم ہوگا۔ برخلاف عمومی دعوت کے کیونکہ عمومی دعوت قبول کرنے میں قاضی متہم نہ ہوگا۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ اس حکم میں یعنی خصوصی دعوت قبول نہ کرنے میں قاضی کا قرابتدار بھی شامل ہے۔ یعنی قاضی خصوصی دعوت قبول نہ کرے دائی خواہ اجنبی ہو خواہ اس کا ذی رحم محرم ہو ۔ یہی شیخین کا قول ہے۔ حضرت امام محمد نے فرمایا کہ قاضی ذی رحم محرم کی دعوت قبول کر لے اگر چہ خصوصی دعوت ہو ۔ جیسا کہ اسکا ہدیہ قبول کرنا جائز ہے۔ اور دعوت عامہ اور دعوت خاصہ میں فرق یہ ہے کہ اگر داعی کو یہ معلوم ہو جائے کہ قاضی نہیں آسکے گا تو وہ اسکو ملتوی کر دے۔ تو یہ دعوتِ خاصہ ہے اور اگر ایسا نہ ہو تو دعوتِ عامہ ہے۔ اور بعض مشائخ نے فرمایا کہ دس آدمیوں سے کم دعوت خاصہ ہے اور اس سے بڑھ کر دعوت عامہ ہے۔ اور اگر ایسا نہ ہو تو یہ دعوتِ عامہ ہے اور بعض نے کہا کہ نکاح اور ختنہ کی دعوت ، دعوت عامہ ہے اور ان کے علاوہ دعوت خاصہ ہے۔
The author of Hidayah says that a judge should not accept a private invitation, but he may accept a public invitation. Because a private invitation would be due to being a judge, and in accepting it he would be suspected. Unlike a public invitation, because in accepting a public invitation the judge is not suspected. The author of Hidayah says that in this ruling, i.e., in not accepting a private invitation, the judge's relative is also included. That is, the judge should not accept a private invitation, whether the inviter is a stranger or his close relative. This is the saying of the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf). Imam Muhammad said that the judge may accept the invitation of a close relative even if it is a private invitation, just as accepting his gift is permissible. And the difference between a public invitation and a private invitation is this: if the inviter knows that the judge will not be able to come, and he postpones it, then it is a private invitation; otherwise, it is a public invitation. And some mashayikh said that an invitation of fewer than ten people is a private invitation, and more than that is a public invitation. And some said that the invitation for a wedding and circumcision is a public invitation, and other than these is a private invitation.
Source pages p. 263

Commentary
This section from Ashraf al-Hidaya discusses the judge's acceptance of invitations. The general ruling is that a judge may attend public gatherings but should avoid private invitations, as they create suspicion of partiality. The author (Sahib al-Hidaya) initially includes relatives in this prohibition, stating that even a close relative's private invitation should be refused. This is the view of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (the two shaykhs). However, Imam Muhammad differs, arguing that since a judge can accept a gift from a close relative, he can also accept a private invitation. Three definitions of 'private' vs 'public' are given: (1) based on whether the inviter would postpone the event if the judge were absent, (2) based on the number of invitees (less than ten = private), (3) based on the occasion (weddings and circumcisions are public, others private). The commentary doesn't specify which view is preferred, but the mention of 'Sahib al-Hidayah' and 'the two shaykhs' suggests their view is relied upon.

Key Terms
دعوت خاصہ (da'wa khassa): A private invitation where the inviter would only invite the judge and would postpone if the judge cannot attend.
دعوت عامہ (da'wa 'amma): A public invitation, open to many, such as wedding or circumcision feasts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), what is the ruling on a judge accepting a private invitation from his close relative?
A) It is permissible because family ties override suspicion
B) It is not permissible, as all private invitations are prohibited
C) It is permissible only if the relative has no case
D) It is recommended to accept to maintain family relations

Key Takeaway
A judge must avoid private invitations to prevent suspicion of partiality; public invitations are permissible, and the two shaykhs extend the prohibition to relatives.

Judge's Duties: Funerals, Sick Visits, and Impartiality
Lists the judge's social duties and a prohibition on partiality, with hadith proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rulings on a judge attending funerals and visiting the sick, and explain why he must not invite one litigant without the other, citing the hadith proofs.

Core Idea
A judge fulfills Muslim brotherhood rights unless they compromise impartiality — and must avoid even the appearance of bias.

Judges are not isolated from society; they have social duties like attending funerals and visiting the sick. However, these duties must be performed with care to maintain impartiality and avoid suspicion. This lesson explores the balance between fulfilling Muslim rights and preserving judicial integrity, based on the Quduri matn and supporting hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positive duties
The text states the judge should attend funerals and visit the sick. These are general rights of Muslims supported by hadith.
These duties are sunnah muakkadah generally, but for a judge they are recommended unless they cause suspicion.
2
Note the exception for visiting a sick litigant
The commentary clarifies that if a litigant (plaintiff or defendant) becomes ill, the judge should not visit him because it would cause distress to the other party and create suspicion of bias.
3
Understand the prohibition on inviting one litigant alone
The judge is prohibited from inviting only one litigant without the other. This is based on a direct Prophetic prohibition and the principle of avoiding suspicion (tuhamat).
This applies to any form of hospitality or private meeting.
4
Recognize the underlying principle
The overarching principle is that the judge must maintain absolute impartiality and avoid any action that could be perceived as favoring one party.
The hadith of the six rights of Muslims is cited to show that these acts are obligations, but the judge's special position imposes additional caution.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قاضی کے لئے جنازہ میں شرکت اور مریض کی عیادت کا حکم قال ويشهد الجنازة ويعود المريض لان ذالك من حقوق المسلمين قال عليه السلام للمسلم على المسلم ستة حقوق و عدمنها هذين ولا يضيف احد الخصمين دون خصمه لان النبى نهى عن ذلك ولان فيه تهمة ترجمہ اور قاضی جنازے میں حاضر ہو ۔ اور مریض کی عیادت کرے اس لئے کی یہ مسلمانوں کے حقوق میں سے ہے ۔ رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ مسلمان کے مسلمان پر چھ حق ہیں انہیں میں سے آپ نے ان دونوں کو شمار فرمایا۔ اور قاضی مدعی اور مدعی علیہ میں سے کسی ایک کی دعوت بغیر دوسرے کے نہ کرے۔ کیونکہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اس سے منع فرمایا ہے۔ اور اس لئے کہ ایسا کرنے میں تہمت ہے۔ تشریح صاحب قدوری فرماتے ہیں کہ قاضی، جنازے میں شرکت کرے اور بیمار کی عیادت کرے۔ کیونکہ یہ دونوں چیزیں مسلمانوں کے حقوق میں سے ہیں۔ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ ایک مسلمان کے دوسرے مسلمان پر چھ حق ہیں۔ ان میں سے ایک جنازہ میں حاضر ہونا بھی ہے اور ایک مریض کی عیادت کرنا بھی ہے۔ چنانچہ مسلم شریف میں ابو ہریرہ کی روایت ہے قال رسول الله حق المسلم على المسلم خمس رد السلام و تشمية العاطس واجابة الدعوة وعيادة المريض واتباع الجنائز واذا استنصحك فانصح له فهذه هي السادسة ۔ یعنی مسلمان کے مسلمان پر پانچ حق ہیں ۔ سلام کا جواب دینا، چھینک کا جواب، دعوت قبول کرنا ، مریض کی عیادت کرنا ، جنازے کی اتباع کرنا اور جب وہ تجھ سے نصیحت چاہے تو اس کو نصیحت کر ، یہی چھنا حق ہے۔ یہ خیال رہے کہ اگر مدعی یا مدعی علیہ بیمار ہو گیا تو قاضی اس کی عیادت نہ کرے۔ کیونکہ اس کی وجہ سے فریق ثانی کو اذیت ہوگی۔ حضرت ابوایوب انصاری کی حدیث کے الفاظ یہ ہیں۔ قال سمعت رسول الله يقول للمسلم على المسلم ست خصال واجبة ان ترك شيئاً منها فقد ترك حقاً واجباً عليه اذا دعاه ان يجيبه واذا مرض ان يعوده و اذامات ان يحضره واذا لقيه ان يسلم عليه واذا استنصحه ان ينصحه واذا عطس أن يشمته حضرت ابوایوب انصاری فرماتے ہیں کہ میں نے رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم کو فرماتے ہوئے سنا کہ مسلم کے لئے مسلمان پر چھ خصال واجب نہیں اگر اس نے کوئی حق تھوڑا تو اپنے اوپر حق واجب ترک کیا، ا۔ جب اس کو دعوت دے تو اس کو قبول کرے۔
Ruling on the judge attending funerals and visiting the sick: He said: He attends the funeral and visits the sick, because that is from the rights of Muslims. The Prophet said: 'For a Muslim, there are six rights over another Muslim, and he counted these two among them.' And he should not invite one of the two litigants without his opponent, because the Prophet forbade that, and because there is suspicion in it. Translation: And the judge should attend the funeral and visit the sick, because these are from the rights of Muslims. The Messenger of Allah said: 'A Muslim has six rights over another Muslim,' and he counted these two among them. And the judge should not invite one of the plaintiff or defendant without the other, because the Messenger of Allah forbade that, and because there is suspicion in it. Explanation: The author of Quduri says that the judge should attend the funeral and visit the sick, because these two things are from the rights of Muslims. The Prophet said: 'A Muslim has five rights over another Muslim: returning the greeting, responding to the sneezer, accepting the invitation, visiting the sick, and following the funeral; and when he seeks your advice, advise him — this is the sixth.' Note: If the plaintiff or defendant becomes sick, the judge should not visit him, because it would cause distress to the other party. The hadith of Abu Ayyub al-Ansari: 'I heard the Messenger of Allah say: A Muslim has six obligatory characteristics; if he leaves any of them, he has left an obligatory right upon him: when he invites him, he should respond; when he is sick, he should visit him; when he dies, he should attend him; when he meets him, he should greet him; when he seeks advice, he should advise him; and when he sneezes, he should respond (to his sneeze).'
Source pages p. 264

Commentary
This passage discusses three matters of judicial etiquette. First, the judge should attend funerals and visit the sick, as these are general rights of Muslims supported by hadith. The commentary cites multiple versions of the hadith listing the rights of Muslims. However, there is a caveat: if the litigant (plaintiff or defendant) is sick, the judge should not visit him because it would cause suspicion or distress to the other party. Second, the judge is prohibited from inviting only one litigant without the other, as this would create suspicion of bias. The proof is a direct prohibition from the Prophet and the general principle of avoiding suspicion. The commentary emphasizes that these rulings are in line with the Quduri's matn and are meant to uphold the judge's impartiality.

Key Terms
جنازہ (janaza): Funeral procession and prayer; attending is a right of the deceased Muslim.
عیادت (iyada): Visiting a sick person; a recommended act of brotherhood.
خصم (khasm): Litigant; either the plaintiff or defendant.
تہمت (tuhamat): Suspicion or accusation; the potential for bias.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, why should a judge not invite one litigant without the other?
A) Because it is a waste of time
B) Because it creates suspicion and is forbidden by the Prophet
C) Because the other litigant might get angry
D) Because it is not practical

Key Takeaway
A judge must balance fulfilling Muslim rights with maintaining absolute impartiality, avoiding even the appearance of bias.

Judge's Acceptance of Invitations: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on judge's invitation acceptance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a judge's acceptance of specific and general invitations, and distinguish the position of Imam Muhammad from that of the two shaykhs.

Core Idea
The judge must reject all specific invitations; only general invitations are permissible.

This passage addresses an important ethical boundary for a Muslim judge: accepting invitations. While general open invitations are allowed, specific invitations tailored to the judge raise suspicion of partiality. The Hanafi school has an internal disagreement on whether this prohibition extends to close relatives. Let us examine the reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and baseline ruling
The act is a judge accepting a specific invitation. The baseline ruling from the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) is prohibition (makruh tahrimi) for all, including relatives.
2
Locate the point of disagreement
Does the prohibition also apply to mahram relatives? Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf say yes; Imam Muhammad says no for mahram relatives.
Intra-madhhab ikhtilaf
3
Examine Imam Muhammad's proof
Imam Muhammad uses qiyas (analogy) with gift acceptance from relatives, which is permissible. He argues that if a judge may accept a gift from a mahram, he may accept an invitation too.
4
Examine the two shaykhs' response
They distinguish between gifts and invitations: invitations involve public appearance and could create suspicion of bias even among relatives.
The distinction is critical
5
Determine the mufta bihi and its practical effect
The view of the two shaykhs is relied upon (mufta bihi). In practice, a judge avoids all specific invitations to maintain impartiality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قرابتدار بھی شامل ہے۔ یعنی قاضی خصوصی دعوت قبول نہ کرے دائی خواہ اجنبی ہو خواہ اس کا ذی رحم محرم ہو ۔ یہی شیخین کا قول ہے۔ حضرت امام محمد نے فرمایا کہ قاضی ذی رحم محرم کی دعوت قبول کر لے اگر چہ خصوصی دعوت ہو ۔ جیسا کہ اسکا ہدیہ قبول کرنا جائز ہے۔ اور دعوت عامہ اور دعوت خاصہ میں فرق یہ ہے کہ اگر داعی کو یہ معلوم ہو جائے کہ قاضی نہیں آسکے گا تو وہ اسکو ملتوی کر دے۔ تو یہ دعوتِ خاصہ ہے اور اگر ایسا نہ ہو تو دعوتِ عامہ ہے۔ اور بعض مشائخ نے فرمایا کہ دس آدمیوں سے کم دعوت خاصہ ہے اور اس سے بڑھ کر دعوت عامہ ہے۔ اور اگر ایسا نہ ہو تو یہ دعوتِ عامہ ہے اور بعض نے کہا کہ نکاح اور ختنہ کی دعوت ، دعوت عامہ ہے اور ان کے علاوہ دعوت خاصہ ہے۔
Relatives are also included. That is, the judge should not accept a specific invitation, whether the inviter is a stranger or a close relative (dhi rahm mahram). This is the saying of the two shaykhs. Imam Muhammad said that the judge should accept the invitation of a close relative (dhi rahm mahram) even if it is a specific invitation, just as it is permissible for him to accept his gift. And the difference between a general invitation and a specific invitation is that if the inviter knows that the judge will not be able to come, he postpones it for him; then it is a specific invitation. And if not, it is a general invitation. Some mashaykh said that an invitation of less than ten people is specific, and more than that is general. And if not, it is a general invitation. And some said that a wedding invitation and a circumcision invitation are general invitations, and other than them are specific invitations.
Source pages p. 264

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the ruling on judges accepting invitations. It begins by clarifying that the ruling covers relatives (قرابتدار) as well. The two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) hold that a judge must not accept a specific دعوت (invitation) regardless of whether the inviter is a stranger or a mahram relative. Imam Muhammad differs, allowing acceptance of a specific invitation from a mahram relative, analogizing to the permissibility of accepting gifts from them. The passage then defines the types of invitations: a specific دعوت خاصہ is one where the inviter would postpone if the judge cannot attend; a general دعوت عامہ is one where no such accommodation is made. Alternative definitions are given: under ten guests is specific, over ten general; or wedding and circumcision feasts are general, all others specific. This intra-Hanafi dispute is resolved in practice by the view of the two shaykhs (mufta bihi).

Key Terms
دعوت خاصہ (da'wat khaassah): A specific invitation tailored to the judge, where the inviter would postpone the event if the judge cannot attend.
دعوت عامہ (da'wat 'aammah): A general open invitation to many people, not specifically for the judge.
شیخین (shaykhayn): Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (the two shaykhs).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), which invitation may a judge accept?
A) Any specific invitation from a mahram relative.
B) Any general invitation that is not tailored to him.
C) A specific invitation from a stranger but not from a relative.
D) A wedding invitation only.

Key Takeaway
A judge must decline any invitation that is specifically tailored to him, regardless of the relation to the inviter, to uphold impartiality.

Judge Attending Funerals and Visiting Sick
States the ruling that a judge must attend funerals and visit the sick, with hadith proofs and the exception for litigants.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that a judge must attend funerals and visit the sick as wajib rights, and explain the hadith proof and the exception when a litigant is sick.

Core Idea
Attending funerals and visiting the sick are obligatory for a judge, but he must avoid causing harm to litigants.

This lesson examines the first ruling from Al-Quduri's Adab al-Qadi. The judge is not exempt from the general Muslim duties of attending funerals and visiting the sick. The passage provides hadith evidence and clarifies an important exception: when the sick person is a litigant, the judge should not visit alone to avoid causing harm to the opposing party.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The judge is commanded to attend funerals and visit the sick. This is a wajib duty based on the huquq al-muslimin.
The ruling applies to judges like any other Muslim, but with an exception for litigants.
2
Locate the dalil
Two hadith are cited: Abu Hurairah's hadith listing the five/six rights, and Abu Ayyub's hadith emphasizing that these six are obligatory (wajib).
Both are found in Sahih Muslim.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative form in the hadith ('you should visit', 'you should attend') indicates obligation (wujub) according to Hanafi usul.
Al-amr yufidu al-wujub.
4
Note the exception
If the sick person is a litigant, the judge must not visit him alone because it would cause distress (aziyat) to the other party and create suspicion.
This exception preserves impartiality.
5
Understand the basis
The exception is based on the principle of avoiding harm (la darar) and tuhmah, even though the general duty remains wajib.
The judge balances rights and judicial integrity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قاضی کے لئے جنازہ میں شرکت اور مریض کی عیادت کا حکم قال ويشهد الجنازة ويعود المريض لان ذالك من حقوق المسلمين قال عليه السلام للمسلم على المسلم ستة حقوق وعد منها هذين ولا يضيف احد الخصمين دون خصمه لان النبى نهى عن ذلك ولان فيه تهمة ترجمہ اور قاضی جنازے میں حاضر ہو ۔ اور مریض کی عیادت کرے اس لئے کی یہ مسلمانوں کے حقوق میں سے ہے ۔ رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ مسلمان کے مسلمان پر چھ حق ہیں انہیں میں سے آپ نے ان دونوں کو شمار فرمایا۔ اور قاضی مدعی اور مدعی علیہ میں سے کسی ایک کی دعوت بغیر دوسرے کے نہ کرے۔ کیونکہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اس سے منع فرمایا ہے۔ اور اس لئے کہ ایسا کرنے میں تہمت ہے۔ تشریح صاحب قدوری فرماتے ہیں کہ قاضی، جنازے میں شرکت کرے اور بیمار کی عیادت کرے۔ کیونکہ یہ دونوں چیزیں مسلمانوں کے حقوق میں سے ہیں۔ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ ایک مسلمان کے دوسرے مسلمان پر چھ حق ہیں۔ ان میں سے ایک جنازہ میں حاضر ہونا بھی ہے اور ایک مریض کی عیادت کرنا بھی ہے۔ چنانچہ مسلم شریف میں ابو ہریرہ کی روایت ہے قال رسول الله حق المسلم على المسلم خمس رد السلام و تشمية العاطس واجابة الدعوة وعيادة المريض واتباع الجنائز واذا استنصحك فانصح له فهذه هي السادسة ۔ یعنی مسلمان کے مسلمان پر پانچ حق ہیں ۔ سلام کا جواب دینا، چھینک کا جواب، دعوت قبول کرنا ، مریض کی عیادت کرنا ، جنازے کی اتباع کرنا اور جب وہ تجھ سے نصیحت چاہے تو اس کو نصیحت کر ، یہی چھنا حق ہے۔ یہ خیال رہے کہ اگر مدعی یا مدعی علیہ بیمار ہو گیا تو قاضی اس کی عیادت نہ کرے۔ کیونکہ اس کی وجہ سے فریق ثانی کو اذیت ہوگی۔ حضرت ابوایوب انصاری کی حدیث کے الفاظ یہ ہیں۔ قال سمعت رسول الله يقول للمسلم على المسلم ست خصال واجبة ان ترك شيئاً منها فقد ترك حقاً واجباً عليه اذا دعاه ان يجيبه واذا مرض ان يعوده و اذامات ان يحضره واذا لقيه ان يسلم عليه واذا استنصحه ان ينصحه واذا عطس أن يشمته حضرت ابوایوب انصاری فرماتے ہیں کہ میں نے رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم کو فرماتے ہوئے سنا کہ مسلم کے لئے مسلمان پر چھ خصال واجب نہیں اگر اس نے کوئی حق تھوڑا تو اپنے اوپر حق واجب ترک کیا، ا۔ جب اس کو دعوت دے تو اس کو قبول کرے۔  كتاب الادب القاضي . اور جب بیمار ہوتو اس کی عیادت کرے۔ . اور جب مرجائے تو اس کے جنازہ میں شرکت کرے۔ ۔ اور جب ملاقات ہو تو اس کو سلام کرے۔ ۵۔ اور جب اس سے نصیحت چاہے تو اس کو نصیحت کرے۔ - اور جب چھینک آئے تو اس کا جواب دے۔ صاحب قدوری فرماتے ہیں کہ قاضی ایسا بھی نہ کرے کہ مدعی اور مدعی علیہ میں سے ایک کی ذرت کرے اور دوسرے کی دعوت نہ کرے۔ کیونکہ حضرت علی کی حدیث ہے انه قال نھانا رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ان نضيف الخصم الا ان يكون خصمه معه. حضرت علی نے فرمایا کہ ہم کو رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم نے منع فرمایا کہ ہم خصم کی ضیافت کریں مگر یہ کہ اس کے ساتھ اس کا خصم ہو۔ یعنی مدعی اور مدعی علیہ میں سے ایک کی دعوت کرنے سے منع فرمایا ہے لیکن اگر ان دونوں کی دعوت کرے تو کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ہے۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ قاضی ایسا کرنے میں متہم ہوگا یعنی لوگ یہ خیال کریں گے کہ قاضی کا اس شخص کی جانب میدان ہے۔
Ruling for the judge regarding attending funerals and visiting the sick. He said: He should attend the funeral and visit the sick, because that is from the rights of the Muslims. The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: For a Muslim upon another Muslim are six rights, and from them he counted these two. And he should not invite one of the two litigants without his opponent, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) forbade that, and because there is suspicion in it. Translation: And the judge should be present at the funeral and visit the sick, because these are from the rights of the Muslims. The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said that a Muslim has six rights upon another Muslim, and from them he counted these two. And the judge should not invite one of the plaintiff and defendant without the other, because the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) forbade that, and because in doing so there is suspicion. Commentary: Sahib al-Quduri says that the judge should attend the funeral and visit the sick, because these two are from the rights of the Muslims. The Prophet (peace be upon him) said that one Muslim has six rights upon another. Among them are attending the funeral and visiting the sick. Thus in Sahih Muslim, a narration from Abu Hurairah: The Messenger of Allah said: The right of a Muslim upon another Muslim is five: returning the greeting, responding to the sneeze, accepting the invitation, visiting the sick, and following the funeral. And when he seeks advice from you, advise him; this is the sixth. That is, a Muslim has five rights upon another Muslim: returning the greeting, responding to the sneeze, accepting the invitation, visiting the sick, following the funeral, and when he seeks advice from you, advise him; this is the sixth right. It should be noted that if the plaintiff or defendant becomes sick, the judge should not visit him, because that would cause harm to the other party. The words of the hadith of Abu Ayyub al-Ansari are: He said: I heard the Messenger of Allah say: For a Muslim upon another Muslim are six obligatory characteristics; if he leaves any of them, he has left a right obligatory upon him: when he invites him, he should respond; when he is sick, he should visit him; when he dies, he should attend; when he meets him, he should greet him; when he seeks advice, he should advise him; when he sneezes, he should respond to it. Abu Ayyub al-Ansari said: I heard the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) say: For a Muslim upon another Muslim are six obligatory qualities; if he has neglected any right, he has left a right obligatory upon himself. 1. When he invites him, he should accept. 2. And when he is sick, he should visit him. 3. And when he dies, he should attend his funeral. 4. And when he meets him, he should greet him. 5. And when he seeks advice from him, he should advise him. 6. And when he sneezes, he should respond to it. Sahib al-Quduri says that the judge should also not do that he invites one of the plaintiff and defendant and does not invite the other, because the hadith of Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) is: He said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) forbade us from inviting a litigant unless his opponent is with him. Ali said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) forbade us from inviting a litigant unless his opponent is with him. That is, he forbade inviting only one of the plaintiff and defendant, but if he invites both, there is no harm. The second proof is that in doing so, the judge would be suspected, meaning people would think that the judge has partiality towards that person.
Source pages p. 264

Commentary
This passage presents two distinct rulings for a judge, both supported by hadith proofs. The first ruling (from Quduri's matn) concerns attending funerals and visiting the sick. These are general rights of Muslims. The commentator provides two hadith: Abu Hurairah's hadith listing five/six rights, and Abu Ayyub's hadith listing six obligatory khisal. The importance is that the judge is not exempt from these general obligations despite his position. However, an exception is noted: if one litigant is sick, the judge should not visit him alone to avoid causing distress to the other litigant. The second ruling prohibits the judge from inviting one litigant without the other (such as for a meal). The proof is the hadith of Ali that the Prophet forbade singling out one litigant for hospitality. The rationale is avoiding suspicion of bias. Both rulings aim to ensure the judge's impartiality and integrity.

Key Terms
حقوق المسلمين (huquq al-muslimin): The rights that Muslims have over each other, including attending funerals and visiting the sick.
تہمت (tuhmah): Suspicion or accusation of bias; a reason for prohibition in judicial conduct.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the commentary say a judge should not visit a sick litigant?
A) Because visiting the sick is not obligatory for a judge.
B) Because it may cause suspicion of bias and harm the other party.
C) Because the judge is too busy.
D) Because the litigant is not a Muslim.

Key Takeaway
The judge must fulfill the wajib rights of attending funerals and visiting the sick, but must avoid any action that creates suspicion or harms the other party.

Qada — Judiciary
intermediate

Judge Not Inviting One Litigant Without the Other
States the ruling that a judge must not invite one litigant without the other, with the hadith of Ali and the rationale of tuhmah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that a judge must not invite one litigant without the other, and explain the hadith proof and the rationale of avoiding suspicion.

Core Idea
A judge must never invite a single litigant alone; it is haram to prevent suspicion of bias.

This lesson covers the second ruling from Al-Quduri: the judge's prohibition against singling out one litigant for hospitality. The passage provides the hadith of Ali and the principle of avoiding tuhmah. The ruling ensures the judge's impartiality is beyond doubt.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is inviting just one litigant (plaintiff or defendant) without the other. The ruling is it is forbidden (haram).
The prohibition is based on explicit hadith and the principle of tuhmah.
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith of Ali: 'The Messenger of Allah forbade us from inviting a litigant unless his opponent is with him.'
This hadith is the primary proof.
3
Understand the rationale
The prohibition is because it creates tuhmah (suspicion) that the judge may be biased toward the invited party.
Avoiding tuhmah is essential for judicial integrity.
4
Note the exception
If the judge invites both litigants together, there is no harm. The prohibition is only against singling out one.
Inviting both equally is permissible.

Source Text

Qada — Judiciary

Judge's Conduct: Equality in Court and Avoiding Partiality
Ruling on judge's mandatory equality in court conduct with proof from hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rules for a judge's physical conduct in court, identify prohibited actions, and explain the legal reasoning based on the hadith.

Core Idea
The judge must treat both litigants equally in seating, gesture, and gaze — any deviation breaks the court's integrity.

This passage from Al-Quduri's matn, expanded by the commentator, establishes the foundational rules for a judge's conduct in the courtroom. It is not merely a matter of etiquette but a legal obligation (wajib) rooted in a direct command of the Prophet (peace be upon him). The goal is to prevent any perception of bias and to maintain the dignity of the court.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
Read the passage and state the core ruling: the judge must make the litigants equal in sitting, attention, gesture, and gaze.
The ruling is found in Quduri's statement: 'sawa baynahuma fi al-julus wa al-iqbal'.
2
Locate the Dalil
Find the hadith quoted as proof: 'When one of you is afflicted with judgment, make them equal in sitting, gesture, and gaze.'
The hadith is ahad but its indication is clear (qati' al-dalala).
3
Extract the Wajh al-Dalalah
Analyze the command 'falisu' (make equal) — in Hanafi usul, the imperative indicates obligation (wujub). The hadith specifies three domains: sitting, gesture, and gaze.
The imperative form 'falisu' is key to establishing the wajib status.
4
List Prohibited Actions
Identify the actions the judge must avoid: whispering to one litigant, gesturing to one, prompting an argument, laughing with one, and jesting with any.
Each prohibition has a specific rationale: suspicion, breaking the other's heart, emboldening the opponent, destroying the court's awe.
5
Understand the Rationale
The overarching reasons are to prevent suspicion (tuhmah) and protect the heart of the other litigant, and to preserve the haybah (awe) of the court.
The commentator emphasizes that equality in seating includes not favoring one side by proximity or right/left placement.

قاضی مدعی اور مدعی علیہ کے درمیان بیٹھے اور توجہ یکساں دے قال واذا حضر سوى بينهما فى الجلوس والاقبال لقوله عليه السلام اذا ابتلى احدكم بالقضاء فليسو بينهم في المجلس والاشارة والنظر ولا يسار احدهما ولا يشير اليه ولا يلقنه حجة للتهمة ولأن فيه مكسرة لقلب الاخر فيترك حقه ولا يضحك فى وجه احدهما لانه يجترئ على خصمه ولا يمازحهم ولا واحدا منهم لانه يذهب بمهابة القضاء ترجمہ اور جب مدعی اور مدعی علیہ دونوں حاضر ہوں تو قاضی دونوں کے درمیان بیٹھے اور توجہ کرنے میں برابری کرے۔ کیونکہ حضور نے فرمایا کہ جب تم میں سے کوئی شخص قضاء میں مبتلا ہو تو خصوم کے درمیان بیٹھے، اشارہ کرنے اور نظر کرنے میں برابری کرے۔ اور تہمت کی وجہ سے اُن دونوں میں سے کسی ایک سے کان میں بات نہ کرے۔ اور نہ کسی ایک کی طرف اشارہ کرے۔ اور نہ اس کو حجت کی تلقین کرے۔ اور اس لئے کہ ایسا کرنے میں دوسرے کی دل شکنی ہے۔ پس وہ اپنا حق ترک کر دے گا۔ اور قاضی ان دونوں میں سے ایک سے مواجہہ کر کے نہ ہنسے کیونکہ وہ اپنے خصم پر دلیر ہو جائے گا۔ اور نہ تمام خصوم سے دل لگی کرے اور نہ ان میں سے کسی ایک سے دل لگی کرے۔ کیونکہ دل لگی کر نا قضاء کی ہیبت ختم کر دیتا ہے۔ تشریح صاحب قدوری نے فرمایا کہ جب مدعی اور مدعی علیہ دونوں حاضر ہوں تو بیٹھنے اور توجہ کرنے میں دونوں کے درمیان برابری کرے۔ یعنی بیٹھنے میں ایک کو دوسرے پر فضیلت نہ دے بلکہ دونوں کے واسطے برابری ہوتی کہ اگر ایک کو مسند پر بٹھلا نا مناسب ہو تو دوسرے کو بھی اسی طرح بھلائے ۔ اور ایک کو دائیں جانب اور ایک کو بائیں جانب بھی نہ بھلائے کیونکہ دائیں جانب کو بائیں جانب پر چونکہ فضیات حاصل ہے اس لئے اس صورت میں برابری حاصل نہ ہو سکے گی۔ اور قاضی دونوں کو ایک جانب بھی نہ بھلائے ۔ اس لئے کہ اس صورت میں ایک کو قاضی سے زیادہ قرب ہوگا اور ایک کو کم قرب ہوگا ۔ پس اس صورت میں بھی برابری قائم نہ رہے گی ۔ مناسب
The judge should sit between the plaintiff and defendant and give equal attention. He said: And when he (the litigant) is present, he should make them equal in sitting and facing, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: When one of you is afflicted with judgment, then make them equal in the sitting, gesture, and gaze. And he should not whisper to one of them, nor gesture to him, nor prompt him with an argument, due to suspicion, and because it breaks the heart of the other, so he will abandon his right. And he should not laugh in the face of one of them, because he will become bold against his opponent. And he should not jest with them or with any one of them, because jesting removes the awe of judgment. Translation: And when both the plaintiff and defendant are present, the judge should sit between them and be equal in giving attention. Because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: When one of you is involved in judgment, sit between the litigants, be equal in gesture and gaze. And due to suspicion, he should not whisper to one of them, nor gesture to one of them, nor prompt him with an argument. And because doing so breaks the heart of the other, so he will abandon his right. And the judge should not laugh face to face with one of them, because he will become bold against his opponent. And he should not jest with all the litigants or with any one of them, because jesting removes the awe of judgment. Commentary: Sahib al-Quduri said that when both the plaintiff and defendant are present, he should make equality between them in sitting and attention. That is, he should not give preference to one over the other in sitting, but there should be equality between them. So if it is appropriate to seat one on a cushion, he should seat the other similarly. And he should not seat one on the right and one on the left, because the right side has superiority over the left, so equality would not be achieved in that case. And the judge should not seat both on one side, because then one would be closer to the judge and the other farther, so equality would not be established. This is appropriate.
Source pages p. 265

Commentary
This passage lays out detailed rules for the judge's conduct in court to ensure absolute equality between the litigants. The matn from Quduri states: when both parties are present, the judge must treat them equally in seating and attention. The proof is the hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) commanding equality in sitting, gesture, and gaze. The commentary elaborates: the judge should not give one a better seat, nor seat one on his right and the other on his left (since right is privileged), nor seat both on the same side (unequal proximity). The prohibition extends to whispering, gesturing, or prompting an argument to one litigant, as these would break the other's heart and cause him to abandon his case. Laughing with one makes him bold; jesting with any removes the judge's dignity and awe (haybah al-qada). All these rules aim to prevent suspicion (tuhmah) and ensure the court's integrity.

Key Terms
الاشارة والنظر (al-isharah wa an-nazar): Gesturing and looking; the judge must be equal in these towards both litigants.
هيبة القضاء (haybah al-qada): The awe and dignity of the court, which is lost by jesting or excessive familiarity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the reason given for the prohibition of a judge whispering to one litigant?
A) It is a waste of time.
B) It may break the heart of the other litigant and cause him to give up his right.
C) It is forbidden for anyone to whisper in court.
D) It is disrespectful to the court clerk.

Key Takeaway
The judge's physical conduct is legally regulated to ensure impartiality and maintain the court's awe.

Prohibition of Hosting One Litigant Without the Other
Prohibition of entertaining one litigant alone due to suspicion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of a judge hosting only one litigant and explain the Hanafi evidence from hadith and the principle of avoiding tuhma.

Core Idea
A judge must not host one litigant alone — avoiding even the appearance of bias is wajib upon the judiciary.

This passage from Al-Quduri establishes a key principle of judicial ethics: a judge must avoid any action that creates suspicion (tuhma) of partiality. The ruling is derived from a clear prophetic prohibition and reinforced by rational reasoning. We will examine the evidence and the precise legal classification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
What specific action is being ruled upon? What is the legal classification (hukm) according to the Hanafi school?
The act is a judge giving hospitality (diyafat) to only one of two litigants.
2
Locate the primary dalil
What proof does the author cite? Identify the source (hadith) and its transmitter.
The hadith of Ali (RA) is cited: the Prophet forbade hosting one litigant without his opponent.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the hadith prove the ruling? What word or phrase indicates the prohibition?
The word 'naha' (forbade) indicates a prohibition; in Hanafi usul this yields karaha tahrimiya.
4
Understand the secondary rational proof
What is the second proof and how does it support the ruling?
The principle of avoiding tuhma (suspicion): people will suspect bias if one litigant is hosted alone.
5
Note the hukm level and its basis
Why is it makruh tahrimi and not haram? What is the mufta bihi?
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) and the harm is through suspicion, so the prohibition is not absolute haram.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صاحب قدوری فرماتے ہیں کہ قاضی ایسا بھی نہ کرے کہ مدعی اور مدعی علیہ میں سے ایک کی ضیافت کرے اور دوسرے کی دعوت نہ کرے۔ کیونکہ حضرت علی کی حدیث ہے انه قال نھانا رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ان نضيف الخصم الا ان يكون خصمه معه. حضرت علی نے فرمایا کہ ہم کو رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم نے منع فرمایا کہ ہم خصم کی ضیافت کریں مگر یہ کہ اس کے ساتھ اس کا خصم ہو۔ یعنی مدعی اور مدعی علیہ میں سے ایک کی دعوت کرنے سے منع فرمایا ہے لیکن اگر ان دونوں کی دعوت کرے تو کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ہے۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ قاضی ایسا کرنے میں متہم ہوگا یعنی لوگ یہ خیال کریں گے کہ قاضی کا اس شخص کی جانب میدان ہے۔
Sahib al-Quduri says: The judge should not do such that he gives hospitality to one of the plaintiff and defendant and does not invite the other. Because of the hadith of Ali (may Allah be pleased with him): he said, 'The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) forbade us from giving hospitality to a litigant except that his opponent be with him.' Ali said: The Messenger of Allah forbade us from inviting one litigant, except that both are invited together. That is, he forbade inviting only one of the plaintiff and defendant, but if he invites both, there is no harm. The second proof is that in doing so the judge will be suspected, i.e., people will think that the judge is inclined towards that person.
Source pages p. 265

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the hadith of Ali (ra). Al-Quduri states that a judge must not host a meal or gathering for only one of the litigants. The primary proof is the explicit prohibition (nahy) from the Prophet (saw) as narrated by Ali. The hadith indicates that it is permissible to host both litigants together, but hosting one alone is forbidden. The second proof is rational: such an act creates suspicion (tuhma) of bias in the minds of people, which a judge must avoid. The ruling is one of karaha tahrimiya (prohibitively disliked) because it leads to tuhma and is against the principle of impartiality.

Key Terms
ضیافت (diyafat): Hospitality or feast given to a guest
تہمت (tuhma): Suspicion or accusation; here it means the appearance of bias that leads to distrust in the judge's impartiality.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Recommended (mustahabb)
C) Prohibitively disliked (makruh tahrimi)
D) Forbidden (haram)

Key Takeaway
A judge must not host one litigant alone because it creates suspicion of bias and contradicts the prophetic prohibition.

Qada — Judiciary

Equal Treatment of Litigants in the Courtroom
Commands equality in seating, attention, and prohibits whispering and joking.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on equal treatment of litigants in seating and attention, identify the prohibited acts that violate impartiality, and explain the legal basis (dalil) and rationale behind each prohibition.

Core Idea
A judge must treat both litigants equally; any preferential gesture, whisper, or jest taints the court's integrity.

The courtroom is a place of justice where impartiality is paramount. A judge's conduct must reflect absolute neutrality, not only in the verdict but in every interaction with the parties. This passage from al-Hidayah lays down clear rules: equal seating, equal attention, and a ban on any action that could create suspicion or undermine the court's dignity. Understanding these rules is essential for anyone who will sit in judgment or advise on judicial conduct.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
First, recognize that the passage gives two categories of rulings: positive commands (equality in seating and attention) and prohibitions (whispering, gesturing, prompting, laughing, joking). Determine the legal status (hukm) of each: equality is wajib; the prohibitions are makruh tahrimi.
The imperative 'falisu' in the hadith indicates obligation in Hanafi usul.
2
Locate the dalil (evidence)
The primary proof is the hadith narrated by Umm Salama: 'When one of you is afflicted with qadha, then make them equal in sitting, gesture, and glance.' This is a hadith ahad, so its thubut is zanni, but its dalala is qati' (clear meaning).
A second proof is the general principle of avoiding suspicion (tuhma) and heartbreak.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative verb 'falisu' (make equal) is a command, which, according to Hanafi usul, indicates obligation (wujub) unless there is a qarinah to the contrary. The prohibitions use negative imperatives ('la yusarr', 'la yushir', etc.) which indicate prohibition (karaha tahrimiyya).
The rationale of tuhma (suspicion) and heartbreak supports the prohibitions.
4
Note the specific prohibitions and their reasons
Whispering, gesturing, prompting, laughing, and joking are all prohibited because they create suspicion of bias, cause heartbreak to the other party, or diminish the awe (haybah) of the court. Each prohibition is tied to a specific harm.
Prompting (talqin hujja) is particularly serious as it may lead to a false impression of partiality.
5
Apply the ruling to modern court settings
Consider how these rules translate to contemporary courtrooms: a judge should avoid any private communication with one party, not use body language that favors one side, not assist one party with evidence, and maintain a dignified demeanor.
The same principles apply in arbitration and other quasi-judicial proceedings.

Source Text

قال واذا حضر سوى بينهما فى الجلوس والاقبال لقوله عليه السلام اذا ابتلى احدكم بالقضاء فليسو بينهم في المجلس والاشارة والنظر ولا يسار احدهما ولا يشير اليه ولا يلقنه حجة للتهمة ولأن فيه مكسرة لقلب الاخر فيترك حقه ولا يضحك فى وجه احدهما لانه يجترئ على خصمه ولا يمازحهم ولا واحدا منهم لانه يذهب بمهابة القضاء. ترجمہ اور جب مدعی اور مدعی علیہ دونوں حاضر ہوں تو قاضی دونوں کے درمیان بیٹھے اور توجہ کرنے میں برابری کرے۔ کیونکہ حضور نے فرمایا کہ جب تم میں سے کوئی شخص قضاء میں مبتلا ہو تو خصوم کے درمیان بیٹھے، اشارہ کرنے اور نظر کرنے میں برابری کرے۔ اور تہمت کی وجہ سے اُن دونوں میں سے کسی ایک سے کان میں بات نہ کرے۔ اور نہ کسی ایک کی طرف اشارہ کرے۔ اور نہ اس کو حجت کی تلقین کرے۔ اور اس لئے کہ ایسا کرنے میں دوسرے کی دل شکنی ہے۔ پس وہ اپنا حق ترک کر دے گا۔ اور قاضی ان دونوں میں سے ایک سے مواجہہ کر کے نہ ہنسے کیونکہ وہ اپنے خصم پر دلیر ہو جائے گا۔ اور نہ تمام خصوم سے دل لگی کرے اور نہ ان میں سے کسی ایک سے دل لگی کرے۔ کیونکہ دل لگی کر نا قضاء کی ہیبت ختم کر دیتا ہے۔ تشریح صاحب قدوری نے فرمایا کہ جب مدعی اور مدعی علیہ دونوں حاضر ہوں تو بیٹھنے اور توجہ کرنے میں دونوں کے درمیان برابری کرے۔ یعنی بیٹھنے میں ایک کو دوسرے پر فضیلت نہ دے بلکہ دونوں کے واسطے برابری ہوتی کہ اگر ایک کو مسند پر بٹھانا مناسب ہو تو دوسرے کو بھی اسی طرح بٹھائے ۔ اور ایک کو دائیں جانب اور ایک کو بائیں جانب بھی نہ بٹھائے کیونکہ دائیں جانب کو بائیں جانب پر چونکہ فضیلت حاصل ہے اس لئے اس صورت میں برابری حاصل نہ ہو سکے گی۔ اور قاضی دونوں کو ایک جانب بھی نہ بٹھائے ۔ اس لئے کہ اس صورت میں ایک کو قاضی سے زیادہ قرب ہوگا اور ایک کو کم قرب ہوگا ۔ پس اس صورت میں بھی برابری قائم نہ رہے گی ۔ مناسب یہ ہے کہ مدعی اور مدعی علیہ دونوں قاضی کے سامنے زمین پر بیٹھیں ۔ اسی طرح دونوں کی طرف دیکھنے اور توجہ کرنے میں بھی برابری کرے۔ یعنی قاضی دونوں کی طرف برابر متوجہ ہو ۔ اور دونوں کو یکسانیت کے ساتھ دیکھے۔ دلیل حضرت ام سلمہ کی حدیث ہے قالت قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم من ابتلى بالقضاء بين المسلمين فليسو بينهم في المجلس والاشارة والنظر ولا يرفع صوته على احد الخصمين اكثر من الآخر - ام سلمہ کہتی ہیں کہ رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ جوشخص مسلمانوں میں منصب قضاء کے ساتھ مبتلا کر دیا گیا ہو۔ وہ فریقین کے درمیان بیٹھنے ، اشارہ کرنے اور دیکھنے میں برابری کرے۔ اور احد الخصمین پر دوسرے سے زیادہ آواز بلند نہ کرے۔ صاحب قدوری فرماتے ہیں کہ قاضی کسی ایک کے ساتھ چپکے چپکے باتیں نہ کرے۔ اور اپنے ہاتھ یا سر یا ابرو سے اشارہ نہ کرے اور نہ اس کو حجت کی تلقین کرے۔ کیونکہ ایسا کرنے میں قاضی ، رشوت اور طرفداری کے ساتھ متہم ہو سکتا ہے۔ پس تہمت سے بچنے کے لئے مذکورہ امور نہ کرے۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ ایسا کرنے میں چونکہ دوسرے کی دل شکنی ہے اس لئے وہ اپنا حق ہی چھوڑ دے گا۔ یعنی جب وہ یہ خیال کرے گا کہ قاضی کا میرے خصم کی طرف میلان طبع ہے تو وہ قاضی سے انصاف کی امید نہ رکھ کر اپنا حق چھوڑ دے گا ۔ اور قاضی فریقین میں سے کسی کی طرف دیکھ کر نہ ہنسے اور نہ مسکرائے ۔ کیونکہ یہ فریق جس کی طرف دیکھ کر قاضی مسکرایا ہے دوسرے فریق پر دلیر ہوگا اور اس کی وجہ سے دوسرے فریق کی دل شکنی ہوگی۔ اور قاضی فریقین کے ساتھ یا ان میں سے کسی ایک کے ساتھ مذاق بھی نہ کرے کیونکہ دل لگی، اور مذاق کرنا منصب قضاء کے رعب اور ہیبت کو ختم کر دیتا ہے حالانکہ قاضی کے لئے بارعب اور با وقار رہنا ضروری ہے۔
He said: And when both are present, he should make them equal in sitting and attention, because he (peace be upon him) said: 'When one of you is afficted with qadha, then make them equal in sitting, gesture, and glance.' And he should not whisper to one of them, nor gesture to him, nor prompt him with an argument, due to suspicion, and because it causes heartbreak to the other, so he may abandon his right. And he should not laugh in the face of one of them, because that emboldens him against his opponent. And he should not joke with them or with any one of them, because joking removes the awe of qadha. Translation and commentary follow with details on equal seating, the hadith of Umm Salama, and prohibitions on whispering, gesturing, prompting, laughing, and joking.
Source pages p. 265

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof detailing the judge's obligation to treat both litigants equally in the courtroom. It begins with the matn commanding equality in sitting and attention, citing the Prophet's hadith. The commentary explains practical implementation: both parties should be seated equally, preferably on the ground before the judge, without giving any preferential seating (e.g., not placing one on the right or closer). The judge must not whisper, gesture, or prompt one party, as this creates suspicion and heartbreaks the other. Laughing or joking with one party is also prohibited because it diminishes the court's dignity and emboldens the other party. A second hadith from Umm Salama is presented as additional proof. The overall objective is to maintain impartiality, avoid tuhma, and preserve the majesty of the judiciary.

Key Terms
تسویہ (taswiyah): Making equal; here, the judge must treat both litigants equally in seating, attention, and gestures.
تلقین حجت (talqin hujja): Prompting a litigant with an argument or evidence that he has not mentioned.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is a judge prohibited from laughing with one litigant?
A) Laughter is haram in court
B) It makes the other litigant feel inferior and may cause him to abandon his right
C) It wastes court time
D) It is considered a form of bribery

Key Takeaway
A judge must be scrupulously impartial in conduct, avoiding even subtle gestures or words that could create suspicion or hurt a litigant's confidence in the court.

Ruling on Prompting a Witness (Talqin al-Shahid)
Prohibition of prompting witness with Abu Yusuf's exception.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on talqin al-shahid and differentiate between the positions of Abu Hanifa/Muhammad and Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
Prompting a witness is generally forbidden to avoid bias, but Abu Yusuf allows it when no suspicion exists.

This lesson explores an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether a judge may prompt a witness to testify. The majority view holds it is makruh because it assists one litigant and creates suspicion. However, Abu Yusuf permits it in the absence of suspicion, citing the need to uncover the truth. Understanding this ikhtilaf sharpens your grasp of legal principles like sadd al-dhara'i' and istihsan.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its default ruling
What is talqin al-shahid? The judge asks a witness: 'Do you testify to such-and-such?' The matn states it is makruh (disliked).
The default ruling is based on the principle of avoiding tuhma (suspicion).
2
Trace the dalil for the majority
Why is it makruh? Qiyas on talqin al-khasm (prompting a litigant) – both assist one party and create suspicion.
The underlying illa (effective cause) is the appearance of partiality.
3
Analyze Abu Yusuf's Istihsan
Abu Yusuf deems it mustahsan (preferable) in non-suspicious situations because the witness may be overwhelmed by the court's awe. Analogy to sending a person to fetch a witness or taking a surety – both are permissible facilitations.
Istihsan overrides qiyas here due to the need to establish truth.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical difference: Under the majority, prompting is always makruh. Under Abu Yusuf, it becomes permissible when no tuhma exists and the witness is hesitant.
The judge must assess tuhma case-by-case.
5
Identify the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position: Generally makruh, but Abu Yusuf's view is adopted in fatwa when conditions of necessity and absence of suspicion are met.
This combines both views for a balanced approach.

قال ويكره تلقين الشاهد ومعناه ان يقول له أتشهد بكذا وكذا وهذا لانه اعانة لاحد الخصمين فيكره كتلقين الخصم واستحسنه ابويوسف في غير موضع التهمة لان الشاهد قد يحصر لمهابة المجلس فكان بمنزلة الإشخاص والتكفيل. ترجمہ اور گواہ کو تلقین کرنا مکروہ ہے۔ اور اس کے معنی یہ ہیں کہ گواہ سے کہے کہ کیا تو ایسی ایسی بات کا گواہ ہے۔ اور یہ اسلئے کہ یہ احد الخصمین کی اعانت ہے۔ پس یہ خود خصم کو تلقین کرنے کی طرح مکروہ ہے۔ اور امام ابو یوسف نے موضع تہمت کے علاوہ میں اس کو مستحسن رکھا ہے۔ کیونکہ گواہ کبھی عدالت کی ہیبت سے رُک جاتا ہے۔ پس اس کو تلقین کرنا حق کو زندہ کرنا ہو گا۔ جیسے کسی شخص کو بھیجنا اور احد الخصمین سے کفیل لینا۔ تشریح تلقین قاضی ایسی بات کہے جس سے گواہ اُس چیز کو حاصل کرے جو شہادت کے ساتھ متعلق ہے ۔ مثلاً قاضی گواہ سے کہے کہ کیا تو فلاں بات کا گواہ ہے۔ بہر حال گواہ کو اس طرح کی تلقین کرنا مکروہ ہے ۔ اور وجہ کراہت یہ ہے کہ اس میں فریقین میں سے ایک کی مدد کرنا لازم آتا ہے۔ پس جس طرح خود فریقین میں سے کسی ایک کو تلقین کرنا مکروہ ہے اسی طرح گواہوں کو تلقین کرنا بھی مکروہ ہو گا۔ حضرت امام ابو یوسف نے فرمایا کہ موضع تہمت کے علاوہ میں گواہ کو تلقین کرنا مستحسن ہے۔ کیونکہ قضاء لوگوں کے حقوق زندہ کرنے کا ذریعہ ہے۔
He said: And it is makruh (disliked) to prompt the witness. Its meaning is that he says to him: 'Do you testify to such-and-such?' This is because it is assisting one of the two litigants, so it is disliked like prompting the litigant. And Abu Yusuf deemed it istihsan (preferable) in a place other than suspicion, because the witness may be overwhelmed due to the awe of the court, so it is like sending a person and taking surety from one of the litigants. Translation and commentary explain that prompting a witness is disliked because it helps one party. Abu Yusuf however considers it permissible (mustahsan) outside of suspicious situations to help reveal the truth, akin to sending someone to fetch a witness or taking a guarantor.
Source pages p. 266

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on prompting a witness. The matn of al-Quduri states that it is makruh to prompt a witness by asking 'Do you testify to such-and-such?' because it assists one litigant, similar to prompting the litigant himself. The commentary elaborates the reason: it creates suspicion of bias. However, Imam Abu Yusuf holds that in situations where there is no tuhma (suspicion), prompting is mustahsan (preferable) because the witness may be hesitant due to the court's gravity, and prompting helps to establish the truth. He analogizes it to sending a person to bring a witness or taking a surety from a litigant, which are permitted facilitations. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the Hanafi school is that talqin al-shahid is generally makruh, but Abu Yusuf's view is given weight in contexts free from suspicion.

Key Terms
تلقین الشاهد (talqin al-shahid): The judge prompting a witness by asking if he testifies to a specific fact.
موضع تہمت (mawdi' tuhma): A situation that raises suspicion of partiality or bias on the part of the judge.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school generally prohibits prompting a witness to avoid bias, but permits it under Abu Yusuf's view when no suspicion exists, balancing procedural integrity with truth-seeking.

Judge's Equality Between Litigants in Sitting and Attention
Ruling with proof on judicial equality in demeanor

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a qadi must treat both litigants equally in sitting, looking, and gesture, and identify the primary hadith evidence and the rational reason for this obligation.

Core Idea
Equality between litigants in demeanor is wajib for a qadi to ensure impartiality and avoid suspicion.

The judge's demeanor must reflect perfect neutrality. The Hanafi school, based on a prophetic command, obligates the qadi to treat both parties equally in every visible aspect—sitting, looking, gesture, and voice. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its primary proof from the hadith of Umm Salamah (may Allah be pleased with her), and the additional etiquettes derived by Sahib al-Quduri to prevent even the appearance of partiality.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage states that the plaintiff and defendant must both sit on the ground before the judge, and the judge must be equal in looking and paying attention to both. The ruling is that equality in these matters is wajib (obligatory).
The Arabic verb 'falisaw' (let him be equal) is an imperative, indicating obligation in Hanafi usul.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The author cites the hadith of Umm Salamah (may Allah be pleased with her) where the Prophet (peace be upon him) commands equality in sitting, gesture, and gaze, and forbids raising one's voice to one litigant more than the other.
This is a hadith ahad, which is zanni al-thubut but qat'i al-dalalah in Hanafi usul due to the clear imperative.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'falisaw' indicates wujub (obligation) because in Hanafi usul, al-amr yufidu al-wujub (a command indicates obligation) unless there is a qarina (indication) to the contrary. The prohibition of raising voice also indicates tahrim.
The rational reasoning reinforces the textual proof: partial behavior causes the disadvantaged party to lose hope and abandon their right.
4
Note additional guidelines from Quduri
Sahib al-Quduri adds that the judge should not whisper with one party, gesture with hand/head/eyebrow, prompt a litigant with evidence, laugh or smile at one party, or joke with parties. These are all prohibited to avoid accusations of bribery and favoritism.
These etiquettes are derived from the principle of sadd al-dhara'i' (blocking the means to evil) to maintain the judge's dignity.
5
Understand the rational reason
The second evidence is rational: if the judge shows partiality, the other litigant will become disheartened and may abandon their rightful claim. Thus, equality in demeanor is necessary to preserve trust in the judiciary.
This reasoning is consistent with the maqasid (higher objectives) of justice.

Source Text

کتاب الادب القاضي
اشرف البدایہ جلد-نم یہ ہے کہ مدعی اور مدعی علیہ دونوں قاضی کے سامنے زمین پر بیٹھیں ۔ اسی طرح دونوں کی طرف دیکھنے اور توجہ کرنے میں بھی برابری کرے۔ یعنی قاضی دونوں کی طرف برابر متوجہ ہو ۔ اور دونوں کو یکسانیت کے ساتھ دیکھے۔
دلیل حضرت ام سلمہ کی حدیث ہے قالت قال رسول الله الله من ابتلى بالقضاء بين المسلمين فليسو بينهم في المجلس والاشارة والنظر ولا يرفع صوته على احدا لخصمين اكثر من الآخر - ام سلمہ کہتی ہیں کہ رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ جوشخص مسلمانوں میں منصب قضاء کے ساتھ مبتلا کر دیا گیا ہو۔ وہ فریقین کے درمیان بیٹھنے ، اشارہ کرنے اور دیکھنے میں برابری کرے۔ اور احد انضمین پر دوسرے سے زیادہ آواز بلند نہ کرے۔ صاحب قدوری فرماتے ہیں کہ قاضی کسی ایک کے ساتھ چپکے چپکے باتیں نہ کرے۔ اور اپنے ہاتھ یا سر یا ابرو سے اشارہ نہ کرے اور نہ اس کو حجت کی تلقین کرے۔ کیونکہ ایسا کرنے میں قاضی ، رشوت اور طرفداری کے ساتھ متہم ہو سکتا ہے۔ پس تہمت سے بچنے کے لئے مذکورہ امور نہ کرے۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ ایسا کرنے میں چونکہ دوسرے کی دل شکنی ہے اس لئے وہ اپنا حق ہی چھوڑ دے گا۔ یعنی جب وہ یہ خیال کرے گا کہ قاضی کا میرے خصم کی طرف میلان طبع ہے تو وہ قاضی سے انصاف کی امید نہ رکھ کر اپنا حق چھوڑ دے گا ۔ اور قاضی فریقین میں سے کسی کی طرف دیکھ کر نہ ہنسے اور نہ مسکرائے ۔ کیونکہ یہ فریق جس کی طرف دیکھ کر قاضی مسکرایا ہے دوسرے فریق پر دلیر ہوگا اور اس کی وجہ سے دوسرے فریق کی دل شکنی ہوگی۔ اور قاضی فریقین کے ساتھ یا ان میں سے کسی ایک کے ساتھ مذاق بھی نہ کرے کیونکہ دل لگی، اور مذاق کرنا منصب قضاء کے رعب اور ہیبت کو ختم کر دیتا ہے حالانکہ قاضی کے لئے بارعب اور با وقار رہنا ضروری ہے۔
The book of the etiquette of the judge. Ashraf al-Hidayah volume: It is that the plaintiff and defendant both sit on the ground before the judge. Similarly, he should be equal in looking and paying attention to both. That is, the judge should be equally attentive to both parties and look at them equally. Evidence is the hadith of Umm Salamah: She said, the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever is afflicted with the position of judgment among Muslims, let him be equal between them in sitting, gesture, and looking, and let him not raise his voice to one of the two litigants more than the other.' Umm Salamah says that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever is afflicted with the position of judgment among Muslims, let him be equal between the parties in sitting, gesturing, and looking, and let him not raise his voice to one of the two litigants more than the other.' Sahib al-Quduri says: The judge should not whisper with one of them, nor gesture with his hand, head, or eyebrow, nor should he prompt him with the proof. Because in doing so, the judge may be accused of bribery and favoritism. So to avoid accusation, he should not do the mentioned things. The second evidence is that doing so causes heartbreak to the other, so he might abandon his right. That is, when he thinks that the judge inclines towards his opponent, he will not hope for justice from the judge and will abandon his right. And the judge should not laugh or smile while looking at one of the parties, because the party at whom the judge smiled will become bold against the other party, and this will cause heartbreak to the other party. And the judge should not joke with the parties or with any one of them, because joking and jesting remove the awe and dignity of the position of judgment, whereas the judge must remain awe-inspiring and dignified.
Source pages p. 266

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof on the judge's obligation of equality between litigants. The passage opens by stating that the plaintiff and defendant should both sit on the ground before the judge. This is a practical measure to avoid any appearance of favoritism. The judge must also be equal in looking and paying attention to both parties. The primary proof is the hadith of Umm Salamah (may Allah be pleased with her) in which the Prophet (peace be upon him) commanded equality in sitting, gesture, and gaze, and forbade raising one's voice to one litigant more than the other. The commentary of Sahib al-Quduri is then cited, which adds that the judge should not whisper with one party, gesture with hand/head/eyebrow, or prompt a litigant with evidence, all to avoid accusations of bribery or partiality. A secondary rational proof is given: such partial behavior would cause the disadvantaged party to lose heart and abandon their rightful claim. The passage concludes with additional etiquette: the judge should not laugh or smile at one party, as it makes the other party feel inferior and the favored party becomes bold. Joking with parties is also prohibited as it undermines the dignity required for the office of judge. The overall message is that the judge must maintain strict impartiality in both action and appearance.

Key Terms
قاضی (qadi): The judge appointed to adjudicate disputes among Muslims.
خصم (khasm): Litigant, either plaintiff (mudda'i) or defendant (mudda'a 'alayh).
تلقین (talqin): Prompting a litigant or witness with evidence or words to say.
مجلس (majlis): The session or seating area of the court.
اشارة (isharah): Gesture, including with hand, head, or eyebrow.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school obligates the qadi to maintain strict equality in outward demeanor between litigants, grounded in the Prophetic command and reinforced by the need to avoid even the suspicion of bias.

The Ruling on Prompting a Witness
Ruling with intra-Hanafi dispute on prompting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on talqin al-shahid and apply the distinction between mawdi' al-tuhmah and ghayr mawdi' al-tuhmah.

Core Idea
Prompting a witness is generally disliked, but Abu Yusuf permits it to revive a right where no suspicion arises.

In court proceedings, the judge must maintain impartiality. This lesson examines whether a judge may prod a hesitant witness. The Hanafi school addresses this through an intra-madhhab dispute, balancing the need to avoid partiality with the objective of reviving rights.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and base ruling
The act is talqin al-shahid: the judge prompting a witness by asking leading questions. The base ruling is makruh (disliked).
The text uses 'makruh' without specifying tahrimi or tanzihi; context suggests it is makruh tahrimi due to analogy with prompting a litigant.
2
Locate the reasoning
The reasoning (ta'lil) is that prompting aids one litigant, akin to prompting a litigant directly, which is already makruh.
This is an analogy (qiyas) between witness and litigant.
3
Identify the exception
Abu Yusuf uses istihsan to allow prompting in non-suspicious situations (ghayr mawdi' al-tuhmah). He argues that the witness may be hesitant due to awe of the court.
Istihsan overrides the general qiyas.
4
Understand the illa for the exception
The effective cause is the witness's hesitation, which threatens the revival of a rightful claim. Prompting becomes a means to achieve the purpose of qada: reviving rights.
Analogies: sending someone to call a party or taking a surety are also commendable assistances.
5
Apply the example of mawdi' al-tuhmah
When the judge's prompting could correct a discrepancy in testimony (e.g., witness testifies for 1000 while plaintiff claimed 1500), prompting is unanimously impermissible because it creates suspicion of bias.
This boundary preserves impartiality.

قاضی کے لئے گواہ کو تلقین کرنے کا حکم
قال ويكره تلقين الشاهد ومعناه ان يقول له اتشهد بكذا وكذا وهذا لانه اعانة لاحد الخصمين فيكره كتلقين الخصم واستحسنه ابويوسف في غير موضع التهمة لان الشاهد فد يحصر لمهابة المجلس فكان ــــق بمنزلة الاشخــــاص والتـــــــــــفـيــــــل
ترجمہ اور گواہ کو تلقین کرنا مکروہ ہے۔ اور اس کے معنی یہ ہیں کہ گواہ سے کہے کہ کیا تو ایسی ایسی بات کا گواہ ہے۔ اور یہ اسلئے کہ یہ احداتضمین کی اعانت ہے۔ پس یہ خود خصم کو تلقین کرنے کی طرح مکروہ ہے۔ اور امام ابو یوسف نے موضع تہمت کے علاوہ میں اس کو ستحسن رکھا ہے۔ کیونکہ گواہ کبھی عدالت کی ہیبت سے رُک جاتا ہے۔ پس اس کو تلقین کرنا حق کو زندہ کرنا ہو گا۔ جیسے کسی شخص کو بھیجنا اور احمد اختصم مین سے کفیل لینا۔
تشریح تلقین قاضی ایسی بات کہے جس سے گواہ اُس چیز کو حاصل کرے جو شہادت کے ساتھ متعلق ہے ۔ مثلاً قاضی گواہ سے کہے کہ کیا تو فلاں بات کا گواہ ہے۔ بہر حال گواہ کو اس طرح کی تلقین کرنا مکروہ ہے ۔ اور وجہ کراہت یہ ہے کہ اس میں فریقین میں سے ایک کی مدد کرنا لازم آتا ہے۔ پس جس طرح خود فریقین میں سے کسی ایک کو تلقین کرنا مکروہ ہے اسی طرح گواہوں کو تلقین کرنا بھی مکروہ ہو گا۔ حضرت امام ابو یوسف نے فرمایا کہ موضع تہمت کے علاوہ میں گواہ کو تلقین کرنا مستحسن ہے۔ کیونکہ قضاء لوگوں کے حقوق زندہ کرنے
اشرف البدایہ جلد - شميم
كتاب الأدب القاضي کے لئے مشروع ہوئی ہے۔ اور گواہ کبھی بھی عدالت کی ہیبت اور رعب کی وجہ سے بیان کرنے سے رک جاتا ہے پس ایسی صورت میں گواہ کو تلقین کرنا، انسانی حق زندہ کرنے کے لئے ہوگا جیسے کسی شخص کو فریقین میں سے ایک کو بلانے کے لئے بھیجنا اور احدا اتضمین سے دوسرے کے لئے کفیل لینا یہ اعانت مستحسن ہے۔ اسی طرح غیر موضع تہمت میں گواہ کو تلقین کرنے کے ذریعہ مدد کرنا بھی مستحسن ہے۔ موضع تہمت کی مثال یہ ہے کہ مدعی نے ایک ہزار پانچ سو درہم کا دعوی کیا اور مدعی علیہ نے پانچ سو درہم کا انکار کیا اور گواہ نے ایک ہزار کی گواہی دی۔ پس اگر قاضی نے کہا کہ شاید مدعی نے پانچ سو درہم معاف کر دیے ہوں تو اس سے گواہ آگاہ ہو کر اپنی گواہی درست کر لے گا۔ پس ایسی تلقین بالا تفاق نا جائز ہے۔
The ruling on prompting a witness by the judge. He said: It is disliked (makruh) to prompt a witness. Its meaning is that he says to him: 'Do you testify to such and such?' This is because it is assistance to one of the two litigants, so it is disliked like prompting the litigant. Abu Yusuf deemed it good (istihsan) in a place free from suspicion, because the witness may be hesitant due to the awe of the court. So it becomes similar to sending a person and taking a surety from one of the disputants. Translation: And prompting a witness is disliked. Its meaning is that he says to the witness: 'Are you a witness to such and such a thing?' And this is because it is assistance to one of the litigants, so it is disliked like prompting the litigant himself. And Imam Abu Yusuf deemed it good (istihsan) in a place free from suspicion, because sometimes the witness is restrained by the awe of the court. So prompting him becomes reviving a right, like sending someone and taking a surety from one of the disputants. Explanation: Talqin by the judge means he says something by which the witness obtains that which is related to testimony. For example, the judge says to the witness: 'Are you a witness to such and such?' In any case, prompting the witness in this manner is disliked. And the reason for dislike is that it necessarily involves helping one of the parties. So just as prompting one of the litigants himself is disliked, similarly prompting witnesses is also disliked. Imam Abu Yusuf said that outside the place of suspicion, prompting the witness is commendable (mustahsan), because the judiciary was legislated to revive people's rights. And sometimes the witness refrains from speaking due to the awe and dignity of the court. So in such a case, prompting the witness will be for reviving a human right, just as sending a person to call one of the parties and taking a surety from one of the disputants for the other is commendable assistance. Similarly, outside the place of suspicion, helping the witness by prompting is also commendable. An example of a place of suspicion is that the plaintiff claimed one thousand five hundred dirhams, and the defendant denied five hundred dirhams, and the witness testified for one thousand. Then if the judge says, 'Perhaps the plaintiff waived five hundred dirhams,' the witness would become aware and correct his testimony. Such prompting is unanimously impermissible.
Source pages p. 266

Commentary
This passage deals with the ruling on a judge prompting a witness (talqin al-shahid). It opens by stating that it is makruh (disliked) for the judge to say to a witness, 'Do you testify to such and such?' The reasoning is that this constitutes assistance to one of the litigants, and prompting a litigant is already makruh, so prompting the witness is likewise. However, Imam Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on him) makes an exception: in situations where there is no suspicion of partiality (ghayr mawdi' al-tuhmah), he considers it mustahsan (commendable) because the witness may be intimidated by the court's awe and may withhold testimony. In such a case, prompting helps revive a right. The text draws an analogy: just as it is commendable to send someone to summon a party or to take a surety for the other, so too is prompting the witness. An example of a place of suspicion is given: if a plaintiff claims 1500 dirhams, the defendant denies 500, and the witness testifies for 1000, the judge should not say 'Perhaps the plaintiff waived 500' because that would guide the witness to adjust his testimony, which is impermissible by consensus. Thus, the general rule is makruh, but Abu Yusuf's istihsan applies where no suspicion arises and the witness is genuinely hesitant due to awe.

Key Terms
تلقین (talqin): The judge prompting a witness by suggesting what to say or asking leading questions.
شاہد (shahid): A witness who testifies in court.
موضع تہمت (mawdi' al-tuhmah): A situation where the judge's prompting could be seen as biased or suspicious.
استحسان (istihsan): A method of juristic preference, used here by Abu Yusuf to override the general dislike.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under what condition did Imam Abu Yusuf deem prompting a witness commendable (mustahsan)?
A) When the witness is a relative of the judge
B) In any situation where the judge feels it is needed
C) Outside the place of suspicion, when the witness is hesitant due to court awe
D) Only when the defendant requests it

Key Takeaway
Prompting a witness is generally makruh, but becomes mustahsan to revive a right where no suspicion of bias exists.

Imprisonment of a Debtor: Condition of Procrastination Must Appear
Setting the rule for when a debtor may be imprisoned after a claim is proven.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for when a debtor may be imprisoned after the debt is established, distinguishing between confession (iqrar) and evidence (bayyinah).

Core Idea
Imprisonment is punishment for procrastination; a confessing debtor must first be ordered to pay.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a practical aspect of judicial authority: when can a judge imprison a debtor who fails to pay? The Hanafi school emphasizes that imprisonment is not a default penalty but a last resort to coerce a procrastinator. The critical condition is that procrastination (mumatalah) must be evident before the judge orders detention. This lesson unpacks that rule and its proofs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon (imprisonment of a debtor) and the hukm level (imprisonment is a permitted means of coercion, not a punishment).
The ruling focuses on the judge's duty: when to imprison, not the debtor's obligation.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the proofs cited: Quranic verse (Surah al-Ma'idah 5:33 interpreted as imprisonment), Sunnah (Prophet's practice), and rational analogy (judge cannot use beating, so imprisonment is necessary).
The author uses both naqli and aqli proofs.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the proofs yield the specific ruling. The Quranic 'exile' is interpreted as detention; the Sunnah shows precedent; reason shows imprisonment is a milder coercion.
The link between the dalil and the ruling is through the concept of mumatalah.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Identify the difference with other schools: some allow immediate imprisonment on confession; Hanafis require a prior order to pay and refusal.
The ikhtilaf is only for confession; for evidence, all agree on immediate imprisonment.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is relied upon (mufta bihi) because it protects the debtor from hasty imprisonment and ensures that only deliberate procrastination is punished.
The tarjih is based on the principle that punishment must follow clear proof of the cause (mumatalah).

Chapter on Imprisonment. Translation: This chapter is about imprisoning in jail. Explanation: Since imprisonment is among the rulings of judiciary and many rulings are attached to it, the issues of imprisonment are mentioned in a separate chapter. Imprisonment is legislated by both the Book and the Sunnah. From the Book, because in Allah's statement 'or they be exiled from the land' (Surah al-Ma'idah 5:33), the intended meaning of exile is imprisonment. From the Sunnah, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) imprisoned a person for the crime of suspicion. And Imam al-Khassaf mentioned that some people from Hijaz fought until they killed a person, so the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) imprisoned them. In the time of the Prophet and Abu Bakr, there were no regular prisons. If there was a need to imprison someone, they would imprison in the mosque or in the hallway. Umar al-Farooq, during his caliphate, bought a house in Makkah for four thousand dirhams and made it a prison. Some scholars think that regular prisons did not exist in the time of Umar and Uthman; rather, Ali was the first to build a prison. Allamah Ibn al-Humam wrote quoting from al-Faiq that Ali built a prison of bamboo etc. and named it 'Nafi'. But once thieves broke in and prisoners escaped, he built a prison of mud and mortar and named it 'Khas'. Rationally, the legitimacy of a prison is also established: the judge's primary duty is to deliver rights to people. But if the defendant refuses to pay the plaintiff's right, the judge will force him to pay. And it is agreed that beating is not used for coercion. So coercion through detention and imprisonment is better. And when coercion through detention and imprisonment is done, then building a prison is also legitimate. Instructions for the judge regarding imprisonment: He said: When the right is established before the judge and the right-holder demands the imprisonment of his debtor, he should not hasten to imprison him, and should order him to pay what is due from him, because imprisonment is the punishment for procrastination, so its appearance is necessary. And this is when the right is established by his confession, because he is not known to be procrastinating at first glance; perhaps he hoped for a delay and did not bring the money. Then if he refuses after that, he imprisons him, because his procrastination has become apparent. But if it is established by evidence, he imprisons him, because procrastination is apparently established by his denial. Translation: And when the right is established before the judge and the right-holder demands the imprisonment of his debtor, he should not hasten to imprison him, and order the debtor to pay whatever is upon him. Because imprisonment is the punishment for procrastination, so the appearance of procrastination is necessary. And this is when the right is established by the confession of the defendant, because initially his procrastination is not known. So perhaps he thought he would get a delay and did not bring the money. Then when he refuses after that, he should imprison him because his procrastination has become apparent.
Source pages p. 268

Commentary
This passage begins the chapter on imprisonment (fasl fi al-habs) from the book on the judge's conduct (Adab al-Qadi). The author first establishes the legitimacy of imprisonment from the Quran, Sunnah, and reason. From the Quran, the verse 'or they be exiled from the land' is interpreted to include imprisonment. From the Sunnah, the Prophet's practice of detaining suspects is cited, and the early caliphs' establishment of prisons. Rationally, since a judge cannot use physical force, imprisonment is a necessary tool to compel payment of debts. The passage then presents the first ruling: when a debt is proven and the creditor demands imprisonment, the judge should not immediately imprison the debtor. Instead, he should first order the debtor to pay. Imprisonment is a punishment for procrastination (mumatalah), so procrastination must first be evident. This applies when the debt is established by the debtor's own confession (iqrar), because initially the debtor may not be procrastinating—he may have simply not brought the money hoping for a delay. If after being ordered to pay he refuses, then he may be imprisoned. However, if the debt is established by evidence (bayyinah), the judge may imprison him immediately because the debtor's denial itself indicates procrastination. The text ends with that rule.

Key Terms
حبس (habs): Imprisonment as a judicial measure to coerce a debtor to pay or a defendant to appear.
مماطلة (mumāṭalah): Deliberate procrastination in paying a debt despite ability to pay.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

D) Only if the debtor is wealthy

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a debtor who confesses to a debt cannot be imprisoned immediately; the judge must first order payment and only detain after refusal, ensuring that imprisonment is a punishment for true procrastination.
