The Legitimacy of Imprisonment in Islamic Law
Establishes the legitimacy of imprisonment from Quran, Sunnah, and reason

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the evidence from Quran, Sunnah, and reason for the legitimacy of imprisonment in Hanafi fiqh.

Core Idea
Imprisonment is legislated via Quranic interpretation, prophetic practice, and rational necessity—a vital tool for enforcing rights.

This passage from the Hanafi text 'Ashraf al-Hidayah' establishes the legal basis for imprisonment. The author argues from three sources: the Quranic verse on exile (5:33), the Prophet's practice of imprisoning suspects, and a rational argument that since a judge cannot use beating, imprisonment is the appropriate means of coercion. Understanding this foundational ruling is essential for grasping the judge's authority in Islamic criminal and civil law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three proofs
Recognise that the author uses Quran, Sunnah, and rational reasoning to justify imprisonment.
These correspond to the three types of Islamic legal evidence: naqli (Quran), naqli (Sunnah), and aqli (reason).
2
Examine the Quranic evidence
The verse 'or exile from the land' (5:33) is interpreted as imprisonment, not literal exile.
This interpretation is based on the broader goal of incapacitating criminals.
3
Examine the Sunnah evidence
The Prophet imprisoned a person on suspicion and later a group for fighting. This shows practical application.
Imam al-Khassaf reported these incidents.
4
Examine the rational proof
The judge must enforce rights but cannot use beating; therefore imprisonment is the best coercion.
This is a qiyas based on maslaha (public interest).
5
Understand the historical development
Formal prisons were not built until later caliphs, showing gradual institutionalization.
Ali built the first permanent prison called 'Nafi' and later 'Khis'.

Commentary
This passage establishes the legal basis for imprisonment in Islamic law. Finally, it provides a rational argument: since a judge must enforce rights and cannot use physical beating, imprisonment is a legitimate means of coercion. This is a ruling with proof from Quran, Sunnah, and rational reasoning. The Hanafi position is that imprisonment is legislated and necessary for the functioning of justice.

Key Terms
حبس (habs): Imprisonment, confinement; a legal tool for coercion in debts and criminal cases.
مشروع (mashru'): Legislated, lawful; established by divine law.

Imprisonment for Debt: Admission vs. Evidence (Intra-Hanafi Dispute)
Explains the judge's procedure based on mode of proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the mainstream Hanafi ruling on imprisoning a debtor based on the mode of proof (admission vs. evidence), explain the rationale of procrastination (mumatlah), and distinguish the mainstream view from the opposing view of Shams al-A'imma al-Sarkhasi.

Core Idea
Imprisonment is punishment for procrastination, not debt; only when procrastination is apparent (from evidence) is immediate imprisonment justified.

This passage from al-Hidayah addresses a practical qada issue: when a creditor demands imprisonment of a debtor, the judge must not act hastily. The key is to determine whether the debtor is procrastinating (mumatlah) or simply unable to pay. The mode of proof—admission or evidence—signals whether procrastination is present. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its rationale, and an important intra-Hanafi disagreement.

Guided Path
1
State the mainstream Hanafi position
First, identify the two scenarios: debt proven by admission vs. by evidence. The mainstream view (from al-Hidayah) states that on admission, the judge orders payment and only imprisons if the debtor refuses; on evidence, the judge imprisons immediately.
2
Examine the rationale (talil)
Understand the underlying reasoning: imprisonment is a punishment for procrastination (mumatlah). Therefore, procrastination must be established. With admission, the debtor may have a plausible excuse (e.g., hope for delay), so procrastination is not yet apparent. With evidence, the debtor's denial itself constitutes procrastination.
This is a causal link: mumatlah → punishment.
3
Identify the opposing intra-Hanafi view
Shams al-A'imma al-Sarkhasi reverses the ruling: immediate imprisonment on admission, delay on evidence. His reasoning: with evidence, the debtor can claim ignorance of the debt, so procrastination is not certain; with admission, the debtor knew and did not pay, so procrastination is clear.
4
Analyse the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
Consider a debtor who admits but asks for time. Under the mainstream view, he gets a chance; under Sarkhasi's view, he would be imprisoned immediately. This shows how the difference in inference of procrastination changes the outcome.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon position (as in al-Hidayah) is the mainstream view, despite Sarkhasi's respected dissent. Tarjih is based on the weight of the majority and the standard practice.
Ibn al-Humam mentions both views but upholds the Hidayah position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

قال و اذا ثبت الحق عند القاضى وطلب صاحب الحق حبس غريمه لم يعجل بحبسه وامره بدفع ما عليه لان الحبس جزاء المماطلة فلا بد من ظهورها و هذا اذا ثبت الحق باقراره لانه لم يعرف كونه مما طلا فى اول الوهلة قلعله طمع في الامهال فلم يستصحب المال فاذا امتنع بعد ذلك حبسه لظهور مطله اما اذا ثبت ينة حبسه كـ ثبت ظهور المطل بانکاره
ترجمہ اور جب قاضی کے نزدیک حق ثابت ہوا اور صاحب حق نے اپنے قرضدار کا قید کیا جانا طلب کیا تو اس کو قید کرنے میں جلدی نہ کرے اور قرضدار کو حکم کرے کہ جو کچھ اس پر ہے وہ دیدے۔ اس لئے کہ محبوس کرنا ٹال مٹول کی سزا ہے پس ٹال مٹول کا ظاہر ہونا ضروری ہے اور یہ اس وقت ہے جب مدعی علیہ کے اقرار سے حق ثابت ہوا ہو ۔ کیونکہ اول وہلہ میں اس کا ٹال مٹول کرنے والا ہونا معلوم نہیں ہوا۔ پس شائد اس نے مہلت پانے کا گمان کیا ہو اور مال ساتھ نہ لایا ہو۔ پھر جب اس کے بعد اس نے انکار کیا تو اس کو قید کرے کیونکہ اس کا ٹال مٹول کرنا ظاہر ہو گیا۔ اور اگر حق گواہوں کے ذریعہ ثابت ہوا تو قاضی اس کو حق ثابت ہوتے ہی قید کرے گا۔ کیونکہ اس کے انکار کرنے کی وجہ سے ٹال مٹول کرنا ظاہر ہو گیا۔
تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ جب صاحب حق کا حق قاضی کے نزدیک ثابت ہو جائے اور صاحب حق اپنے قرضدار کی گرفتاری کا مطالبہ کرے تو اس کی دو صورتیں ہیں۔
ا اس کا حق یا تو اقرار کے ذریعہ ثابت ہوگا۔
اور یا گواہوں کے ذریعہ ثابت ہوگا۔
اگر اؤل ہے تو قاضی قرضدار کو محبوس کرنے میں جلدی نہ کرے بلکہ قرضدار کو حکم دے کہ وہ صاحب حق کا قرضہ ادا کرے۔ قرضہ ایک درہم ہو یا اس سے کم ہو یا اس سے زائد ہو۔
دلیل یہ ہے کہ قید اور جس ٹال مٹول کی سزا ہے لہذا قید کرنے کے واسطے قرضدار کی طرف سے ٹال مٹول کا ظاہر ہونا ضروری ہے ۔ پس جب قرضدار کے اقرار کی وجہ سے صاحب حق کا حق ثابت ہو گیا تو اول دہلہ میں اس کی طرف سے ٹال مٹول کا اظہار نہیں ہو سکے گا ۔ کیونکہ وہ یہ کہ سکتا ہے کہ مجھ کو چونکہ مہات مل جانے کی امید تھی اس لئے میں اپنے ساتھ مال نہیں لایا تھا۔ اب اگر آپ مہات دینے سے انکار کرتے ہیں تو میں آپ کا حق ادا کرتا ہوں ۔ لیکن اگر صاحب حق کا حق ثابت ہونے کے بعد قرضدار اس کا حق ادا کرنے سے رک گیا تو اس صورت میں چونکہ قرضدار کی طرف سے ٹال مٹول کرنا پایا گیا۔ اس لئے قاضی اس کو قید کرے گا ۔ اور اگر ثانی ہے یعنی حق گواہوں کے ذریعہ ثابت ہوا ہے تو قاضی ، قرضدار کو حق ثابت ہوتے ہی قید کر سکتا ہے۔ کیونکہ گواہوں کے ذریعہ حق اس وقت ثابت کیا جاتا ہے جب مدعی علیہ حق کا منکر ہو ۔ پس جب مدعی علیہ یعنی قرضدار نے قرضہ کا انکار کیا تو وہ ٹال مٹول کرنے والا ہو گیا۔ اور ٹال مٹول کی سزا چونکہ قید ہے اس لئے حق ثابت ہوتے ہی قرضدار کو قید کر لیا جائے گا۔ علامہ ابن الہمام نے لکھا ہے کہ شمس الائمہ سرخی کے نزدیک اس کا بر عکس ہے یعنی حق ، بینہ کے ذریعہ ثابت ہونے کی صورت میں اول وبلہ میں قرضدار کو قید نہیں کیا جائے گا۔ اور اقرار سے ثابت ہونے کی صورت میں فورا قید کر لیا جائے گا۔ اور وجہ یہ بیان کی ہے کہ بینہ کے ذریعہ ثابت ہونے کی صورت میں قرضدار یہ کہ سکتا ہے کہ مجھے معلوم نہیں تھا کہ مجھ پر قرضہ ہے لیکن اب جبکہ معلوم ہو گیا کہ مجھ پر قرضہ ہے تو اب اس کو ادا کرنے میں سستی نہیں کروں گا۔ پس اس عذر کے بعد یہ نہیں کہا جا سکتا کہ قرضدار کی طرف سے ٹال مٹول کرنا پایا گیا اور جب ٹال مٹول کرنا نہیں پایا گیا تو اس کو قید بھی نہیں کیا جا سکتا ہے۔ لیکن اقرار کی صورت میں قرضدار یہ عذر پیش نہیں کر سکتا۔ اور جب یہ عذر پیش نہیں کر سکتا تو ٹال مٹول کرنے کی وجہ سے اس کو قید کر لیا جائے گا۔
Instructions for the judge regarding imprisonment: He said: If the right is established before the judge and the claimant demands imprisonment of his debtor, he should not hasten to imprison him, and order him to pay what is due. Because imprisonment is the punishment for procrastination, so procrastination must appear. This is when the right is established by his admission, because it is not known at first that he is procrastinating; perhaps he hoped for a delay and did not bring the money. If he refuses after that, imprison him because his procrastination has become apparent. But if it is established by evidence, imprison him as soon as it is established, because procrastination appears by his denial. Translation: When the right is established before the judge and the claimant demands his debtor be imprisoned, he should not hasten to imprison him, but order the debtor to pay what is on him. Because imprisonment is the punishment for procrastination, so procrastination must appear. This is when the right is established by the defendant's admission, because at first it is not known that he is procrastinating. Perhaps he hoped for a delay and did not bring the money. Then if he refuses after that, imprison him because his procrastination has become apparent. But if the right is established by witnesses, the judge will imprison him as soon as the right is established, because procrastination appears by his denial. Explanation: The scenario is when the claimant's right is established before the judge and he demands the arrest of his debtor. There are two cases: (1) His right is established by admission. (2) It is established by witnesses. If the first, the judge should not hasten to imprison the debtor, but order him to pay the debt. The evidence is that imprisonment is the punishment for procrastination, so for imprisonment, procrastination must appear. When the debt is established by the debtor's admission, initially procrastination cannot be shown because he can say: 'I hoped for a delay, so I didn't bring the money. Now if you refuse to give me a delay, I will pay your right.' But if after the right is established, the debtor stops paying, then procrastination is found, so the judge will imprison him. If the second, i.e., the right is established by witnesses, the judge can imprison the debtor as soon as the right is established. Because the right is established by witnesses only when the defendant denies the right. So when the defendant denied the debt, he became procrastinating. And since the punishment for procrastination is imprisonment, the debtor will be imprisoned as soon as the right is established. Allamah Ibn al-Humam wrote that according to Shams al-A'imma al-Sarkhasi, the opposite is the case: in case of proof by evidence, the debtor should not be imprisoned initially, and in case of admission, he should be imprisoned immediately. The reason given is that in case of evidence, the debtor can say: 'I did not know I owed this debt, but now that I know, I will not be lazy in paying it.' After this excuse, it cannot be said that procrastination is found, and when procrastination is not found, he cannot be imprisoned. But in case of admission, the debtor cannot offer this excuse, and since he cannot offer it, he will be imprisoned for procrastination.
Source pages p. 268

Commentary
This passage details the procedure for a judge when a creditor demands imprisonment of a debtor. The ruling distinguishes between two modes of proof: admission (iqrar) and evidence (bayyinah). In case of admission, the judge gives the debtor a chance to pay, unless he refuses, showing procrastination. In case of evidence (which implies denial), the judge can imprison immediately. The reasoning is that imprisonment is a punishment for procrastination, and only when the debtor has shown procrastination is it justified. With admission, the debtor may have a valid excuse for not bringing the money, so he is given an opportunity. With evidence, the debtor's denial already demonstrates procrastination. The passage also presents an intra-Hanafi dispute: Shams al-A'imma al-Sarkhasi reverses the ruling, arguing that with evidence the debtor can claim ignorance, thus no procrastination, while with admission his refusal is clear. The relied-upon position (from al-Hidayah) is the first view.

Key Terms
مماطلة (mumatlah): Procrastination, delay in payment; the key condition for imprisoning a debtor.
اقرار (iqrar): Admission, confession; the debtor's own acknowledgment of the debt.
بينة (bayyinah): Evidence, proof, typically by two male witnesses.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mainstream Hanafi position, when can a judge imprison a debtor immediately?
A) When the debt is proven by admission
B) When the debt is proven by evidence
C) Only after the debtor has been asked three times
D) Never

Key Takeaway
The judge must distinguish between admission and evidence when deciding to imprison a debtor, because only evidence signals procrastination.

Types of Debt Warranting Imprisonment (Hanafi)
Specifies which debts lead to imprisonment of the debtor

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which debts justify imprisonment in Hanafi law and explain the rationale behind the distinction.

Core Idea
Imprisonment is only for debts where the debtor received property or freely obligated himself.

When can a judge imprison a debtor? Not every debt leads to jail. Hanafi law draws a clear line: only debts arising from exchange (like sale price) or voluntary contractual obligations (like dower or guaranty) qualify. This lesson examines the rule and its underlying logic.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal act
What is the ruling about? The act of imprisoning a debtor for non-payment of debt. The passage specifies the scope of this act.
2
List the qualifying debts
From the text: price of a sold item (thaman al-mabi'), prompt dower (mu'ajjal mahr), and guaranty (kafalah). These debts share the characteristic of the debtor having received property or voluntarily undertaken the obligation.
Prompt dower is due immediately; deferred dower is excluded.
3
Identify the exception
Deferred dower (mu'ajjal) is explicitly excluded. The due date has not arrived, so imprisonment is not allowed.
4
Understand the reasoning
The rationale: when the debtor receives property or voluntarily obligates, it indicates his ability to pay. The text states: 'because when the property came into his hand, his freedom from need is established... he only undertakes what he is able to pay.'
This reasoning prevents imprisonment for debts that do not imply solvency.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کس قرضہ کے عوض قید خانہ میں قاضی ڈال سکتا ہے
قال فان امتنع حبسه في كل دين لزمه بدلا عن مال حصل في يده كثمن المبيع او التزمه بعقد كالمهر والكفالة لانه اذا حصل المال فى يده ثبت غناؤه به و اقدامه على التزامه باختبار، دليل يساره اذهو لا يلتزم الا ما يقدر على ادائه والمراد بالمهر معجله دون مؤجله
For what debt the judge can imprison? He said: If he refuses, imprison him for every debt that is incumbent on him as a substitute for property that came into his hand, such as the price of a sold item, or that he obligated by contract, such as dower and guaranty. Because when the property came into his hand, his freedom from need is established by it, and his undertaking it is by choice, evidence of his solvency; for he only undertakes what he is able to pay. And by 'dower' is meant the prompt dower, not the deferred.
Source pages p. 268

Commentary
This passage specifies the types of debts for which a judge can imprison a debtor. The principle is that imprisonment is for debts that arise from a contract where the debtor received property (like price of sale) or obligated himself (like dower or guaranty). The reason is that by receiving the property or undertaking the obligation, the debtor is assumed to be capable of paying. However, this does not apply to all debts; for example, deferred dower is excluded because the due date is not yet reached. This is a ruling statement that defines the scope of imprisonment in debts.

Key Terms
دين (dayn): Debt; here specifically debts arising from exchange (sale price) or contractual obligations (dower, guaranty).
مهر (mahr): Dower; prompt (mu'ajjal) dower is subject to imprisonment, deferred is not.
كفالة (kafalah): Guaranty, surety; a contractual obligation to pay if the principal defaults.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Both prompt and deferred
B) Only prompt
C) Only deferred
D) Neither

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, imprisonment for debt is limited to debts where the debtor received property or voluntarily obligated himself, such as sale price, prompt dower, and guaranty.

Imprisoning a Debtor: Acknowledgment vs. Witnesses
Intra-Hanafi dispute on imprisoning debtor

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on immediate imprisonment of a debtor based on whether the debt is proven by acknowledgment or witnesses, and explain the intra-Hanafi disagreement with Shams al-A'imma al-Sarkhasi.

Core Idea
Imprisonment is for evasion; only when denial is clear (witnesses) is it immediate.

A judge faces a request to imprison a debtor. The ruling depends on how the debt was proven. If the debtor acknowledged the debt, he may have a valid excuse for not paying immediately, so imprisonment is not immediate. But if witnesses proved the debt, the debtor must have denied it—which itself is evasion—so the judge can imprison right away. However, a prominent Hanafi scholar, Shams al-A'imma al-Sarkhasi, held the opposite view. Let's examine the reasoning and the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two methods of proving debt
Note that a debt can be established either by the debtor's own acknowledgment (iqrar) or by the testimony of witnesses (bayyinah).
Acknowledgment implies the debtor does not deny; witnesses imply he did deny.
2
Understand the legal principle
Imprisonment is a penalty for evasion (tal-matool). So, for immediate imprisonment, evasion must be apparent from the debtor.
If the debtor has a reasonable excuse, there is no evasion.
3
Apply to acknowledgment scenario
When the debtor acknowledges, he may claim he did not bring money because he hoped for a respite. This is a valid excuse, so evasion is not established. The judge should first order payment, and only imprison if the debtor later refuses.
The key is that the debtor can offer an excuse at the time of acknowledgment.
4
Apply to witnesses scenario
When witnesses testify, it implies the debtor denied the debt in court, which is itself an act of evasion (he is avoiding payment by denying). Therefore, evasion is already apparent, and the judge can imprison immediately upon proof.
The debtor's denial shows unwillingness to pay, justifying immediate imprisonment.
5
Note the contrary view of Shams al-A'imma al-Sarkhasi
Sarkhasi reverses the two scenarios: immediate imprisonment for acknowledgment (since the debtor cannot claim ignorance of the debt), and no immediate imprisonment for witnesses (since the debtor can claim he did not know he owed the debt).
This is an intra-Hanafi disagreement; both views are valid but the first is the relied-upon position.
6
Determine the mufta bihi
The main text's position (immediate imprisonment for witnesses, not for acknowledgment) is the standard Hanafi ruling, as it is presented as the default and is from the established texts.
Later Hanafi authorities like Ibn al-Humam report Sarkhasi's view but the original view remains operative.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ٹال مٹول کرنا ظاہر ہو گیا۔ اور اگر حق گواہوں کے ذریعہ ثابت ہوا تو قاضی اس کو حق ثابت ہوتے ہی قید کرے گا۔ کیونکہ اس کے انکار کرنے کی وجہ سے ٹال مٹول کرنا ظاہر ہو گیا۔
تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ جب صاحب حق کا حق قاضی کے نزدیک ثابت ہو جائے اور صاحب حق اپنے قرضدار کی گرفتاری کا مطالبہ کرے تو اس کی دو صورتیں ہیں۔
ا اس کا حق یا تو اقرار کے ذریعہ ثابت ہوگا۔
اور یا گواہوں کے ذریعہ ثابت ہوگا۔
اگر اؤل ہے تو قاضی قرضدار کو محبوس کرنے میں جلدی نہ کرے بلکہ قرضدار کو حکم دے کہ وہ صاحب حق کا قرضہ ادا کرے۔ قرضہ ایک درہم ہو یا اس سے کم ہو یا اس سے زائد ہو۔
دلیل یہ ہے کہ قید اور جس ٹال مٹول کی سزا ہے لہذا قید کرنے کے واسطے قرضدار کی طرف سے ٹال مٹول کا ظاہر ہونا ضروری ہے ۔ پس جب قرضدار کے اقرار کی وجہ سے صاحب حق کا حق ثابت ہو گیا تو اول دہلہ میں اس کی طرف سے ٹال مٹول کا اظہار نہیں ہو سکے گا ۔ کیونکہ وہ یہ کہ سکتا ہے کہ مجھ کو چونکہ مہات مل جانے کی امید تھی اس لئے میں اپنے ساتھ مال نہیں لایا تھا۔ اب اگر آپ مہات دینے سے انکار کرتے ہیں تو میں آپ کا حق ادا کرتا ہوں ۔ لیکن اگر صاحب حق کا حق ثابت ہونے کے بعد قرضدار اس کا حق ادا کرنے سے رک گیا تو اس صورت میں چونکہ قرضدار کی طرف سے ٹال مٹول کرنا پایا گیا۔ اس لئے قاضی اس کو قید کرے گا ۔ اور اگر ثانی ہے یعنی حق گواہوں کے ذریعہ ثابت ہوا ہے تو قاضی ، قرضدار کو حق ثابت ہوتے ہی قید کر سکتا ہے۔ کیونکہ گواہوں کے ذریعہ حق اس وقت ثابت کیا جاتا ہے جب مدعی علیہ حق کا منکر ہو ۔ پس جب مدعی علیہ یعنی قرضدار نے قرضہ کا انکار کیا تو وہ ٹال مٹول کرنے والا ہو گیا۔ اور ٹال مٹول کی سزا چونکہ قید ہے اس لئے حق ثابت ہوتے ہی قرضدار کو قید کر لیا جائے گا۔ علامہ ابن الہمام نے لکھا ہے کہ شمس الائمہ سرخی کے نزدیک اس کا بر عکس ہے یعنی حق ، بینہ کے ذریعہ ثابت ہونے کی صورت میں اول وبلہ میں قرضدار کو قید نہیں کیا جائے گا۔ اور اقرار سے ثابت ہونے کی صورت میں فورا قید کر لیا جائے گا۔ اور وجہ یہ بیان کی ہے کہ بینہ کے ذریعہ ثابت ہونے کی صورت میں قرضدار یہ کہ سکتا ہے کہ مجھے معلوم نہیں تھا کہ مجھ پر قرضہ ہے لیکن اب جبکہ معلوم ہو گیا کہ مجھ پر قرضہ ہے تو اب اس کو ادا کرنے میں سستی نہیں کروں گا۔ پس اس عذر کے بعد یہ نہیں کہا جا سکتا کہ قرضدار کی طرف سے ٹال مٹول کرنا پایا گیا اور جب ٹال مٹول کرنا نہیں پایا گیا تو اس کو قید بھی نہیں کیا جا سکتا ہے۔ لیکن اقرار کی صورت میں قرضدار یہ عذر پیش نہیں کر سکتا۔ اور جب یہ عذر پیش نہیں کر سکتا تو ٹال مٹول کرنے کی وجہ سے اس کو قید کر لیا جائے گا۔
Evasion became apparent. And if the right is proven through witnesses, the judge will imprison him immediately upon proof, because due to his denial, evasion became apparent. Explanation: The case is that when the right of the claimant is established before the judge and the claimant demands the arrest of his debtor, there are two scenarios: 1) His right is proven through acknowledgment. 2) Or through witnesses. If the first, the judge should not hasten to imprison the debtor but order him to pay the debt, whether it is one dirham or less or more. The reason is that imprisonment is the penalty for evasion, so for imprisonment, evasion must be apparent from the debtor. So when the right is proven through the debtor's acknowledgment, in the first instance evasion is not manifested because he can say: 'I hoped to get a respite, so I did not bring money with me. Now if you deny me a respite, I will pay your right.' But if after proof the debtor refrains from paying, then evasion is found and the judge imprisons him. If the second, i.e., the right is proven through witnesses, the judge can imprison the debtor immediately, because the right is proved through witnesses only when the defendant denies the right. So when the defendant denied the debt, he became an evader. And since the penalty for evasion is imprisonment, he is imprisoned immediately. Allama Ibn al-Humam wrote that according to Shams al-A'imma al-Sarkhasi, the opposite is true: if proven by bayyinah, he is not imprisoned initially; if by acknowledgment, he is imprisoned immediately. His reason: when proven by bayyinah, the debtor can say he did not know he had a debt, but now that he knows, he will not delay. So evasion is not found. But in acknowledgment, he cannot make this excuse, so he is imprisoned for evasion.
Source pages p. 269

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute and ruling clarification. The text first states the general principle: imprisonment is for evasion. When a debt is proven by the debtor's own acknowledgment, he may have a valid excuse for not paying immediately (e.g., he thought he could get more time). Therefore, the judge should first order him to pay and only imprison if he refuses after that. If the debt is proven by witnesses, the debtor must have denied the debt, which is already evasion, so imprisonment is immediate. Then a contrary view from Shams al-A'imma al-Sarkhasi is reported: he reverses the two scenarios. His reasoning: with witnesses, the debtor can claim ignorance; with acknowledgment, he cannot. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the first one (the main text), as this is from the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
ٹال مٹول (tal-matool): Evasion or delaying tactics in paying a debt.
اقرار (iqrar): Acknowledgment or confession of debt by the debtor.
بینہ (bayyinah): Witness evidence presented in court.
قید (qayd): Imprisonment, specifically as a legal penalty for evasion of debt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the main Hanafi position, when is a debtor immediately imprisoned upon proof of debt?
A) When the debt is proven by the debtor's acknowledgment
B) When the debt is proven by witnesses
C) In both cases equally
D) Only if the debt is more than 10 dirhams

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes between acknowledgment (possible excuse, no immediate imprisonment) and witnesses (denial implies evasion, immediate imprisonment), with an intra-madhhab alternative from Sarkhasi.

Debts That Justify Imprisonment: Property Received or Voluntary Contract
Ruling with rational proof on imprisonable debts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two categories of debts that justify imprisonment in Hanafi law and distinguish between immediate and deferred mahr.

Core Idea
Imprisonment applies only when the debtor received property or voluntarily undertook the debt.

In this lesson, we examine a classical Hanafi ruling on which debts allow the judge to imprison a debtor who refuses to pay after being ordered. The passage distinguishes between debts arising from property actually received and debts voluntarily undertaken by contract. The rational proof (dalil aqli) links debt capacity to the debtor's ability to pay. We also see an important distinction between immediate and deferred mahr.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
What is the judge ordered to do? Imprison the debtor if he refrains from paying a qualifying debt.
Imprisonment is wajib on the judge for these debts.
2
Recognize the two categories of debts
First: debts that are a substitute for property received (e.g., price of a sold item). Second: debts voluntarily obligated by contract (e.g., mahr, kafalah).
Both categories share the illa that the debtor is solvent or able to pay.
3
Understand the rational proof (dalil aqli)
Receiving property proves solvency; voluntarily undertaking a debt proves capability to pay. A solvent person should not be allowed to evade payment.
This is a logical inference, not a textual proof.
4
Apply the distinction for mahr
Only immediate mahr (mahr mu'ajjal) qualifies for imprisonment; deferred mahr (mahr mu'ajjal) does not because it is not due immediately.
The Hidayah clarifies this based on custom.
5
Derive the practical consequence
If a debt does not fall into either category, or if mahr is deferred, the judge should not imprison.
This limits the scope of imprisonable debts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کس قرضہ کے عوض قید خانہ میں قاضی ڈال سکتا ہے
قال فان امتنع حبسه في كل دين لزمه بدلا عن مال حصل في يده كثمن المبيع او التزمه بعقد كالمهر والكفالة لانه اذا حصل المال فى يده ثبت غناؤه به و اقدامه على التزامه باختبار، دليل يساره اذهو لا يلتزم الا ما يقدر على ادائه والمراد بالمهر معجله دون مؤجله
ترجمہ پھر اگر وہ (ادا کرنے سے ) رُک گیا تو اس کو ہر ایسے قرضہ میں قید کرے جو ایسے مال کا عوض ہو جو اس کے قبضہ میں حاصل ہوا ہے جیسے مبیع کا من یا عقد سے اسکو لازم کیا ہے جیسے مہر اور کفالہ کا مال۔ اس لئے کہ جب مال اس کے قبضہ میں آیا تو اس مال کے ذریعہ سے اس کا مالدار ہونا ثابت ہو گیا ہے۔ اور اپنے اختیار سے مال کے التزام پر اس کا اقدام کرنا اس کے مالدار ہونے کی دلیل ہے۔ اس لئے کہ وہ نہیں التزام کرے گا مگر اس مال کا جس کے ادا کرنے پر وہ قادر ہے اور مہر معجل مراد ہے نہ کہ مہر مؤجل ۔

دلیل یہ ہے کہ جب قرضدار کے قبضہ میں مال آیا تو اُس مال کے ذریعہ اُس کا مالدار ہونا ثابت ہو گیا۔ اور جب مالدار قرضہ ادا کرنے سے رک جاتا ہے تو اس کو قید کر لیا جاتا ہے۔ لہذا اس قرضہ میں مذکورہ قرضدار کو قید کر لیا جائے گا یعنی اس سے مطالبہ کیا جائے گا کہ جو بیچ اس کے قبضہ میں ہے اس کو بیچ کر بائع کا مشن ادا کرے۔ اور اپنے اختیار سے اپنے اوپر مال لازم کرنے کا اقدام کرنا اس کے مالدار ہونے کی دلیل ہے۔ کیونکہ انسان اپنے اوپر ایسے ہی مال کا التزام کرے گا۔ جس کو وہ ادا کر سکتا ہے۔ پس مہر اور کفالہ کا مال جب اس نے اپنے ذمہ لیا ہے تو گویا اس کو ادا کر سکتا ہے۔

For which debt can the judge imprison? He said: If he refrains, imprison him for every debt that he owes as a substitute for property that came into his possession, like the price of a sold item, or that he obligated by contract, like mahr and kafalah. Because when wealth came into his possession, his solvency is established, and his action of undertaking obligation voluntarily is evidence of his wealth, as he only undertakes what he can pay. And by mahr is meant immediate mahr, not deferred mahr. Translation: Then if he refrains from paying, the judge imprisons him for every debt that is a substitute for property received in his possession, like the price of a sold item, or that he obligated by contract, like mahr and kafalah. Because when the wealth came into his possession, his solvency is established. And his action of undertaking obligation voluntarily is evidence of his wealth, as he only undertakes what he can pay. And by mahr is meant immediate mahr, not deferred. Explanation: Sahib al-Quduri said: If after the judge's order the debtor refrains from paying, and the creditor demands imprisonment, the judge will imprison him for every debt that is a substitute for property he received in his possession, like the price of the sold item, even if the price is obligatory, but the sold item came into his possession. Or a debt that he obligated by contract, like mahr from marriage, or the property of kafalah. The proof: When property came into his possession, his solvency is established. And when a solvent person refrains from paying, he is imprisoned. So he is imprisoned for such a debt, meaning he is asked to sell what he has in hand and pay the price. And his voluntary undertaking of liability is evidence of his solvency, because a person only undertakes what he can pay. So when he took mahr or kafalah upon himself, he is able to pay. Sahib al-Hidayah says: By mahr in the text is meant immediate (mu'ajjal) mahr, not deferred (mu'ajjal). Because customarily immediate mahr is delivered, not deferred. So if he does not pay immediate mahr, he is imprisoned; if he does not pay deferred mahr, he is not imprisoned.
Source pages p. 269

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof (dalil) regarding which debts justify imprisonment. It specifies two categories: (1) debts that are a substitute for property the debtor actually received (e.g., price of a sold item he bought, so he has the item and can sell it to pay), and (2) debts he voluntarily undertook by contract (e.g., mahr and kafalah). The proof is rational: if he received property, he is solvent; if he undertook a debt voluntarily, he must have capacity to pay. The text also specifies that only immediate mahr (mu'ajjal) is the basis, not deferred mahr, because deferred mahr is not due immediately. The commentary by Sahib al-Quduri and Sahib al-Hidayah reinforces this.

Key Terms
مہر معجل (mahr mu'ajjal): Immediate dower, due at the time of marriage.
كفالة (kafalah): Suretyship or guarantee, where one undertakes to pay another's debt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, which of the following debts would allow the judge to imprison the debtor?
A) A debt for the price of a sold item that the buyer has received.
B) A debt for charity promised but not paid.
C) A debt for deferred mahr (mahr mu'ajjal).
D) A debt for a broken promise (not a contract).

Key Takeaway
Imprisonment for debt in Hanafi fiqh is limited to debts arising from property received or voluntary contracts, and only immediate mahr qualifies.

When the Judge Does Not Imprison a Debtor Claiming Poverty
Lists exceptions to imprisoning a debtor when he claims poverty.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rule regarding imprisonment of a debtor who claims poverty and identify the exceptions and the correct view on the duration of imprisonment.

Core Idea
The debtor's claim of poverty is accepted unless the creditor proves solvency.

This passage from Al-Hidayah clarifies a key procedural rule in qada (judicial rulings): when a debtor claims poverty, the judge does not automatically imprison him. Instead, the burden shifts to the creditor to prove that the debtor has wealth. The text also discusses exceptions and the discretionary duration of imprisonment. Understanding this helps you grasp the Hanafi approach to protecting the rights of both parties while presuming hardship (usr) as the default state.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Core Ruling
Read the first part: 'He does not imprison him apart from that if he says 'I am poor' unless his creditor proves that he has wealth.' This is the general rule: the debtor's claim of poverty is taken as true.
The judge does not imprison based on a mere claim of poverty; evidence of wealth is required for imprisonment.
2
Understand the Basis
The passage explains: 'because no indication of solvency exists, so the word of the debtor is accepted, and the creditor must prove his wealth.' The default is asl al-usr (hardship). This is a procedural presumption in favor of the debtor.
The onus is on the creditor to prove solvency.
3
Note the Two Narrations
Two narrations are given: (1) the debtor's word is accepted in all such matters; (2) except for a debt that is a substitute for property (badal mal). Recognize the exception: when the debt arises from a sale or similar exchange, the debtor's claim is not automatically accepted.
The second narration suggests that if the debtor once had the property (e.g., sold an item), there is an indication of wealth.
4
Apply the Rule to Specific Cases
Two examples: (a) in nafaqah (maintenance) claims, the husband's word of insolvency is accepted; (b) in freeing a jointly-owned slave, the emancipator's word is accepted. These illustrate that nafaqah is not a regular debt but a gift (silah), so the rule differs.
Maintenance falls due upon death by consensus, unlike ordinary debts.
5
Determine the Duration of Imprisonment
When the creditor proves wealth or the judge has suspicion, the debtor may be imprisoned for a limited period (2-3 months) to uncover hidden assets. The correct view: 'al-sahih anna al-taqdeer mufawwad ila ra'y al-qadi' – duration is left to the judge's discretion based on individual circumstances.
Other estimates (1 month, up to 6 months) exist, but the preferred opinion is judicial discretion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كن امور میں قاضی قید میں نہ ڈالے
قال ولا يحبسه فيما سوى ذلك اذا قال انى فقير الا ان يثبت غريمه ان له مالا فيحبسه لانه لم يوجد دلالة اليسار فيكون القول قول من عليه الدين وعلى المدعى اثبات غناه ويروى ان القول لمن عليه الدين في جميع ذلك لان الاصل هو العسرة ويروى ان القول له الا فيما بدله مال و في النفقة القول قول الزوج انه معسر و فى اعتاق العبد المشترك القول للمعتق والمسألتان تؤيد ان القولين الآخرين والتخريج على ما قال فى الكتاب انه ليس بدين مطلق بل هو صلة حتى تسقط النفقة بالموت على الاتفاق وكذا عند ابي حنيفة ضمان الاعتاق ثم فيما كان القول قول المدعى ان له مالاً او ثبت ذلك بالبينة فيما كان القول قول من عليه يحبسه شهرين او ثلثة ثم يسأل عنه فالحبس لظهور ظلمه في الحال وانما يحبسه مدة ليظهر ماله لو كان يخفيه فلا بد من ان تمتد المدة ليفيد هذه الفائدة فقدر بما ذكره ويروى غير ذلك من التقدير بشهر او اربعة الى ستة اشهر والصحيح ان التقدير مفوض الى رأى القاضى لاختلاف احوال الاشخاص فيه
In which matters the judge does not imprison. He said: And he does not imprison him apart from that if he says 'I am poor' unless his creditor proves that he has wealth, then he imprisons him. Because no indication of solvency exists, so the word of the debtor is accepted, and the creditor must prove his wealth. It is narrated that the word of the debtor is accepted in all such matters because the original assumption is hardship. And it is narrated that his word is accepted except regarding a substitute for property. And in the matter of maintenance (nafaqah), the word of the husband is accepted that he is insolvent. And in the emancipation of a jointly owned slave, the word of the emancipator is accepted. These two issues support the two other narrations. And the distinction is based on what he said in the book: that it (maintenance) is not an absolute debt but a gift (silah), so maintenance falls due upon death by consensus. Similarly, according to Abu Hanifah, the guarantee of emancipation (daman al-i'taq). Then regarding those where the word is of the creditor that he has wealth or it is proven by evidence, and those where the word of the debtor is accepted, he imprisons him for two or three months and then asks about him. The imprisonment is for the appearance of his oppression immediately, and he imprisons him for a period to manifest his wealth if he was hiding it. So the period must be extended to achieve this benefit. He estimated it as mentioned. And it is narrated other estimates of one month or four to six months. And the correct view is that the estimate is left to the discretion of the judge due to the differing conditions of individuals.
Source pages p. 270

Commentary
This passage covers cases where a judge does not imprison a debtor who claims poverty. The general rule: the debtor's claim of poverty is accepted (since the default is hardship), unless the creditor proves the debtor has wealth. There are two narrations: one says debtor's word is accepted in all such cases; another says except when the debt is a substitute for property (like price of sold item) because then there is an indication of wealth (the property he received). Then two examples are given: in nafaqah (maintenance) claims, the husband's word of insolvency is accepted; in emancipation of a jointly owned slave, the one who wants to free can claim inability? Actually 'al-qawl li al-mu'tiq' probably means the word of the one who frees is accepted regarding his share. These two examples support the other narrations. The text also discusses imprisonment for a limited period (2-3 months) to see if the debtor was hiding wealth, after which the judge investigates. The duration is left to the judge's discretion. This is a critical refinement (hasiya-style) of the ruling.

Key Terms
یسار (yasar): Solvency, ability to pay debts.
نفقہ (nafaqah): Maintenance, financial support for family.
بدل مال (badal mal): Substitute for property; debt arising from sale or exchange.
عسرہ (usrah): Hardship; the original assumption that people are in difficulty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the correct view regarding the duration of imprisonment for a debtor who claims poverty?
A) Fixed at one month
B) Fixed at three months
C) Fixed at six months
D) Left to the discretion of the judge

Key Takeaway
The judge does not imprison a debtor who claims poverty unless the creditor proves wealth; the duration of imprisonment, if any, is at the judge's discretion.

Two Categories of Debts Warranting Imprisonment
Specifying two categories of debts for imprisonment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two categories of debts for which a Hanafi qadi must imprison a debtor who refuses to pay.

Core Idea
Imprisonment applies only when the debt arises from property received or a voluntary undertaking.

This lesson clarifies the specific types of debts that trigger mandatory imprisonment. The passage distinguishes between debts that are a substitute for property the debtor has already received and debts that the debtor voluntarily took upon himself through a contract. Understanding this ruling is crucial for qadis and muftis dealing with enforcement of payment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The passage begins with a conditional ruling: if the debtor stops paying after the qadi's order, the qadi must imprison him for certain debts.
This is a wajib ruling for the qadi.
2
Name the first category
First category: debts that are a substitute (iwad) for property that has come into the debtor's possession, such as the price of a sold item (thaman al-mabi').
The key point is that the debtor received the property, so he can sell it to pay.
3
Name the second category
Second category: debts that the debtor made binding upon himself through a contract, like immediate dower (mahr mu'ajjal) and the amount guaranteed in kafalah.
Voluntary undertaking indicates the debtor believes he can pay.
4
Understand the condition implied
The passage implies that for these debts, the qadi does not need to verify the debtor's ability to pay; the nature of the debt itself establishes that ability.
This is based on the principle that a person only undertakes what he can pay.

پھر اگر وہ (ادا کرنے سے ) رُک گیا تو اس کو ہر ایسے قرضہ میں قید کرے جو ایسے مال کا عوض ہو جو اس کے قبضہ میں حاصل ہوا ہے جیسے مبیع کا ثمن یا عقد سے اس کو لازم کیا ہے جیسے مہر اور کفالہ کا مال۔ اس لئے کہ جب مال اس کے قبضہ میں آیا تو اس مال کے ذریعہ سے اس کا مالدار ہونا ثابت ہو گیا ہے۔ اور اپنے اختیار سے مال کے التزام پر اس کا اقدام کرنا اس کے مالدار ہونے کی دلیل ہے۔ اس لئے کہ وہ نہیں التزام کرے گا مگر اس مال کا جس کے ادا کرنے پر وہ قادر ہے اور مہر معجل مراد ہے نہ کہ مہر مؤجل ۔
تشریح صاحب قدوری نے فرمایا کہ اگر قاضی کے حکم کے بعد قرضدار، قرضہ ادا کرنے سے رک گیا۔ اور قرض خواہ نے اس کو قید کرنے کا مطالبہ کیا تو قاضی اس کو ہر ایسے قرضہ کے بارے میں قید کرے گا جو قرضہ ایسے مال کا عوض ہو جس کو اس نے اپنے قبضہ میں لیا ہے جیسے مبیع کا ثمن یعنی قرضدار پر اگر چہ ثمن کا قرضہ واجب ہوا لیکن مبیع اس کے قبضہ میں آئی ہے۔ یا ایسا قرضہ ہو جو اس نے عقد سے اپنے اوپر لازم کیا ہے جیسے عقد نکاح سے مہر کا مال لازم کیا ہو۔ یا عقد کفالہ سے مال مکفول بہ لازم کیا ہو۔
دلیل یہ ہے کہ جب قرضدار کے قبضہ میں مال آیا تو اُس مال کے ذریعہ اُس کا مالدار ہونا ثابت ہو گیا۔ اور جب مالدار قرضہ ادا کرنے سے رک جاتا ہے تو اس کو قید کر لیا جاتا ہے۔ لہذا اس قرضہ میں مذکورہ قرضدار کو قید کر لیا جائے گا یعنی اس سے مطالبہ کیا جائے گا کہ جو بیع اس کے قبضہ میں ہے اس کو بیچ کر بائع کا ثمن ادا کرے۔ اور اپنے اختیار سے اپنے اوپر مال لازم کرنے کا اقدام کرنا اس کے مالدار ہونے کی دلیل ہے۔ کیونکہ انسان اپنے اوپر ایسے ہی مال کا التزام کرے گا۔ جس کو وہ ادا کر سکتا ہے۔ پس مہر اور کفالہ کا مال جب اس نے اپنے ذمہ لیا ہے تو گویا اس کو ادا کر سکتا ہے۔
صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ متن میں مہر سے مراد مہر معجل ہے ، نہ کہ مہر مؤجل ۔ کیونکہ عادۃ مہر معجل سپرد کیا جاتا ہے نہ کہ مہر مؤجل، پس مہر معجل ادا نہ کرنے کی صورت میں قید ہو گا اور مہر مؤجل ادا نہ کرنے کی صورت میں قید نہ ہوگا۔
Then if he (the debtor) stops (from paying), he (the qadi) should imprison him for every such debt which is a substitute for property that has come into his possession, like the price of a sold item, or which he has made binding upon himself through a contract, like mahr and the wealth of kafalah. Because when the property came into his possession, his being wealthy became established through that property. And his initiating the undertaking of wealth by his own choice is evidence of his being wealthy, because he only undertakes that wealth which he is able to pay. And what is meant by mahr is immediate mahr, not deferred mahr.
Explanation: Sahib al-Quduri said: If after the qadi's order, the debtor stops paying the debt, and the creditor demands his imprisonment, then the qadi will imprison him for every such debt which is a substitute for property that he has taken into his possession, like the price of a sold item—that is, even though the debt of the price became obligatory on the debtor, the sold item has come into his possession. Or such a debt which he made binding upon himself through a contract, like making the wealth of mahr binding through a marriage contract, or making the wealth of the guaranteed thing binding through a kafalah contract.
The proof is that when property came into the debtor's possession, his being wealthy became established through that property. And when a wealthy person stops paying the debt, he is imprisoned. Therefore, in this debt, the mentioned debtor will be imprisoned, meaning he will be demanded to sell the commodity that is in his possession and pay the seller's price. And his initiating the undertaking of wealth by his own choice is evidence of his being wealthy, because a person only undertakes that wealth which he can pay. So when he has taken the wealth of mahr and kafalah upon his liability, it is as if he can pay it.
Sahib al-Hidayah says: In the matn, by mahr is meant immediate mahr, not deferred mahr, because customarily immediate mahr is handed over, not deferred mahr. So in the case of not paying immediate mahr, he will be imprisoned, and in the case of not paying deferred mahr, he will not be imprisoned.
Source pages p. 270

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding when a qadi may imprison a debtor who refuses to pay. It states two categories of debts: (1) debts that are a substitute for property the debtor has received (e.g., the price of a purchased item), and (2) debts that the debtor voluntarily undertook through a contract (e.g., dower in marriage or a guarantee in kafalah). The rationale is that the debtor's receipt of property or voluntary undertaking indicates his ability to pay, so his claim of poverty is not accepted. The passage also clarifies that the dower referred to is the immediate dower (mahr mu'ajjal), not the deferred one, because customarily only the immediate dower is handed over at the time of contract. The commentary by Sahib al-Quduri expands on this, and Sahib al-Hidayah confirms the distinction.

Key Terms
قید (qayd): Imprisonment by the qadi as a means of compelling payment of a debt.
عوض (iwad): A substitute or price given in exchange for property received, like the price of a sold item.
مہر معجل (mahr mu'ajjal): The portion of dower that is paid immediately at the time of marriage, as opposed to deferred dower.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following debts does NOT warrant imprisonment for a debtor who refuses to pay?
A) The price of a sold item that the debtor has received.
B) The immediate dower (mahr mu'ajjal) from a marriage contract.
C) The amount guaranteed in a kafalah contract.
D) A debt arising from a personal loan (qard).

Key Takeaway
A qadi must imprison a debtor who refuses to pay only if the debt is a substitute for property received or voluntarily undertaken through a contract.

The Proof for Imprisonment and the Exception for Deferred Dower
Explaining the proof for imprisonment and the refinement regarding deferred dower

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi rationale (talil) for imprisoning debtors of specific debts and identify why deferred dower is exempted.

Core Idea
The debtor's receipt of property or voluntary undertaking is legal evidence of ability to pay, except for deferred dower due to custom.

This lesson delves into the proof structure (talil) behind the ruling. The passage provides a clear reasoning chain: receipt of property establishes wealth, and voluntary undertaking indicates capacity. Additionally, the commentator refines the ruling by excluding deferred dower based on customary practice. Understanding this logic allows a mufti to apply the ruling to similar cases.

Guided Path
1
Extract the proof (talil)
Identify the two proof statements in the passage: (1) 'When property came into his possession, his wealth became established.' (2) 'His initiating the undertaking of wealth by choice is evidence of his ability to pay.'
These are not explicit Quranic verses or hadith but a reasoning based on observable indicators.
2
Understand the first proof
The first proof applies to debts that are a substitute for property received. Having the property (e.g., the purchased item) in hand is a strong indicator that the debtor is not truly poor.
The qadi does not need to investigate further; the possession itself suffices.
3
Understand the second proof
The second proof applies to voluntarily undertaken debts. A rational person would not commit to pay something he cannot afford; therefore, the act of undertaking itself proves ability.
This is a logical presumption (zahir) that is accepted in Hanafi law.
4
Apply the exception
The passage explicitly excludes deferred dower (mahr mu'ajjal) from imprisonment. The reason is custom ('urf): only immediate dower is customarily handed over at the marriage contract, so non-payment of deferred dower does not indicate inability or refusal to pay.
This shows how custom (urf) can restrict the application of a general proof.

مہر مؤجل (mahr mu'ajjal): Deferred dower, payable at a later date or upon divorce, not immediately at marriage.
عرف (urf): Customary practice that is recognized as a source of law in Hanafi fiqh.

Imprisonment for Other Debts: Burden of Proof and Duration
Intra-Hanafi dispute on burden of proof and duration for imprisoning debtors

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi position on when a qadi may imprison a debtor who claims poverty and distinguish between different narrations within the school.

Core Idea
For debts outside substitute or voluntary categories, the qadi does not imprison a debtor who claims poverty unless the creditor proves wealth.

One of the qadi's tools in debt recovery is imprisonment, but it is not automatic. The Hanafi school distinguishes between debts that are substitutes for property or voluntarily undertaken, and other debts. When a debtor claims poverty, the default rule is that his statement is accepted, but the creditor may rebut it with proof. This lesson examines the burden of proof, the intra-Hanafi differences on whose word is believed, and the duration of imprisonment that the qadi may impose.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of debt
Recall from the previous lesson that for debts that are a substitute for property (e.g., price of goods sold) or voluntarily undertaken (e.g., loan), the qadi may imprison the debtor immediately upon his claim of poverty. This lesson deals with 'other' debts (e.g., tort damages, penalties).
These two categories are not repeated here; the matn starts with 'for other than that'.
2
State the default rule for other debts
The matn says: the qadi does not imprison a debtor who says 'I am poor' for debts outside the two categories, unless the creditor proves the debtor has wealth. The debtor's statement is accepted because the original state is poverty (al-asl al-usr).
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi narrations
Three positions exist: (1) debtor's word accepted in all cases, (2) debtor's word accepted except for debts that are a substitute for property, (3) the matn's distinction. The examples of nafaqah (maintenance) and itaq (freeing a joint slave) support the second view, as these obligations are gifts, not absolute debts.
The matn's position is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) view.
4
Determine the condition for imprisonment
If the creditor proves the debtor's wealth (with bayyinah), the qadi may imprison. The debtor is then seen as evading payment despite ability.
Bayyinah typically means two male witnesses or one male and two females.
5
Examine the duration of imprisonment
Various narrations: two or three months, one month, four to six months. The correct view (sahih) is that the duration is left to the qadi's discretion based on the individual's circumstances, since the purpose is to compel disclosure of hidden wealth.
The qadi should set a reasonable period, then inquire again.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کن امور میں قاضی قید میں نہ ڈالے
قال ولا يحبسه فيما سوى ذلك اذا قال انى فقير الا ان يثبت غريمه ان له مالا فيحبسه لانه لم يوجد دلالة اليسار فيكون القول قول من عليه الدين وعلى المدعى اثبات غناه ويروى ان القول لمن عليه الدين في جميع ذلك لان الاصل هو العسرة ويروى ان القول له الا فيما بدله مال و في النفقة القول قول الزوج انه معسر و فى اعتاق العبد المشترك القول للمعتق والمسألتان تؤيد ان القولين الآخرين والتخريج على ما قال فى الكتاب انه ليس بدين مطلق بل هو صلة حتى تسقط النفقة بالموت على الاتفاق وكذا عند ابي حنيفة ضمان الاعتاق ثم فيما كان القول قول المدعى ان له مالاً او ثبت ذلك بالبينة فيما كان القول قول من عليه يحبسه شهرين او ثلثة ثم يسأل عنه فالحبس لظهور ظلمه في الحال وانما يحبسه مدة ليظهر ماله لو كان يخفيه فلا بد من ان تمتد المدة ليفيد هذه الفائدة فقدر بما ذكره ويروى غير ذلك من التقدير بشهر او اربعة الى ستة اشهر والصحيح ان التقدير مفوض الى رأى القاضى لاختلاف احوال الاشخاص فيه
ترجمہ اور قرضہ مذکورہ کے علاوہ میں قاضی اس کو قید نہ کرے۔ جبکہ اس نے یہ کہا کہ میں فقیر ہوں ۔ مگر یہ کہ اس کا قرض خواہ یہ ثابت کر دے کہ اس کے پاس مال موجود ہے تو قاضی اس کو محبوس کرے گا۔ کیونکہ مالداری کی دلیل نہیں پائی گئی ۔ لہذا جس پر قرضہ ہے اسی کا قول قبول ہوگا۔ اور مدعی پر اس کی مالداری کا ثابت کرنا واجب ہے۔ اور مروی ہے کہ تمام صورتوں میں قرضدار کا قول معتبر ہو گا۔ اس لئے کہ تنگدستی اصل ہے۔ اور یہ بھی روایت کیا جاتا ہے کہ قرضدار کا قول معتبر ہے مگر ایسی صورت میں جس میں اس کا عوض مال ہو۔ اور نفقہ میں شوہر کا یہ قول معتبر ہو گا کہ میں تنگدست ہوں۔ اور مشترک غلام آزاد کرنے کی صورت میں آزاد کرنے والے کا قول قبول ہوگا۔ اور یہ دونوں مسئلہ بعد والے دونوں قولوں کی تائید کرتے ہیں۔ اور تخریج اُس کے مطابق جو کتاب میں کہا یہ ہے کہ وہ قرضہ مطلق نہیں ہے بلکہ وہ ایک صلہ ہے حتی کہ وہ بالاتفاق موت کی وجہ سے ساقط ہو جاتا ہے۔ اور ایسا ہی امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک ضمان اعتاق ہے۔ پھر اُس صورت میں کہ مدعی کا قول معتبر ہو کہ مدعی علیہ کے پاس مال ہے یا قرضدار کا قول قبول ہونے کی صورت میں بینہ کے ذریعہ مال کا ہونا ثابت ہو جائے تو قاضی اس کو دو تین ماہ قید کر کے پھر اس کا حال دریافت کرے گا۔ پس محبوس کرنا فی الحال اس کے ظلم کے ظاہر ہونے کی وجہ سے ہے اور ایک مدت تک اس لئے محبوس کرے گا تا کہ اس کا مال ظاہر ہو جائے اگر وہ اس کو چھپاتا ہو پس مدت کا دراز ہونا ضروری ہے تا کہ یہ فائدہ حاصل ہو۔ اور اس کی مقدار مذکورہ بالا مہینوں کے ساتھ مقدر کی گئی ہے اور اس کے علاوہ مقدار ایک ماہ یا چار ماہ سے چھ ماہ تک مروی ہے اور صحیح یہ ہے کہ مدت کی مقدار قاضی کی رائے کے سپرد کر دی جائے ۔ کیونکہ اس میں لوگوں کے حالات مختلف ہیں۔
تشریح صاحب قدوری نے فرمایا کہ اگر قرضدار پر ایسا قرضہ ہو جو کسی مال کا عوض ہو کر لازم ہوا ہو یا کسی عقد کی وجہ سے اس کا التزام کیا ہو اور پھر قرضدار یہ کہہ کر کہ میں فقیر ہوں قرضہ ادا کرنے سے رُک گیا تو قاضی اس کو قید کرے گا۔ لیکن ان دونوں صورتوں کے علاوہ میں اگر قرضدار نے یہ کہا کہ میں فقیر ہوں تو قاضی اس کو قید نہ کرے گا ۔ ہاں اگر قرض خواہ نے گواہوں سے یہ ثابت کر دیا کہ اس کے پاس مال موجود ہے تو قاضی اس کو قید کرے گا۔ مثلاً ایک شخص نے کسی کا مال تلف یا غصب کر کے ضائع کیا یا اُس پر کوئی تاوان واجب ہوا ۔ پھر اس نے دعوی کیا کہ میں تنگدست ہوں تو اس کا یہ قول قبول کیا جائے گا اور قاضی اس کو قید نہ کرے گا ۔ لیکن اگر قرض خواہ نے کہا کہ ایسا نہیں بلکہ اس کو ادا کرنے کی قدرت حاصل ہے اور اُس نے اس بات کو بینہ کے ذریعہ ثابت کر دیا تو قاضی اس کو قید کرے گا۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ جب تک قرض خواہ کی طرف سے قرضدار کے مالدار اور فراخ حال ہونے کی کوئی دلیل نہ پائی جائے اس وقت تک اُسی کا قول معتبر ہو گا جس پر قرضہ ہے کیونکہ وہ اپنے حال سے زیادہ واقف ہے۔
(صاحب البيت ادرى ما في (البيت) لیکن جب قرض خواہ نے بینہ سے قرضدار کا مالدار ہونا ثابت کر دیا تو مال مدعی علیہ کے ادا کرنے پر قدرت پائی گئی ۔ اور جب قرض دار دین ادا کرنے پر قادر ہے مگر اس کے باوجود ادا نہیں کرتا تو اس کو ٹال مٹول کرنے کی وجہ سے قید کر لیا جائے گا۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا کہ ایک روایت یہ ہے کہ تمام صورتوں میں (خواہ قرضہ کسی مال کا عوض ہو کر لازم ہوا ہو یا عقد سے اس کا التزام کیا ہو خواہ ان کے علاوہ ہو ) قرضدار کا قول معتبر ہو ۔ کیونکہ آدمی کا تنگدست
In which matters the qadi does not imprison.
He (the author) said: And he (the qadi) shall not imprison him for other than that when he (the debtor) says, 'I am poor,' unless his creditor proves that he has wealth, then he shall imprison him. Because there is no indication of wealth, so the statement of the one upon whom the debt is due is taken, and it is upon the plaintiff to prove his wealth. And it is narrated that the statement of the one upon whom the debt is due is accepted in all of that because the original state is hardship. And it is narrated that the statement is accepted except for what is a substitute for property. And in maintenance (nafaqah), the statement of the husband that he is insolvent is accepted. And in freeing a joint slave, the statement of the one freeing is accepted. And these two issues support the latter two sayings. And the derivation according to what is said in the book is that it is not an absolute debt but rather a gift, such that maintenance falls due at death by agreement, and similarly according to Abu Hanifa is the guarantee of freeing. Then, in the case where the statement of the plaintiff is accepted that he (the defendant) has wealth, or that is established by evidence, in the case where the statement of the one upon whom the debt is due is accepted, he (the qadi) shall imprison him for two or three months, then ask about him. So imprisonment is due to the appearance of his oppression at the present moment, and he only imprisons him for a period so that his wealth may appear if he had been hiding it. So the period must be extended to achieve this benefit, and it is determined by what he mentioned. And other than that is narrated of determination by a month or from four to six months. And the correct view is that the determination is delegated to the opinion of the qadi due to the difference in conditions of people in it.

Translation: And other than the mentioned debt, the qadi shall not imprison him when he says, 'I am poor,' unless his creditor proves that he has wealth, then the qadi will imprison him. Because there is no indication of wealth, so the statement of the one upon whom the debt is due is accepted. And it is obligatory upon the plaintiff to prove his wealth. And it is narrated that the debtor's statement is valid in all cases because hardship is the norm. And it is also narrated that the debtor's statement is valid except in a case where it is a substitute for property. And in maintenance, the husband's statement that he is insolvent is valid. And in the case of freeing a joint slave, the statement of the one freeing is accepted. And these two issues support the latter two sayings. And the derivation according to what is said in the book is that it is not an absolute debt but rather a gift, such that it falls due at death by agreement, and similarly according to Abu Hanifa is the guarantee of freeing. Then, in the case where the plaintiff's statement is accepted that the defendant has wealth, or in the case where the debtor's statement is accepted, if wealth is established by evidence, then the qadi shall imprison him for two or three months, then inquire about his condition. So imprisonment at the present moment is due to the appearance of his oppression, and he only imprisons him for a period so that his wealth may appear if he had been hiding it. So the period must be extended to achieve this benefit, and it is determined by what he mentioned. And other than that is narrated of determination by a month or from four to six months. And the correct view is that the determination is delegated to the opinion of the qadi because the conditions of people differ in it.

Explanation: Sahib al-Quduri said: If on the debtor there is a debt that became binding as a substitute for property or he undertook it through a contract, and then the debtor stops paying saying 'I am poor,' then the qadi will imprison him. But apart from these two cases, if the debtor says 'I am poor,' the qadi will not imprison him. Yes, if the creditor proves with witnesses that he has wealth, then the qadi will imprison him. For example, a person destroyed or usurped someone's property and caused loss, or a penalty was due on him, then he claimed that he is insolvent, his statement is accepted and the qadi will not imprison him. But if the creditor says that it is not so but rather he has the ability to pay, and he proves this with evidence, then the qadi will imprison him. The proof is that as long as there is no evidence from the creditor about the debtor being wealthy and well-off, the statement of the one upon whom the debt is due is accepted because he is more aware of his own condition.
(The owner of the house knows best what is in the house) But when the creditor proves the debtor's wealth with evidence, then the ability to pay is found on the part of the defendant. And when the debtor is able to pay but still does not pay, he will be imprisoned due to evasion. Sahib al-Hidayah said: One narration is that in all cases (whether the debt became binding as a substitute for property or through a contract, or otherwise), the debtor's statement is accepted because a person's being insolvent...
Source pages p. 270

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about the conditions for imprisoning a debtor for debts outside the two categories (substitute for property received or voluntarily undertaken). The matn states that for other debts, the qadi does not imprison a debtor who claims poverty unless the creditor proves wealth. The rationale is that the debtor's claim is accepted because the original state is poverty. However, two narrations (riwayat) are mentioned: one that the debtor's word is accepted in all cases, and another that it is accepted except where the debt is a substitute for property. The examples of maintenance (nafaqah) and freeing a joint slave are cited to support the latter view, as in both cases the obligation is not an absolute debt but a gift (silah) that falls due at death. The passage also discusses the duration of imprisonment: some say two or three months, others one month or four to six months, but the correct view (sahih) is that it is left to the qadi's discretion due to differing circumstances. The commentary by Sahib al-Quduri clarifies that for debts outside the two categories, the qadi does not imprison unless the creditor proves wealth, and Sahib al-Hidayah mentions the narration that accepts the debtor's word in all cases.

Key Terms
فقیر (faqir): A person who claims to have no wealth to pay the debt, i.e., insolvent.
بینہ (bayyinah): Clear evidence, typically two witnesses, to prove a claim in court.
نفقہ (nafaqah): Maintenance payable by a husband to his wife, or by a relative to dependents.
عتاق (itaq): The act of freeing a slave; here specifically freeing a jointly owned slave.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the correct view in the passage, how should the qadi determine the duration of imprisonment for a debtor who is proven to have wealth but refuses to pay?
A) Exactly two or three months as prescribed in the matn.
B) Exactly one month as in the narration.
C) A fixed period of four to six months.
D) The duration is left to the qadi's discretion based on the individual's circumstances.

Key Takeaway
For debts outside the two categories, the qadi does not imprison a debtor claiming poverty unless the creditor proves wealth; the duration of imprisonment is left to the qadi's discretion.

Qada — Judiciary
intermediate
10 min
Three Hanafi Views on Imprisoning a Debtor Claiming Poverty
Intra-Hanafi dispute on accepting debtor's claim of poverty, with supporting examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on imprisoning a debtor claiming poverty, identify the thamarah al-khilaf, and evaluate which position is mufta bihi.

Core Idea
A debtor's claim of poverty is accepted by default unless the debt is compensatory—then he may be imprisoned immediately.

This passage from the Book of Adab al-Qadi presents a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute about a common courtroom scenario: a debtor claims he is poor and cannot pay. The judge must decide whether to imprison him or accept his word. The Hanafi scholars offer three distinct positions, each grounded in principles of evidence and the original state of humans. Through this lesson, you will disentangle these views and understand the practical consequences for a judge's ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three positions
Read the passage carefully. Note the three narrations: first (Quduri's matn) distinguishes compensatory debts, second accepts claim in all cases, third accepts claim except for compensatory debts. Write each clearly.
The second narration uses the principle that poverty is the original state (asl).
2
Analyze the supporting examples
The author brings two examples from other chapters: nafaqah (husband's claim of poverty) and manumission of a shared slave (the freeing partner's claim). Understand how these examples seem to support the latter two positions and oppose the first.
These examples are from Kitab al-Nikah and Kitab al-Itaq.
3
Examine the reconciliation (takhrij)
Sahib al-Hidayah offers an interpretation that the examples do not necessarily contradict the first position. Consider how he might harmonize them.
This is a key method in Hanafi fiqh: preserving the relied-upon view by reinterpreting apparently conflicting evidence.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical difference between the three positions in terms of the judge's immediate action. Use a concrete scenario.
Under the first view, a debtor who took a loan is imprisoned immediately; under the second, he is not unless the creditor proves wealth.
5
Identify the mufta bihi
The author of Hidayah indicates which position is relied upon for fatwa. Confirm that the first view (Quduri's) is the most authoritative (zahir al-riwayah).
The other views are recognized but not operative for fatwa.

قاضی اس کو قید کرے گا۔ مثلاً ایک شخص نے کسی کا مال تلف یا غصب کر کے ضائع کیا یا اُس پر کوئی تاوان واجب ہوا ۔ پھر اس نے دعوی کیا کہ میں تنگدست ہوں تو اس کا یہ قول قبول کیا جائے گا اور قاضی اس کو قید نہ کرے گا ۔ لیکن اگر قرض خواہ نے کہا کہ ایسا نہیں بلکہ اس کو ادا کرنے کی قدرت حاصل ہے اور اُس نے اس بات کو بینہ کے ذریعہ ثابت مکر دیا تو قاضی اسکو قید کرے گا۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ جب تک قرض خواہ کی طرف سے قرضدار کے مالدار اور فراخ حال ہونے کی کوئی دلیل نہ پائی جائے اس وقت تک اُسی کا قول معتبر ہو گا جس پر قرضہ ہے کیونکہ وہ اپنے حال سے زیادہ واقف ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا کہ ایک روایت یہ ہے کہ تمام صورتوں میں (خواہ قرضہ کسی مال کا عوض ہو کر لا زم ہوا ہو یا عقد سے اس کا التزام کیا ہو خواہ ان کے علاوہ ہو ) قرضدار کا قول معتبر ہو ۔ کیونکہ آدمی کا تنگدست ہونا اصل ہے۔ اور تنگدست ہونا اصل اس لئے ہے کہ پیدائشی طور پر آدمی کے پاس مال موجود نہیں ہوتا پس قرض دار کا یہ کہنا کہ میں فقیر ہوں اصل کے مطابق ہے اور قرض خواہ کا یہ کہنا کہ اس کے پاس مال موجود ہے خلاف اصل ہے اور چونکہ جس کا قول اصل کے مطابق ہوتا ہے وہ مدعی علیہ کہلاتا ہے اور جس کا قول خلاف اصل ہوتا ہے وہ مدعی کہلا تا ہے ۔اس لئے قرض خواہ مدعی اور قرضدار مدعی علیہ ہو گا ۔ اور مدعی کے پاس ہینہ موجود نہ ہونے کی صورت میں مدعی علیہ کا قول مع الیمین معتبر ہوتا ہے لہذا مدعی علیہ یعنی قرضدار کا قول کہ میں تنگ دست ہوں مع الیمین معتبر ہوگا۔ لیکن اگر مدعی یعنی قرض خواہ نے بینہ کے ذریعہ قرضدار کا مالدار ہونا ثابت کر دیا تو اس صورت میں قرض خواہ کا قول معتبر نہ ہوگا۔ اور ایک روایت یہ ہے کہ اگر قرضدار پر قرضہ کسی مال کا عوض ہو کر لازم ہوا ہو تو اس صورت میں قرض دار کا قول کہ میں تنگدست ہوں قبول نہ ہوگا ۔ لیکن اس کے علاوہ تمام صورتوں میں قبول ہوگا۔ زوجہ کے نفقہ کے سلسلہ میں کتاب النکاح میں مذکور ہے کہ اگر عورت نے اپنے شوہر پر دعوی کیا کہ وہ مالدار ہے اور مجھے کو مالداروں کا سا نفقہ ملنا چاہیئے ۔ اور شوہر نے دعویٰ کیا کہ میں تنگدست ہوں ۔ لہذا مجھ پر تنگدستوں کا سا نفقہ واجب ہونا چاہیئے ۔ تو شوہر کا قول چونکہ اصل کے موافق ہے اس لئے اُس کا قول معتبر ہوگا۔ لیکن اگر عورت نے ہینہ کے ذریعہ اپنے شوہر کا مالدار ہونا ثابت کر دیا تو شوہر کا قول معتبر نہ ہو گا۔ اور کتاب العتاق میں مذکور ہے کہ اگر ایک غلام دو آدمیوں کے درمیان مشترک ہو اور ان میں سے ایک نے اپنے حصہ کو آزاد کر کے اپنے تنگدست ہونے کا دعویٰ کر دیا ہوتا کہ اپنے شریک کے لئے آدھے غلام کی قیمت کا ضامن نہ ہونا پڑے اور دوسرے شریک نے دعوی کیا کہ یہ مالدار ہے لہذا میرے حصہ کا تاوان ادا کرے تو جس شریک نے اپنا حصہ آزاد کیا ہے تنگدست ہونے کے سلسلہ میں اسی کا قول معتبر ہوگا۔ کیونکہ اس کا قول اصل کے موافق ہے۔ لیکن اگر شریک آمر نے ہینہ کے ذریعہ اس کا مالدار ہونا ثابت کر دیا تو اس صورت میں اس کا قول معتبر ہوگا اور معتیق پر تاوان واجب کیا جائے گا۔ صاحب ہدایہ فر ماتے ہیں کہ یہ دونوں مسئلہ ( یعنی مسئلہ نفقہ اور عبد مشترک کے اعتباق کا مسئلہ ) اخیر کے دونوں اقوال کی تائید کرتے ہیں۔ اور قول اول جو متن میں مذکور ہے اس کے مخالف ہیں۔ یہ دونوں مسئلے قول اول کے مخالف اس لئے ہیں کہ قولِ اوّل میں کہا گیا ہے کہ اگر قرضدار پر ایسا قرضہ لازم ہوا ہو جس کے عوض اس کو مال ملا ہو یا اس نے عقد سے اپنے اوپر مال لازم کیا ہو تو ان دونوں صورتوں میں اگر قرضدار نے اپنے تنگدست ہونے کا دعویٰ کیا تو تنگدست ہونے کے سلسلہ میں قرضداروں کا قول معتبر نہ ہو گا بلکہ قرض خواہ کا قول کہ وہ مالدار ہے معتبر ہو گا۔ حالانکہ مذکورہ دو مسئلوں میں سے پہلے مسئلہ میں شوہر نے عقد نکاح کے ذریعہ اپنے اوپر نفقہ لازم کیا ہے اور دوسرے مسئلہ میں احد الشریکین نے اپنا حصہ آزاد کرنے پر اقدام کیا ہے مگر اس کے باوجود تنگدستی کے سلسلہ میں شوہر کا قول اور آزافذ کرنے والے شریک کا قول معتبر ہے۔ اگر یہ دونوں مسئلے قول اول کے موافق ہوتے تو مالداری کے دعوئی میں عورت اور شریک سا کرنے کا قول معتبر ہوتا۔ پس ثابت ہو گیا کہ یہ دونوں مسئلے قول اول کے مخالف ہیں۔ اور جب قول اول کے مخالف ہیں تو قدرتی طور پر اخیر کے دونوں اقوال کے موافق ہوں گے۔ والتخريج على ما قال في الكتاب سے صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ دونوں مسئلوں کی تاویل ایسے انداز میں فرمارہے ہیں جس سے قول اول پر کوئی نقض وارد نہ ہو۔
Book of Adab al-Qadi. And except for the mentioned debt and loan, the judge shall not imprison him when he says 'I am poor,' unless the creditor proves that he has wealth, then the judge will imprison him. Because no evidence of wealth is found. Therefore, the statement of the debtor is accepted. And it is obligatory for the claimant to prove his wealth. And it is narrated that in all cases the debtor's statement is accepted, because poverty is the original state. And it is also narrated that the debtor's statement is accepted except in the case where there is a compensation for property. And in nafaqah, the husband's statement that he is insolvent is accepted. And in the case of freeing a shared slave, the statement of the one who frees is accepted. And these two cases support the latter two statements. Explanation: Sahib al-Quduri said: If the debtor has a debt that is due as compensation for property or obligated through a contract, and then the debtor stops paying saying 'I am poor,' the judge will imprison him. But in other than these two cases, if the debtor says 'I am poor,' the judge will not imprison him. Yes, if the creditor proves through witnesses that he has wealth, the judge will imprison him. For example, a person destroys or usurps someone's property or owes some penalty, then claims to be insolvent – his statement is accepted and the judge will not imprison him. But if the creditor says it is not so but that he has ability to pay, and proves it through evidence, then the judge will imprison him. The proof is that as long as no evidence from the creditor proves the debtor's wealth and ease, the statement of the debtor is accepted because he knows his own condition better. Sahib al-Hidayah said: One narration is that in all cases (whether the debt is due as compensation for property or obligated through a contract, or otherwise), the debtor's statement is accepted. Because a person's insolvency is the original state. And insolvency is the original state because a person is not born with wealth; thus the debtor's saying 'I am poor' conforms to the original, and the creditor's saying that he has wealth is contrary to the original. And since the one whose statement conforms to the original is called the defendant, and the one whose statement is contrary to the original is called the claimant, the creditor is the claimant and the debtor is the defendant. And when the claimant has no evidence, the defendant's statement with an oath is accepted. Thus the defendant's (debtor's) statement that he is insolvent with an oath is accepted. But if the claimant (creditor) proves the debtor's wealth through evidence, then the creditor's statement is not accepted. And another narration is that if the debt is due as compensation for property, then the debtor's statement that he is insolvent is not accepted, but in other cases it is accepted. In the matter of wife's nafaqah, it is mentioned in Kitab al-Nikah that if the wife claims her husband is wealthy and she should get the nafaqah of the wealthy, and the husband claims he is insolvent, so the nafaqah of the insolvent should be due, then the husband's statement is accepted because it conforms to the original. But if the wife proves her husband's wealth through evidence, then the husband's statement is not accepted. And in Kitab al-Itaq, it is mentioned that if a slave is shared between two men, and one of them frees his share and claims to be insolvent so that he should not be liable for the value of half the slave to his partner, and the other partner claims he is wealthy so he should pay compensation for his share, then the statement of the partner who freed his share regarding insolvency is accepted because it conforms to the original. But if the other partner proves his wealth through evidence, then his statement is accepted and compensation is imposed on the manumitter. Sahib al-Hidayah says: These two cases (i.e., the case of nafaqah and the case of the shared slave's manumission) support the latter two statements and oppose the first statement mentioned in the text. These two cases oppose the first statement because in the first statement it is said that if the debt is due as compensation for property or obligated through contract, then in these two cases if the debtor claims insolvency, his statement is not accepted but the creditor's statement that he is wealthy is accepted. Whereas in the two mentioned cases, in the first case the husband obligated nafaqah through the marriage contract, and in the second case one partner undertook to free his share, yet despite that, the husband's statement and the manumitter's statement regarding insolvency are accepted. If these two cases conformed to the first statement, then in the claim of wealth, the wife and the other partner's statement would be accepted. So it is established that these two cases oppose the first statement. And since they oppose the first statement, naturally they conform to the latter two statements. And the interpretation according to what is said in the book, Sahib al-Hidayah interprets these two cases in a way that does not constitute a contradiction to the first statement.
Source pages p. 271

Commentary
This passage from the Book of Adab al-Qadi deals with the intricate ruling on imprisoning a debtor who claims to be insolvent. The author first presents the view of al-Quduri (the matn author) which distinguishes between two types of debts: (1) a debt that arose as compensation for property (i.e., the debtor received something in return, like sale price or dower) or (2) a debt undertaken through a contract (like a loan or guarantee). In such cases, if the debtor claims poverty, the judge will imprison him immediately. For other debts (e.g., torts like destruction of property), the debtor's claim of poverty is accepted, and he is not imprisoned unless the creditor proves he has concealed wealth. The reasoning is that the debtor is better informed of his own state, and the burden of proof lies on the claimant. Then the author presents three narrations within the Hanafi school. The first is the one just mentioned. The second, attributed to a narration, says that in all cases the debtor's claim of poverty is accepted because poverty is the original state of humans (they are born without wealth). The third, another narration, says the debtor's claim is accepted except when the debt is a compensation for property. These differences lead to an intra-Hanafi dispute. The author then brings two supporting examples from other chapters: (1) from Kitab al-Nikah, regarding the husband's claim of poverty in nafaqah disputes, and (2) from Kitab al-Itaq, regarding the freeing partner's claim of poverty in shared slave manumission. Both examples show that the claim of poverty is preferred as it conforms to the original state (asl). The author of Hidayah (likely al-Marghinani) notes that these two examples support the latter two statements and oppose the first statement of Quduri. However, he also offers an interpretation (takhrij) that these examples can be harmonized with the first statement, thereby preserving its validity.

Key Terms
قرضدار (qarzdār): Debtor – the person who owes a debt (qarḍ) or any financial obligation.
قرض خواہ (qarẓ khwāh): Creditor – the person to whom the debt is owed, also called mudda‘ī (claimant) in this context.
تنگدست (tangdast): Insolvent, financially unable to pay the debt.
بینہ (bayyinah): Evidence, usually two male witnesses or one male and two females, used to prove wealth in court.
اصل (aṣl): Original state; the default presumption in legal reasoning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the first statement (Quduri's view) in this passage, in which case will the judge imprison a debtor who claims poverty?
A) When the debt is from a tort (like destruction of property).
B) When the debt is compensation for property or undertaken through a contract.
C) In all cases, immediately upon the debtor's claim.
D) Only if the creditor provides two male witnesses proving the debtor's wealth.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has three positions on debtor's claim of poverty; the mufta bihi is Quduri's view: claim accepted except for compensatory debts.
