Qada — Judiciary
intermediate
12 min
Acceptance of Debtor's Claim of Poverty and Detention Procedure
Explains who is claimant/defendant in debt disputes and judge's detention of debtor

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for accepting a debtor's claim of poverty based on the principle of asl, identify the claimant and defendant in debt disputes, and explain the judge's detention procedure including the discretion on duration.

Core Idea
Debtor's claim of poverty is accepted with oath because poverty is the original state; judge detains if evasion is suspected, with duration at discretion.

This passage from al-Hidayah establishes a foundational rule: a person's default state is poverty. The creditor is the claimant because his claim of wealth contradicts the original state. The debtor's statement is accepted with an oath unless the creditor brings evidence. An exception exists for absolute debts, which Sahib al-Hidayah reconciles. The passage also details the judge's procedure for detaining a debtor suspected of hiding wealth, emphasising judicial discretion over fixed periods.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claimant and defendant based on asl
Apply the principle that the original state (asl) of a person is poverty. The one whose statement aligns with asl is the defendant (mudda'a alayh); the one whose statement is contrary is the claimant (mudda'i). Determine who is who in a debt dispute.
The debtor says 'I am poor' (aligns with asl) → defendant. Creditor says 'he is wealthy' (contrary to asl) → claimant.
2
State the default ruling for accepting the debtor's claim
The defendant's statement is accepted with an oath if the claimant has no evidence. Thus, the debtor's claim of poverty is accepted with an oath unless the creditor brings bayyinah (evidence) to prove wealth.
This is the default; the burden of proof is on the claimant.
3
Analyze the exception for absolute debts
One narration says that if the debt is a consideration for property or undertaken by contract, the debtor's claim of poverty is not accepted. Sahib al-Hidayah resolves this by limiting the exception to 'dayn mutlaq' (absolute debt) – a debt that is only discharged by payment or release.
Examples: maintenance (nafaqah) and compensation for emancipation (daman al-itq) are not dayn mutlaq; they are like gifts or non-absolute obligations.
4
Examine the supporting examples from nafaqah and itq
In maintenance and joint slave emancipation cases, the debtor's claim of poverty is accepted despite the debt arising from a contract. This seems to contradict the exception, but Sahib al-Hidayah explains that these are not absolute debts.
Thus, the exception does not apply in those cases; the default rule holds.
5
Understand the detention procedure and duration
If the debtor is suspected of hiding wealth (either the creditor's claim is accepted or the debtor's claim is accepted but evidence of wealth appears), the judge detains him for two to three months, then investigates. The correct view is that duration is at the judge's discretion based on the individual's temperament and circumstances.
Different narrations suggest 1 month (Tahawi) or 4-6 months (Hasan ibn Ziyad), but discretion is preferred. Release if no wealth appears after the period.

طور پر اخیر کے دونوں اقوال کے موافق ہوں گے۔ والتخريج على ما قال في الكتاب سے صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ دونوں مسئلوں کی تاویل ایسے انداز میں فرمارہے ہیں جس سے قول اول پر کوئی نقض وارد نہ ہو۔ اور یہ دونوں مسئلہ قول اول کے مخالف نہ رہیں ۔ چنانچہ فرمایا کہ قدوری کی عبارت حبسه فی کل دین لزمه بدلاً عن مال او التزمه بعقد میں دین سے دین مطلق مراد ہے۔ اور دین مطلق ہی کو دین صحیح کہتے ہیں ۔ دین مطلق اور دین صحیح اس کو کہتے ہیں کہ جو یا تو ادا کرنے سے ساقط ہو اور یا صاحب حق کے بری کرنے سے ساقط ہو بہر حال قدوری کی عبارت میں دین سے دین مطلق مراد ہے۔ اور مذکورہ دونوں مسئلوں میں یعنی نفقہ کے مسئلہ میں نفقہ دین مطلق نہیں ہے۔ بلکہ شوہر کی طرف سے ایک صلہ ہے یہی وجہ ہے کہ شوہر کی موت سے بالاتفاق نفقہ ساقط ہو جاتا ہے۔ اور اسی طرح دوسرے مسئلہ میں غلام مشترک آزاد کرنے کا تاوان حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک دین مطلق نہیں ہے۔ پس جب قول اول یعنی قدوری کی عبارت میں دین سے دین مطلق مراد ہے اور ان دونوں مسئلوں میں نفقہ اور ضمان اعتقاق دین مطلق نہیں ہے تو یہ دونوں مسئلہ قول اول کے موافق کیسے ہو سکتے ہیں۔ اور ان دونوں مسئلوں سے قول اول پر کس طرح نقض وارد کیا جا سکتا ہے۔
صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ جس صورت میں قرض خواہ کا قول کہ قرضدار مالدار ہے معتبر ہو ۔ یا جس صورت میں قرضدار کا قول کہ میں تنگدست ہوں معتبر ہو لیکن قرض خواہ، بینہ کے ذریعہ ثابت کر دے کہ اس کے پاس مال موجود ہے تو ان دونوں صورتوں میں قاضی، قرضدار کو دو یا تین ماہ کے لئے قید کرے گا۔ پھر اس کے پڑوس کے لوگوں اور اس کے متعلقین سے اس کی تنگدستی اور مالداری کے بارے میں دریافت کرے گا کہ یہ قرضدار تنگدست ہے یا مالدار ہے؟ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ قرضدار کو قید تو اس لئے کیا جائے گا کہ ٹال مٹول کرنے کی وجہ سے فی الحال اس کا ظالم ہونا ظاہر ہو گیا ہے۔ اور ظلم کی سزا چونکہ قید ہے اس لئے اس کو قید کیا جائے گا۔ اور وہ تین ماہ کی مدت اس لئے قید میں رکھا جائے گا تا کہ اس کا کچھ مال ہو جس کو وہ چھپاتا ہے ظاہر ہو جائے ۔ پس اس مقصد کے پیش نظر قید کی مدت کا دراز ہونا ضروری ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہے کہ دو یا تین ماہ کی مدت کے علاوہ اور بھی مدتیں مردی ہیں۔ چنانچہ حضرت امام طحاوی نے ایک ماہ مقرر کی ہے اور حسن بن زیاد نے حضرت امام ابوحنیفہ سے چار ماہ سے چھ ماہ کی مدت روایت کی ہے۔ مگر صحیح قول یہ ہے کہ مدت کی تقدیر کا مسئلہ قاضی کی رائے کے سپرد کیا جائے ۔ قاضی صاحب جس قدر مناسب سمجھیں اس کو قید کریں۔ کیونکہ اس بارے میں لوگوں کے حالات مختلف ہوتے ہیں۔ بعض شریف لوگ قید کی سختی اور رسوائی سے گھبرا کر جلد ہی معاملہ کوختم کرنے کی کوشش کرتے ہیں۔ اور بعض لوگ ایسے ناہنجار قسم کے ہوتے ہیں کہ ان کے یہاں شرم و غیرت کا کوئی مسئلہ ہی نہیں ہوتا۔ چنانچہ وہ مدتوں قید میں رہنے کے باوجود بھی اپنے پاس مال ہونے کا اقرار نہیں کرتے۔ پس قاضی چونکہ لوگوں کا مزاج شناس بھی ہوتا ہے۔اس لئے مدت قید کا معاملہ قاضی ہی کی رائے کے سپرد کر دیا جائے گا۔
محبوس کا مال معلوم نہ ہو سکے تو قید خانہ سے نکال دے
فان لم يظهر له مال خلی سبیله یعنی بعد مضي المدة لأنه استحق النظرة الى الميسرة فيكون حبسه بعد ذالك ظلماً ولو قامت البيئة على افلاسه قبل المدة تقبل فى رواية وفى رواية لا تقبل وعلى الثانية عامة المشائخ قال في الكتاب على سبيله ولا يحول بينه و بين غرمائه وهذا كلام في الملازمة و سنذكره في كتاب الحجر ان شاء الله تعالى و فى الجامع الصغير رجل اقر عند القاضى بدين فانه يحبسه ثم يسأل عنه فان كان موسرًا ابد حبسه وان كان معسرًا خلى سبيله ومراده اذا اقر عند غير القاضي او عنده مرة فظهرت مما طلته والحبس اولاً ومدته قد بيناه فلا نعيده
It is the original state. And being destitute is the original state because by birth a person does not possess wealth. So the debtor's saying 'I am poor' is in accordance with the original state, and the creditor's saying 'he possesses wealth' is contrary to the original state. And since the one whose statement aligns with the original state is called the defendant, and the one whose statement is contrary to the original state is called the claimant, therefore the creditor is the claimant and the debtor is the defendant. And when the claimant has no evidence, the statement of the defendant with an oath is accepted. Hence the statement of the defendant, i.e., the debtor, 'I am destitute' with an oath will be accepted. But if the claimant, i.e., the creditor, proves through evidence that the debtor is wealthy, then the creditor's statement will be accepted. And there is one narration that if the debt has become obligatory upon the debtor as a consideration for some property, then in that case the debtor's statement that he is destitute will not be accepted. But in all other cases it will be accepted. Regarding the wife's maintenance in the Book of Marriage, it is mentioned that if a woman claims against her husband that he is wealthy and she should receive the maintenance of the wealthy, and the husband claims that he is destitute, so the maintenance of the destitute should be obligatory upon him, then the husband's statement will be accepted because it aligns with the original state. But if the woman proves through evidence that her husband is wealthy, then the husband's statement will not be accepted. And in the Book of Emancipation, it is mentioned that if a slave is jointly owned by two men, and one of them frees his share and claims to be destitute so that he should not become guarantor for half the slave's value to his partner, and the other partner claims that he is wealthy so he should pay compensation for his share, then regarding being destitute, the statement of the partner who freed his share will be accepted because his statement aligns with the original state. But if the other partner proves through evidence that he is wealthy, then in that case his statement will be accepted and compensation will be imposed upon the manumitter. Sahib al-Hidayah says that both these issues (i.e., the issue of maintenance and the issue of the jointly-owned slave's emancipation) support the later two statements and are opposed to the first statement mentioned in the text. These two issues are opposed to the first statement because in the first statement it is said that if a debt becomes obligatory upon the debtor in exchange for property or he undertakes it by contract, then in both these cases if the debtor claims to be destitute, his statement regarding destitution will not be accepted; rather the creditor's statement that he is wealthy will be accepted. Whereas in the first of the two mentioned issues, the husband has obligated maintenance upon himself through the marriage contract, and in the second issue, one of the partners initiated freeing his share, yet despite that, regarding destitution, the husband's statement and the statement of the partner who freed are accepted. If these two issues were in accordance with the first statement, then in the claim of wealthiness, the statement of the woman and the other partner would be accepted. So it is established that these two issues are opposed to the first statement. And since they are opposed to the first statement, naturally they will be in accordance with the later two statements. By saying 'and the derivation according to what is said in the book', Sahib al-Hidayah interprets these two issues in such a manner that no objection (naqd) occurs against the first statement. And these two issues will not remain opposed to the first statement. Thus he says that in Quduri's phrase 'his imprisonment for every debt incurred as a substitute for property or undertaken by contract', the word 'debt' means absolute debt (dayn mutlaq). And absolute debt is called valid debt (dayn sahih). Absolute and valid debt is that which is discharged either by payment or by the creditor's release. In any case, Quduri's phrase means absolute debt. And in the two mentioned issues, the maintenance in the maintenance issue is not an absolute debt; rather it is a gift (silah) from the husband, which is why the maintenance is unanimously cancelled upon the husband's death. Similarly, in the second issue, the compensation for freeing a jointly-owned slave, according to Imam Abu Hanifa, is not an absolute debt. So when in the first statement, i.e., Quduri's phrase, 'debt' means absolute debt, and in these two issues, maintenance and compensation for emancipation are not absolute debts, how can these two issues be in accordance with the first statement? And how can an objection be raised against the first statement based on these two issues?
Sahib al-Hidayah says: In the case where the creditor's statement that the debtor is wealthy is accepted, or in the case where the debtor's statement that he is destitute is accepted but the creditor proves through evidence that he possesses wealth, in both these cases the judge will imprison the debtor for two or three months. Then he will inquire from the neighbors and relatives about his destitution and wealth: is this debtor destitute or wealthy? Sahib al-Hidayah says: The debtor will be imprisoned because due to evasion, his being a wrongdoer has become evident. And since the punishment for wrongdoing is imprisonment, he will be imprisoned. And he will be kept imprisoned for three months so that any wealth he is hiding may become apparent. Therefore, for this purpose, the length of imprisonment is necessary. Sahib al-Hidayah says: Besides the period of two or three months, there are other periods mentioned. Thus Imam Tahawi specified one month, and Hasan ibn Ziyad narrated from Imam Abu Hanifa a period of four to six months. But the correct view is that the determination of the period is left to the judge's discretion. The judge may imprison him for as long as he deems appropriate. Because people's conditions differ in this regard. Some noble people, fearing the severity and disgrace of imprisonment, try to conclude the matter quickly. And some people are so shameless that they have no sense of shame or honor. Thus, despite being imprisoned for long periods, they do not admit to possessing wealth. Since the judge is also knowledgeable about people's temperaments, the matter of the imprisonment period is left to his discretion.
If the wealth of the imprisoned person cannot be known, release him from prison. 'If no wealth appears for him, let him go', i.e., after the period has passed, because he is entitled to respite until ease, so imprisoning him after that is oppression. And if evidence of his insolvency is produced before the period, in one narration it is accepted, and in another narration it is not accepted. And the second narration is followed by the majority of scholars. He said in the book: 'Let him go his way, and do not place a barrier between him and his creditors.' This is a discussion about confinement, and we will mention it in the Book of Guardianship, Allah willing. And in al-Jami' al-Saghir: 'A man confessed a debt before the judge, so he imprisoned him, then inquired about him. If he was wealthy, he continued his imprisonment; if he was destitute, he let him go.' And his meaning is when he confessed before someone other than the judge, or before him once, then it became apparent from the debt claim. And the imprisonment first and its period we have explained, so we do not repeat it.
Source pages p. 272

Commentary
This passage is an expansion (sharh) by Sahib al-Hidayah on the ruling regarding the debtor's claim of poverty and the judge's procedure. It begins by establishing the legal principle that the debtor's statement of being destitute is aligned with the original state (asl) because humans are born without wealth. Thus, the debtor is the defendant (mudda'a alayh) and the creditor is the claimant (mudda'i). The defendant's statement is accepted with an oath unless the claimant brings evidence. An exception is noted in one narration: if the debt is a consideration for property or undertaken by contract, the debtor's claim of poverty is not accepted. However, this is nuanced by Sahib al-Hidayah through examples from maintenance (nafaqah) and joint slave emancipation (itq). In those cases, the husband's claim of poverty is accepted despite the marriage contract, and the emancipating partner's claim is accepted despite his action. These examples seem to contradict the exception. Sahib al-Hidayah resolves this by interpreting that the exception applies only to 'absolute debt' (dayn mutlaq), which is discharged by payment or release. Maintenance and compensation for emancipation are not absolute debts; maintenance is a gift (silah) that ends upon death, and compensation (daman) in emancipation is not a debt according to Imam Abu Hanifa. Thus, these examples do not conflict with the exception. The passage then discusses the detention (habs) of a debtor who claims poverty but is suspected of hiding wealth. The judge detains him for two to three months, then investigates. If evidence of poverty comes before the period ends, there are two narrations: one accepts it, the other does not; the majority follow the second. The correct view is that the detention period is at the judge's discretion based on the individual's situation. If no wealth appears after the period, the debtor is released. Finally, a reference from al-Jami' al-Saghir is given about confession of debt leading to imprisonment and release based on means.

Key Terms
مدعی (mudda'i): The claimant, the one whose statement is contrary to the original state (asl). In this context, the creditor is the mudda'i because he claims the debtor has wealth contrary to the natural state of poverty.
مدعی علیہ (mudda'a alayh): The defendant, the one whose statement aligns with the original state. Here, the debtor is the mudda'a alayh because his claim of poverty aligns with the natural state.
دین مطلق (dayn mutlaq): Absolute debt, a debt that is discharged only by payment or by the creditor's release. It is not extinguished by death or other causes. In this text, it is contrasted with nafaqah (maintenance) and daman al-itq (compensation for emancipation) which are not absolute debts.
اصل (asl): The original state or default presumption. Here, the asl is that a person is born without wealth, so poverty is the original state. This is used to determine who is claimant vs. defendant.
بینہ (bayyinah): Evidence, typically two male witnesses or one male and two female witnesses. In this context, the creditor can bring bayyinah to prove the debtor is wealthy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, in a dispute between a creditor and a debtor over whether the debtor is wealthy or destitute, who is considered the claimant (mudda'i) and why?
A) The debtor, because he claims poverty which is contrary to the original state.
B) The creditor, because he claims wealth which is contrary to the original state of poverty.
C) The judge, because he must determine the truth.
D) Both are claimants equally.

Key Takeaway
The debtor's claim of poverty is accepted with an oath because it aligns with the original state; an exception for absolute debts is reconciled by Sahib al-Hidayah, and the judge detains the debtor at his discretion if evasion is suspected.

Qada — Judiciary
intermediate
8 min
Imprisonment of the Debtor and the Evidentiary Rule of Solvency
Commentary on Hidayah's rules for imprisoning a debtor and the dispute over whose qawl is accepted.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for accepting the debtor's claim of poverty, explain the exception for debts in exchange for property, and apply the imprisonment procedure as per the Hidayah.

Core Idea
Poverty is the original state; the debtor's claim is accepted unless the debt is in exchange for property.

This lesson examines the procedure a judge follows when a debtor claims poverty but the creditor claims wealth. The central legal principle is 'asl al-iflas' – the original state of a person is poverty. The Hanafi school applies this principle to determine who bears the burden of proof, but an important exception exists for debts incurred in exchange for property. The passage also details the imprisonment period and the judge's discretion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
The core dispute is whose statement the judge accepts regarding the debtor's financial status: the debtor's claim of poverty or the creditor's claim of wealth.
2
Understand the principle of asl al-iflas
Recognize that poverty (iflas) is the default state of a person, as one is born without property. The debtor's statement conforms to this original state.
This makes the debtor the mudda'a alayh (defendant).
3
Distinguish absolute debt (dayn mutlaq)
The rule applies only to absolute debts that are discharged by payment or release. Nafaqah and compensation for freeing a jointly owned slave are not absolute debts.
This distinction is crucial for reconciling the two case studies.
4
Analyze the exception for debts in exchange for property
If the debt was incurred in exchange for property (e.g., a sale), the presumption of poverty is overcome because the debtor received value. In such cases, the creditor's claim of wealth is accepted.
This is the qawl al-awwal (first opinion) that is limited by later opinions.
5
Evaluate the thaamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical consequences: in nafaqah and itq cases, the debtor's claim of poverty is accepted, so the burden is on the claimant to prove wealth.
This is the mufta bihi position supported by the commentator.

كتاب الادب القاضي
كل دين لازمه بدلاً عن مال او التزمه بعقد میں دین سے دین مطلق مراد ہے۔ اور دین مطلق ہی کو دین صحیح کہتے ہیں ۔ دین مطلق اور دین صحیح اس کو کہتے ہیں کہ جو یا تو ادا کرنے سے ساقط ہو اور یا صاحب حق کے بری کرنے سے ساقط ہو بہر حال قدوری کی عبارت میں دین سے دین مطلق مراد ہے۔ اور مذکورہ دونوں مسلوں میں یعنی نفقہ کے مسئلہ میں نفقہ دین مطلق نہیں ہے۔ بلکہ شوہر کی طرف سے ایک صلہ ہے یہی وجہ ہے کہ شوہر کی موت سے بالا تفاق نفقہ ساقط ہو جاتا ہے۔ اور اسی طرح دوسرے مسئلہ میں غلام مشترک آزاد کرنے کا تاوان حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک دین مطلق نہیں ہے۔ پس جب قول اول یعنی قدوری کی عبارت میں دین سے دین مطلق مراد ہے اور ان دونوں مسئلوں میں نفقہ اور ضمان اعتقاق دین مطلق نہیں ہے تو یہ دونوں مسئلہ قول اول کے موافق کیسے ہو سکتے ہیں۔ اور ان دونوں مسئلوں سے قول اول پر کس طرح نقض وارد کیا جا سکتا ہے۔
صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ جس صورت میں قرض خواہ کا قول کہ قرضدار مالدار ہے معتبر ہو ۔ یا جس صورت میں قرضدار کا قول کہ میں تنگدست ہوں معتبر ہو لیکن قرض خواہ، بینہ کے ذریعہ ثابت کر دے کہ اس کے پاس مال موجود ہے تو ان دونوں صورتوں میں قاضی، قرضدار کو دو یا تین ماہ کے لئے قید کرے گا۔ پھر اس کے پڑوس کے لوگوں اور اس کے متعلقین سے اس کی تنگدستی اور مالداری کے بارے میں دریافت کرے گا کہ یہ قرضدار تنگدست ہے یا مالدار ہے؟ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ قرضدار کو قید تو اس لئے کیا جائے گا کہ ٹال مٹول کرنے کی وجہ سے فی الحال اس کا ظالم ہونا ظاہر ہو گیا ہے۔ اور ظلم کی سزا چونکہ قید ہے اس لئے اس کو قید کیا جائے گا۔ اور وہ تین ماہ کی مدت اس لئے قید میں رکھا جائے گا تا کہ اس کا کچھ مال ہو جس کو وہ چھپاتا ہے ظاہر ہو جائے ۔ پس اس مقصد کے پیش نظر قید کی مدت کا دراز ہونا ضروری ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہے کہ دو یا تین ماہ کی مدت کے علاوہ اور بھی مدتیں مردی ہیں۔ چنانچہ حضرت امام طحاوی نے ایک ماہ ، ت مقرر کی ہے اور حسن بن زیاد نے حضرت امام ابوحنیفہ سے چار ماہ سے چھ ماہ کی مدت روایت کی ہے۔ مگر صحیح قول یہ ہے کہ مدت کی تقدیر کا مسئلہ قاضی کی رائے کے سپرد کیا جائے ۔ قاضی صاحب جس قدر مناسب سمجھیں اس کو قید کریں۔ کیونکہ اس بارے میں لوگوں کے حالات مختلف ہوتے ہیں۔ بعض شریف لوگ قید کی سختی اور رسوائی سے گھبرا کر جلد ہی معاملہ کوختم کرنے کی کوشش کرتے ہیں۔ اور بعض لوگ ایسے ناہنجار قسم کے ہوتے ہیں کہ ان کے یہاں شرم و غیرت کا کوئی مسئلہ ہی نہیں ہوتا۔ چنانچہ وہ مدتوں قید میں رہنے کے باوجود بھی اپنے پاس مال ہونے کا اقرار نہیں کرتے۔ پس قاضی چونکہ لوگوں کا مزاج شناس بھی ہوتا ہے۔اس لئے مدت قید کا معاملہ قاضی ہی کی رائے کے سپر د کر دیا جائے گا۔
محبوس کا مال معلوم نہ ہو سکے تو قید خانہ سے نکال دے
فان لم يظهر له مال خلی سبیله یعنى بعد مضي المدة لأنه استحق النظرة الى الميسرة فيكون حبسه بعد ذالك ظلماً ولو قامت البيئة على افلاسه قبل المدة تقبل فى رواية وفى رواية لا تقبل وعلى الثانية عامة المشائخ قال في الكتاب على سبيله ولا يحول بينه و بين غرمائه وهذا كلام في الملازمة و سنذكره في کتاب الحجر ان شاء الله تعالى و فى الجامع الصغير رجل اقر عند القاضى بدين فانه يحبسه ثم يسأل عنه فان كان موسرًا ابد حبسه وان كان معسرًا خلى سبيله ومراده اذا اقر عند غير القاضي او عنده مرة فظهرت مما طلته والحبس اولاً ومدته قد بيناه فلا نعيده

اشرف الهدایہ جلد نم
كتاب الادب القاضي
ہونا اصل ہے۔ اور تنگدست ہونا اصل اس لئے ہے کہ پیدائشی طور پر آدمی کے پاس مال موجود نہیں ہوتا پس قرض دار کا یہ کہنا کہ میں فقیر ہوں اصل کے مطابق ہے اور قرض خواہ کا یہ کہنا کہ اس کے پاس مال موجود ہے خلاف اصل ہے اور چونکہ جس کا قول اصل کے مطابق ہوتا ہے وہ مدعی علیہ کہلاتا ہے اور جس کا قول خلاف اصل ہوتا ہے وہ مدعی کہلاتا ہے۔ اس لئے قرض خواہ مدعی اور قرضدار مدعی علیہ ہو گا ۔ اور مدعی کے پاس ہینہ موجود نہ ہونے کی صورت میں مدعی علیہ کا قول مع الیمین معتبر ہوتا ہے لہذا مدعی علیہ یعنی قرضدار کا قول کہ میں تنگ دست ہوں مع الیمین معتبر ہوگا۔ لیکن اگر مدعی یعنی قرض خواہ نے بینہ کے ذریعہ قرضدار کا مالدار ہونا ثابت کر دیا تو اس صورت میں قرض خواہ کا قول معتبر نہ ہوگا۔ اور ایک روایت یہ ہے کہ اگر قرضدار پر قرضہ کسی مال کا ہو کر کا نہ ہوگا عوض ہو کر لازم ہوا ہو تو اس صورت میں قرض دار کا قول کہ میں تنگدست ہوں قبول نہ ہو گا ۔ لیکن اس کے علاوہ تمام صورتوں میں قبول ہوگا۔ زوجہ کے نفقہ کے سلسلہ میں کتاب النکاح میں مذکور ہے کہ اگر عورت نے اپنے شوہر پر دعوی کیا کہ وہ مالدار ہے اور مجھ کو مالداروں کا سا نفقہ ملنا چاہیئے۔ اور شوہر نے دعویٰ کیا کہ میں تنگدست ہوں۔ لہذا مجھ پر تنگدستوں کا سا نفقہ واجب ہونا چاہیئے ۔ تو شوہر کا قول چونکہ اصل کے موافق ہے اس لئے اُس کا قول معتبر ہوگا۔ لیکن اگر عورت نے ہینہ کے ذریعہ اپنے شوہر کا مالدار ہونا ثابت کر دیا تو شوہر کا قول معتبر نہ ہو گا۔ اور کتاب العتاق میں مذکور ہے کہ اگر ایک غلام دو آدمیوں کے درمیان مشترک ہو اور ان میں سے ایک نے اپنے حصہ کو آزاد کر کے اپنے تنگدست ہونے کا دعویٰ کر دیا ہوتا کہ اپنے شریک کے لئے آدھے غلام کی قیمت کا ضامن نہ ہونا پڑے اور دوسرے شریک نے دعوی کیا کہ یہ مالدار ہے لہذا میرے حصہ کا تاوان ادا کرے تو جس شریک نے اپنا حصہ آزاد کیا ہے تنگدست ہونے کے سلسلہ میں اس کا قول معتبر ہوگا۔ کیونکہ اس کا قول اصل کے موافق ہے۔ لیکن اگر شریک آنر نے ہینہ کے ذریعہ اس کا مالدار ہونا ثابت کر دیا تو اس صورت میں اس کا قول معتبر ہوگا اور معتق پر تاوان واجب کیا جائے گا۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ یہ دونوں مسئلہ (یعنی مسئلہ نفقہ اور عبد مشترک کے اعتاق کا مسئلہ ) اخیر کے دونوں اقوال کی تائید کرتے ہیں۔ اور قول اول جو متن میں مذکور ہے اس کے مخالف ہیں۔ یہ دونوں مسئلے قول اول کے مخالف اس لئے ہیں کہ قولِ اوّل میں کہا گیا ہے کہ اگر قرضدار پر ایسا قرضہ لازم ہوا ہو جس کے عوض اس کو مال ملا ہو یا اس نے عقد سے اپنے اوپر مال لازم کیا ہو تو ان دونوں صورتوں میں اگر قرضدار نے اپنے تنگدست ہونے کا دعویٰ کیا تو تنگدست ہونے کے سلسلہ میں قرضداروں کا قول معتبر نہ ہوگا بلکہ قرض خواہ کا قول کہ وہ مالدار ہے معتبر ہو گا۔ حالانکہ مذکورہ دو مسئلوں میں سے پہلے مسئلہ میں شوہر نے عقد نکاح کے ذریعہ اپنے اوپر نفقہ لازم کیا ہے اور دوسرے مسئلہ میں احد الشریکین نے اپنا حصہ آزاد کرنے پر اقدام کیا ہے مگر اس کے باوجود تنگدستی کے سلسلہ میں شوہر کا قول اور آزان کرنے ۔ والے شریک کا قول معتبر ہے۔ اگر یہ دونوں مسئلے قول اول کے موافق ہوتے تو مالداری کے دعوئی میں عورت اور شریک ساکت کا قول معتبر ہوتا۔ پس ثابت ہو گیا کہ یہ دونوں مسئلے قول اول کے مخالف ہیں۔ اور جب قول اول کے مخالف ہیں تو قدرتی طور پر اخیر کے دونوں اقوال کے موافق ہوں گے۔ والتخريج على ما قال في الكتاب سے صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ دونوں مسئلوں کی تاویل ایسے انداز میں فرمارہے ہیں جس سے قول اول پر کوئی نقض وارد نہ ہو۔ اور یہ دونوں مسئلہ قول اول کے مخالف نہ رہیں۔ چنانچہ فرمایا کہ قدوری کی عبارت حبسه فی
Chapter on the Etiquette of the Judge. In every debt that becomes binding in exchange for property or that one makes binding upon oneself through a contract, the word 'debt' in the text means absolute debt. And absolute debt is called correct debt. Absolute debt and correct debt are that which is either discharged by payment or discharged by the creditor's release. In any case, in al-Quduri's expression, 'debt' means absolute debt. And in the two mentioned cases, i.e., the case of nafaqah, the nafaqah is not an absolute debt; rather, it is a gift from the husband. This is why, by agreement, the nafaqah lapses upon the husband's death. Similarly, in the second case, the compensation for freeing a jointly owned slave is, according to Imam Abu Hanifa, not an absolute debt. So, when in the first statement, i.e., al-Quduri's expression, 'debt' means absolute debt, and in these two cases, nafaqah and dhaman al-itq are not absolute debts, how can these two cases conform to the first statement? And how can these two cases be used to refute the first statement? The author of al-Hidayah says: In a situation where the creditor's statement that the debtor is wealthy is accepted, or in a situation where the debtor's statement that he is destitute is accepted, but the creditor proves through evidence that he has property, then in both these situations, the judge will imprison the debtor for two or three months. Then he will inquire from his neighbors and relatives about his destitution or wealth: is this debtor destitute or wealthy? The author of al-Hidayah says: The debtor will be imprisoned because, due to his evasion, his being a wrongdoer becomes apparent at the moment. And since the punishment for wrongdoing is imprisonment, he will be imprisoned. And he will be kept in prison for a period of three months so that if he has any property that he is hiding, it becomes apparent. So with this goal in mind, the lengthening of the prison term is necessary. The author of al-Hidayah says: Besides the term of two or three months, there are other terms mentioned. For example, Imam al-Tahawi set one month, and Hasan ibn Ziyad narrated from Imam Abu Hanifa a term of four to six months. But the correct opinion is that the estimation of the term should be left to the judge's discretion. The judge may imprison him for whatever duration he deems appropriate because people's circumstances vary in this regard. Some respectable people, fearing the severity and disgrace of imprisonment, try to resolve the matter quickly. Some people are of such a low character that they have no sense of shame or honor. So, even after being imprisoned for long periods, they do not admit to having property. Since the judge is also knowledgeable about people's temperaments, the matter of the prison term will be left to the judge's discretion. If the imprisoned person's property is not known, he should be released from prison. 'If no property becomes apparent for him, release him' means after the term has passed, because he becomes entitled to respite until ease, so imprisoning him after that would be oppression. And if evidence of his insolvency is established before the term, it is accepted in one narration, and in another narration it is not accepted. The majority of scholars are on the second narration. He said in the book: 'He is to be released, and he is not to be prevented from his creditors.' This speech is about being detained, and we will mention it in the chapter of interdiction, God willing. And in al-Jami' al-Saghir: A man acknowledged a debt before the judge; he imprisoned him, then inquired about him. If he was wealthy, he continued his imprisonment; if he was destitute, he released him. His intention is when he acknowledged before someone other than the judge, or before him once, then it became apparent what he owed. The imprisonment first and its term we have explained, so we will not repeat it. Ashraf al-Hidaya Volume... Chapter of the Etiquette of the Judge. Being is the original state. And being destitute is the original state because by birth a person does not possess property. So the debtor's saying 'I am poor' conforms to the original state, and the creditor's saying 'he has property' is contrary to the original state. And since the one whose statement conforms to the original state is called the defendant, and the one whose statement is contrary to the original state is called the plaintiff, therefore the creditor is the plaintiff and the debtor is the defendant. And when the plaintiff does not have evidence, the defendant's statement with an oath is accepted. Hence, the defendant, i.e., the debtor's statement that 'I am destitute' will be accepted with an oath. But if the plaintiff, i.e., the creditor proves through evidence that the debtor is wealthy, then in that case, the creditor's statement will not be accepted. And there is a narration that if the debt upon the debtor is in exchange for property, i.e., it became binding in exchange, then in that case the debtor's statement that he is destitute will not be accepted. But in all other cases, it will be accepted. Regarding the wife's nafaqah, it is mentioned in the book of Marriage that if a woman claimed against her husband that he is wealthy and that she should receive the nafaqah of the wealthy, and the husband claimed that he is destitute, so the nafaqah of the destitute should be obligatory for him, then the husband's statement, since it conforms to the original state, will be accepted. But if the woman proves through evidence that her husband is wealthy, then the husband's statement will not be accepted. And in the book of Manumission, it is mentioned that if a slave is jointly owned by two persons, and one of them freed his share and claimed to be destitute so that he would not be liable to his partner for half the slave's price, and the other partner claimed that he is wealthy and should pay compensation for my share, then the partner who freed his share, regarding his destitution, his statement will be accepted because his statement conforms to the original state. But if the other partner proves through evidence that he is wealthy, then in that case his statement will be accepted and the compensation will be made obligatory upon the manumitter. The author of al-Hidayah says: These two cases (i.e., the issue of nafaqah and the issue of freeing a jointly owned slave) support the latter two opinions and are contrary to the first opinion mentioned in the text. These two cases are contrary to the first opinion because in the first opinion it was said that if a debtor has a debt that became binding in exchange for property, or he made property binding upon himself through a contract, then in these two situations if the debtor claims to be destitute, his statement regarding destitution will not be accepted; rather, the creditor's statement that he is wealthy will be accepted. While in the two mentioned cases, in the first case the husband made nafaqah binding upon himself through the marriage contract, and in the second case one of the partners proceeded to free his share, yet despite that, regarding destitution, the husband's statement and the partner's statement who freed are accepted. If these two cases were in accordance with the first opinion, then in the claim of wealth, the wife's and the silent partner's statements would be accepted. So it is established that these two cases are contrary to the first opinion. And when they are contrary to the first opinion, then naturally they will be in accordance with the latter two opinions. And from 'And the interpretation is based on what he said in the book', the author of al-Hidayah is interpreting the two mentioned cases in such a manner that no refutation occurs against the first opinion, and these two cases do not remain contrary to the first opinion. For he said that al-Quduri's expression 'he imprisoned him'...

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the chapter of the judge's etiquette, specifically addressing the procedure for handling a debtor who is claimed to be wealthy by the creditor but claims poverty. The commentator begins by clarifying that in al-Quduri's matn, the word 'debt' refers to 'absolute debt'—a debt that is discharged only by payment or by the creditor's forgiveness. This is important because two cases—nafaqah (maintenance) and dhaman al-itq (guarantee for freeing a jointly owned slave)—are not absolute debts as per Imam Abu Hanifa. Nafaqah is a gift from the husband, and compensation for freeing a slave is not a debt in the absolute sense. Therefore, these cases do not contradict the ruling that a debtor's claim of poverty is not accepted when the debt is incurred in exchange for property. The Hidayah then explains that if a debtor's claim of poverty is accepted (or the creditor's claim of wealth is accepted but evidence proves otherwise), the judge should imprison the debtor for two to three months. The imprisonment is not punishment for the debt but for the debtor's evasiveness, which indicates wrongdoing. The judge then investigates the debtor's financial status through neighbors and relatives. There is a difference of opinion on the duration: Imam Tahawi said one month, Hasan ibn Ziyad narrated four to six months from Abu Hanifa, but the correct view is that the duration is left to the judge's discretion based on the individual's circumstances. If the debtor's property is not discovered, he is released after the period because he becomes entitled to respite. The passage then discusses the evidentiary principle: poverty is the original state of a person (asl al-iflas), so the debtor's claim of poverty is in accordance with the original state, making him the defendant (mudda'a alayh), and his statement is accepted with oath. The creditor is the plaintiff (mudda'i) and must provide evidence. An exception exists: if the debt was incurred in exchange for property (i.e., a sale or contract where the debtor received a benefit), then the debtor's claim of poverty is not accepted; the creditor's claim is accepted unless the debtor proves otherwise. The two cases of nafaqah and freeing a jointly owned slave are used to challenge the first opinion (qawl al-awwal) because in those cases, despite the debt being incurred through a contract (marriage or manumission), the debtor's claim of poverty is accepted. The commentator reconciles this by stating that these are not absolute debts, so they do not fall under the first opinion. Thus, these cases actually support the latter two opinions that give more weight to the debtor's claim in cases where the debt is not an absolute debt in exchange for property.

Key Terms
دین مطلق (dayn mutlaq): Absolute debt that is discharged only by payment or by the creditor's release; it is the standard type of debt considered in the ruling.
اصل الافلاس (asl al-iflas): The original state of a person is presumed to be poverty or insolvency, meaning that a person is born without wealth and the default is that he does not possess property.
قول اول (qawl al-awwal): The first opinion in this context, which states that if the debt is incurred in exchange for property or through a contract, the debtor's claim of poverty is not accepted.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the reason that the debtor's claim of poverty is accepted with an oath?
A) Because the debtor is always truthful about his financial state.
B) Because poverty is the original state of a person, so his statement conforms to the original state.
C) Because the creditor's claim is always considered false.
D) Because the judge must believe the debtor to prevent oppression.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school presumes poverty unless the debt is an absolute debt incurred in exchange for property; the debtor's statement is accepted with oath, and the creditor bears the burden of proof.

Releasing the Imprisoned Debtor and Evidence of Insolvency
Ruling on releasing debtor after imprisonment and accepting evidence of insolvency

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on releasing an imprisoned debtor after the imprisonment period, and evaluate the two narrations regarding acceptance of evidence of insolvency before the period ends.

Core Idea
A debtor's proven insolvency after the imprisonment period mandates release; evidence before the period is generally not accepted because it proves a negative.

In Hanafi qadha, imprisonment of a debtor is a legitimate tool to compel payment. But what happens when the debtor remains insolvent after the maximum period? And what if creditors claim to have proof of his insolvency earlier? This lesson unpacks the ruling from al-Quduri and al-Hidayah, focusing on the interplay between the Quranic command of respite and the procedural rules of evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the basic ruling
Determine what the qadi must do after the imprisonment period ends if no wealth appears. State the ruling clearly.
The qadi must release the debtor; further imprisonment would be oppression.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the Quranic verse cited as proof for the basic ruling. Note its reference and text.
Quran 2:280 – 'And if (the debtor) is in hardship, then respite until ease.'
3
Identify the intra-school dispute
The passage presents two narrations on accepting evidence of insolvency before the period ends. List the two positions.
First narration: evidence accepted, immediate release. Second narration: evidence not accepted, debtor stays until period ends.
4
Analyze the preferred view
Understand why the majority of later scholars (mashayikh) prefer the second narration. Focus on the principle that evidence on a negative is not accepted.
Evidence of insolvency is evidence of non-possession (a negative fact), which is generally not accepted in Islamic law.
5
Reconcile apparent contradictions
Examine the apparent conflict between al-Quduri's statement (no initial imprisonment upon confession) and al-Jami' al-Saghir (immediate imprisonment upon confession). Understand the commentator's resolution.
Al-Jami' al-Saghir refers to a debtor who previously confessed outside court and then evaded payment; thus immediate imprisonment is justified.

Then if some of his wealth does not appear, he should be left alone. That is, after the period has passed, because he has become deserving of respite until he becomes wealthy. So after that, imprisoning him would be oppression. And if before the period passes, evidence of his insolvency is established, then according to one narration it will be accepted, and according to another narration it will not be accepted. And the generality of the mashayikh are on the second narration. And what the author said: 'leave his way' and do not interpose between him and his creditors. And this discussion is about following up. And we will mention it in the Book of Hajr. And in al-Jami' al-Saghir, there is that a man confessed a debt before the qadi, so the qadi should imprison him and then investigate his condition. So if he is wealthy, keep him imprisoned; if he is in straitened circumstances, release him. And its meaning is that he had confessed before someone other than the qadi, or once confessed before the qadi and then his evasion became apparent. And the beginning of imprisonment and its period we have already mentioned, so we will not repeat it.
Commentary: Sahib al-Quduri said: According to the difference of opinions, after the imprisonment period has passed, if no wealth appears from the imprisoned person, the qadi should release him. Because now this person has become deserving of respite until he becomes wealthy. As Allah says: 'And if (the debtor) is in hardship, then (let there be) respite until ease.' And when this person becomes deserving of respite, imprisoning him thereafter would be sheer oppression, and removing oppression is necessary, so the qadi will release the imprisoned person. And if before the period passes, evidence of the imprisoned person's insolvency and poverty is established, for example, a trustworthy person or two persons informed, or two persons gave testimony that he is insolvent and according to our knowledge he has no property except his clothes, we have tested him both secretly and openly, then there are two narrations. One narration is that his evidence will be accepted, i.e., the imprisoned person will be released. The second narration is that the evidence will not be accepted, i.e., before the period passes, the imprisoned person will not be released. Sahib al-Hidayah says that the madhhab of the generality of the mashayikh is in accordance with the second narration, and that is more correct. Because evidence of poverty and insolvency is in reality evidence of non-possession of wealth, and evidence of non-possession is evidence of negation, and if evidence is presented on negation, it is not accepted. Therefore, the evidence presented on insolvency will also not be accepted.
Sahib al-Hidayah said that the author's saying 'in his way' means that if no wealth appears from the debtor, he should be released from imprisonment. And the qadi should not interpose between him and his creditors, and this is speech about following up. That is, this is speech about whether the creditor will follow him or not after his release. Its detail, Allah willing, will be mentioned in the Book of Hajr. Sahib al-Hidayah said that in al-Jami' al-Saghir it is that if a man confessed a debt before the qadi, the qadi should imprison him and then inquire about him from the neighbors and other relevant parties, whether he is wealthy or in straitened circumstances. So if his wealth becomes apparent, he should keep him imprisoned; and if his straitened circumstances become apparent, he should release him. This statement of al-Jami' al-Saghir is apparently contradictory and opposite to Quduri's statement. Because Quduri's statement in the first chapter shows that if the debt is established by confession, the qadi will not initially imprison the debtor. And from this statement of al-Jami' al-Saghir, it appears that upon confession, the qadi will imprison the debtor immediately. Since there was an apparent contradiction between the statements of Quduri and al-Jami' al-Saghir, Sahib al-Hidayah quoted the statement of al-Jami' al-Saghir and explained its correct meaning. Thus he said: Imam Muhammad's intention is that the debtor had confessed the debt before someone other than the qadi, but then his non-payment made his insolvency apparent. Then the creditor brought him to the qadi, and as soon as he confessed before the qadi that he had not yet paid the debt, the qadi will imprison him. After this interpretation, there will be no contradiction between the statements of Quduri and al-Jami' al-Saghir. Sahib al-Hidayah said that the beginning of imprisonment mentioned in al-Jami' al-Saghir and the period of imprisonment are the same as previously mentioned, so it will not be repeated.
Source pages p. 276

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the ruling of Imam al-Quduri regarding the imprisonment of a debtor. It begins by stating the basic ruling: if a debtor imprisoned for debt has no apparent wealth after the imprisonment period ends, the qadi must release him. The reason is that the debtor is now entitled to respite until he becomes wealthy, based on the Quranic verse (2:280): 'And if (the debtor) is in hardship, then (let there be) respite until ease.' Continuing to imprison him after this period would be oppression (zulm), which must be removed. The passage then addresses a nuance: what if evidence (bayyinah) of the debtor's insolvency is established before the imprisonment period ends? There are two narrations (riwayat) within the Hanafi school. According to one, the evidence is accepted and the debtor is released immediately. According to the preferred view (the second narration, adopted by the majority of later scholars), the evidence is not accepted, and the debtor remains imprisoned until the period ends. The reasoning is that evidence of insolvency is evidence of a negative fact (lack of wealth), and evidence on a negative is generally not accepted in Islamic law. The author then explains a potential contradiction between the statements of al-Quduri and Imam Muhammad's al-Jami' al-Saghir. Al-Quduri's text suggests that a debtor who confesses debt should not be imprisoned initially, while al-Jami' al-Saghir appears to order immediate imprisonment upon confession. The commentator reconciles this by explaining that al-Jami' al-Saghir refers to a case where the debtor had previously confessed the debt outside the qadi's court and then defaulted, showing his unwillingness to pay. When brought to the qadi, he confirms the debt, so the qadi imprisons him to compel payment. This is not a contradiction but an application to different scenarios. The passage also notes that after release, the issue of whether creditors can pursue the debtor is to be discussed later in the Book of Hajr. The overall ruling is well-established in the Hanafi school, with the mufta bihi position being the second narration favoring the completion of the imprisonment period.

Key Terms
بَيِّنَة (bayyinah): Legal evidence, typically consisting of the testimony of two witnesses or the admission of a party.
مُفْلِس (muflis): An insolvent person whose debts exceed his assets, such that he has no apparent wealth beyond basic necessities.
حَبْس (habs): Imprisonment by the qadi as a means of compelling payment of a debt or performance of an obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred Hanafi view (mufta bihi), which of the following statements is true regarding evidence of a debtor's insolvency presented before the end of his imprisonment period?
A) It is accepted and the debtor is released immediately.
B) It is not accepted because it is evidence of a negative fact.
C) It is accepted only if presented by two male witnesses.
D) It is left to the discretion of the qadi.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school mandates release of an imprisoned debtor after the maximum period; evidence of insolvency before that period is not accepted as mufta bihi, based on the principle that evidence cannot prove a negative.

Qada — Judiciary

Imprisonment for Wife's Maintenance and Father's Debt
Ruling with proof: imprisonment of husband for maintenance and exemption of father for debt

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on imprisoning a husband for non-payment of wife's maintenance and imprisoning a father for his son's debt, and explain the underlying principles of coercion versus punishment.

Core Idea
A father cannot be imprisoned for his son's debt because imprisonment is a punishment, but he can be imprisoned for refusing to provide maintenance for his child.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses two seemingly similar cases: a husband refusing to pay his wife's maintenance and a father refusing to pay his son's debt. The rulings differ sharply, and understanding why reveals a key Hanafi principle: imprisonment for non-payment of maintenance is a coercive measure to protect the vulnerable, while imprisonment for debt is a punitive measure that a son cannot seek against his father. Let's unpack the reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings and their conditions
Extract from the text the first ruling: a husband is imprisoned for not paying his wife's maintenance. Then the second ruling: a father is not imprisoned for his son's debt. Note the exception: if the father refuses to pay his son's maintenance, he is imprisoned.
Both rulings involve a refusal to pay, but the legal outcomes differ.
2
Analyze the reasoning for the first ruling
The text says the husband is 'oppressive' (zālim) by refusing. Imprisonment here is a coercive measure to compel him to fulfill his obligation. It is not a punishment for debt but a means to enforce a continuing duty.
Maintenance is a right of the wife that must be paid regularly; refusal is an ongoing injustice.
3
Analyze the reasoning for the second ruling
The father is not imprisoned because imprisonment is deemed a type of punishment (ʿuqūbah). The text draws an analogy to other punishments: a father is not subject to qisas for killing his son nor to hadd for slandering him. Therefore, the son cannot seek such punishment against his father.
The Quranic verse (17:23) commands humility towards parents, reinforcing this principle.
4
Understand the exception for child maintenance
If the father refuses to pay maintenance for his young child, he is imprisoned. The reason is that maintenance is essential for the child's survival; withholding it is an attempt to harm the child. Furthermore, maintenance cannot be compensated later because it lapses with time.
Here imprisonment is not punishment but a protective measure, similar to the husband's case.
5
Recognize the cross-madhhab status
While the prohibition of imprisoning a father for debt is generally agreed upon among schools, the imprisonment for maintenance of a child may differ. Hanafi law permits it to protect the child.
The passage is from the Hanafi school and relies on the principles of zulm and ʿuqūbah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ويحبس الرجل في نفقة زوجته لانه ظالم بالامتناع ولا يحبس الوالد في دين ولده لانه نوع عقوبة فلا يستحقه الولد على الوالد كالحدود القصاص الا اذا امتنع عن الانفاق عليه لان فيه احياء لولده ولانه لا تدارك لسقوطه بمرور الزمان والله اعلم
ترجمہ اور مرد اپنی بیوی کے نفقہ میں محبوس کیا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ وہ انکار کرنے میں ظالم ہے۔ اور باپ کو اس کے بیٹے کے قرضہ میں محبوس نہیں کیا جائے گا اس لئے کہ قید ہونا ایک طرح کی عقوبت ہے۔ پس بیٹے کو باپ پر ایسی عقوبت کا استحقاق نہیں ہے۔ جیسے حدود اور قصاص مگر جب باپ بیٹے پر خرچ کرنے سے انکار کرے۔ کیونکہ ایسا کرنے میں اس کے بیٹے کی زندگی ہے۔ اور اس لئے کہ اس کا تدارک نہیں ہو سکتا ہے کیونکہ زمانہ گزرنے کی وجہ سے نفقہ ساقط ہو جاتا ہے۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب۔
تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر قاضی نے کسی شخص پر اس کی بیوی کا نفقہ مقرر کر دیا ہو یا زوجین نے نفقہ کی کسی مقدار پر اتفاق کر لیا ہو پھر شوہر نے بیوی کا نفقہ ادا نہ کیا اور بیوی نے قاضی کی عدالت میں مقدمہ پیش کیا تو قاضی شوہر کو محبوس کرے گا کیونکہ نفقہ نہ دینے کی وجہ سے شوہر کا ظالم ہونا ظاہر ہو گیا ہے اور ظالم کی سزا حبس اور قید ہے اس لئے شوہر کو بیوی کا نفقہ ادا کرنے کی وجہ سے محبوس کر لیا جائے گا۔ اور باپ اپنے بیٹے کے قرضہ کی وجہ سے محبوس نہ ہو گا۔ یعنی اگر بیٹے کا باپ پر قرضہ ہو اور باپ ادا نہ کرے اور بیٹا قاضی کے یہاں مرافعہ کرے تو قاضی باپ کو قید نہ کرے گا۔ کیونکہ قید ہونا ایک طرح کی عقوبت ہے اور بیٹے کو باپ پر ایسی عقوبت کا استحقاق نہیں ہے۔ حتی کہ اگر باپ نے بیٹے کو عمدا قتل کر دیا تو باپ سے قصاص نہیں لیا جاتا۔ اور اگر باپ نے اپنے بیٹے پر زنا کی تہمت لگائی تو باپ پر حدِ قذف جاری نہ ہوگی۔ اسی طرح اگر باپ بیٹے کا قرضہ نہ ادا کرے تو بیٹے کو یہ حق حاصل نہیں ہے کہ اپنے قرضہ کی وجہ سے باپ کو محبوس کرائے ۔ اور بیٹے کو یہ حق کیسے حاصل ہو سکتا ہے۔ درانحالیکہ باری تعالیٰ کا ارشاد ہے وَ لَا تَقُلْ لَهُمَا أُفٍّ وَ اخْفِضْ لَهُمَا جَنَاحَ الذُّلِّ مِنَ الرَّحْمَةِ ہاں اگر باپ اپنے بیٹے کا نفقہ دینے سے انکار کرے تو اس کو قید کر لیا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ نفقہ دینے میں اس کے بچے کی زندگی اور پرورش ہے۔ اور نفقہ نہ دینے میں اس کو ہلاک کرنے کی سعی کرنا ہے۔ پس بچہ کو ہلاک کرنے کے ارادے رونے کے سنے اس توقیہ بیا
He said: And a man is imprisoned for the maintenance of his wife because he is oppressive by refusing. And a father is not imprisoned for the debt of his son because it is a type of punishment, so the son does not deserve it from the father, like the hudud and qisas. Except when he refuses to spend on him (the son's maintenance), because in that is the preservation of his son's life, and because its lapse cannot be compensated with the passage of time. And Allah knows best.
Translation: And a man will be imprisoned for the maintenance of his wife. Because he is oppressive in refusing. And a father will not be imprisoned for the debt of his son, because imprisonment is a type of punishment. Therefore, the son does not deserve such punishment from the father, like hudud and qisas. Except when the father refuses to spend on his son. Because in doing so, there is the preservation of his son's life. And because it cannot be compensated, as maintenance lapses with the passage of time. And Allah knows best what is correct.
Commentary: The scenario is that if the qadi has fixed the maintenance of a man's wife, or the spouses have agreed on a certain amount of maintenance, then the husband does not pay the wife's maintenance and the wife files a case in the qadi's court, then the qadi will imprison the husband. Because due to not paying maintenance, the husband's oppression becomes apparent, and the punishment of an oppressor is imprisonment and confinement. Therefore, the husband will be imprisoned for not paying his wife's maintenance. And a father will not be imprisoned for his son's debt. That is, if the son has a debt against the father and the father does not pay, and the son petitions the qadi, the qadi will not imprison the father. Because imprisonment is a type of punishment, and the son does not deserve such punishment from the father. Even if the father intentionally kills the son, qisas is not taken from the father. And if the father accuses the son of adultery, the hadd of qadhf will not be enforced on the father. Similarly, if the father does not pay the son's debt, the son has no right to have the father imprisoned for his debt. And how can the son have this right? Whereas Allah says: 'And say not to them 'uff' and lower to them the wing of humility out of mercy.' Yes, if the father refuses to pay the maintenance of his son, then he will be imprisoned. Because in paying maintenance is the preservation and upbringing of his child. And in not paying maintenance, he is attempting to destroy him.
Source pages p. 277

Commentary
This passage presents two related rulings: (1) imprisonment for non-payment of wife's maintenance, and (2) non-imprisonment of a father for his son's debt, with an exception for the father's refusal to pay his son's maintenance. The first ruling: A husband who refuses to pay his wife's court-ordered or agreed-upon maintenance is imprisoned. The reason is that his refusal constitutes oppression (zulm), and the punishment for an oppressor is imprisonment. This is a means to compel him to fulfill his obligation. The second ruling: A father is not imprisoned for a debt owed to his son. The text draws an analogy (qiyas) to criminal punishments: a father is not subject to qisas for killing his son, nor to the hadd of qadhf for slandering his son. Similarly, imprisonment—being a form of punishment—cannot be applied to a father at the behest of his son. The Quranic imperative to treat parents with humility and not even say 'uff' to them (Surah al-Isra 17:23) reinforces the principle that a son cannot seek punitive measures against his father. However, there is an exception: if a father refuses to pay maintenance (nafaqah) for his young child, he can be imprisoned. The reasoning is that maintenance is essential for the child's survival; withholding it is tantamount to attempted destruction. Moreover, maintenance cannot be compensated later because it lapses with time (if not paid, the child suffers irreparable harm). Therefore, imprisonment is here a preventive and protective measure, not a punishment. This exception does not contradict the general principle because the father's refusal to provide maintenance is seen as a form of neglect endangering life, not a mere financial dispute. The mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school is as stated: father not imprisoned for debt, but imprisoned for maintenance of his child if he refuses to pay.

Key Terms
نَفَقَة (nafaqah): Maintenance, including food, clothing, and shelter, which a husband is obligated to provide for his wife, and a father for his minor children.
عُقُوبَة (uqubah): Punishment, here referring to imprisonment which is considered a type of punishment in Islamic law.
حُدُود (hudud): Fixed penalties prescribed by Islamic law for certain crimes, such as theft, adultery, and false accusation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, in which of the following situations can a father be imprisoned?
A) For refusing to pay his son's debt
B) For refusing to pay his wife's maintenance
C) For refusing to pay his son's maintenance
D) All of the above

Key Takeaway
Imprisonment for maintenance is a coercive remedy to protect dependents, while imprisonment for debt is a punishment that a child cannot seek against a parent.

Reconciling Quduri and Jami' al-Saghir on Imprisonment of a Debtor
Reconciling apparent contradiction between Quduri and Jami' al-Saghir

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how the apparent contradiction between Quduri and Jami' al-Saghir regarding the imprisonment of a debtor is resolved through contextual interpretation (ta'wil).

Core Idea
Imprisonment of a debtor is not based on a bare court acknowledgment, but on prior evidence of insolvency after a previous acknowledgment outside court.

This lesson examines a critical refinement by the commentator of al-Hidayah, who reconciles two seemingly conflicting statements from authoritative Hanafi texts. The apparent contradiction concerns whether a judge should immediately imprison a debtor upon acknowledgment of debt. By analyzing the context, the commentator shows that the positions are actually consistent, and the difference lies in the circumstances surrounding the acknowledgment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the apparent contradiction
Read the statements from Quduri (judge will not imprison in the first instance) and Jami' al-Saghir (judge imprisons upon acknowledgment). Note the conflicting indications.
The contradiction is only apparent; the commentator resolves it.
2
Understand the ta'wil (reconciliation) offered
The commentator explains that the debtor had previously acknowledged the debt outside court and then failed to pay, revealing insolvency. When he later appears before the judge and acknowledges again, imprisonment is appropriate.
The key is the prior acknowledgment and non-payment outside court.
3
Distinguish the two scenarios
Scenario A: Fresh acknowledgment in court with no prior history – no immediate imprisonment (Quduri). Scenario B: Prior acknowledgment elsewhere, failure to pay, then confirmation in court – imprisonment (Jami' al-Saghir).
Both rulings are correct in their respective contexts.
4
Apply the same reasoning to similar cases
Recognize that rulings may appear contradictory without context, but ta'wil harmonizes them. This principle applies when reconciling other textual differences in fiqh.
Always look for contextual factors before concluding contradiction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الادب القاضي
121
اشرف الہدایہ جلد نم
ہوا ہو تو قاضی اول و بلہ میں قرضدار کو محبوس نہیں کرے گا۔ اور جامع صغیر کی اس عبارت سے ظاہر ہے کہ اقرار کرتے ہی قرضدار کو قاضی محبوس کر لے گا۔ قددری اور جامع صغیر کی عبارتوں میں چونکہ بظاہر تناقض تھا اس لئے صاحب ہدایہ نے جامع صغیر کی عبارت نقل فرما کر اس کی صحیح مراد بیان فرمائی ہے۔ چنانچہ فرمایا کہ امام محمد کی مراد یہ ہے کہ قرضدار قاضی کے علاوہ کے پاس قرضہ کا اقرار کر چکا ہے مگر پھر ادا نہ کرنے سے اس کا نادہند ہونا ظاہر ہو گیا۔ پھر قرض خواہ اس کو قاضی کے پاس لے گیا تو جوں ہی اس نے قاضی کے پاس اقرار کیا کہ میں نے ابھی تک قرضہ ادا نہیں کیا ہے تو قاضی اس کو قید کر لے گا۔ اس تاویل کے بعد قدوری اور جامع صغیر کی عبارت میں کوئی تناقض نہ ہو گا۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ جامع صغیر میں مذکور محبوس کرنے کی ابتداء اور حبس کی مدت چونکہ وہی ہے جس کو پہلے بیان کیا جا چکا ہے اس لئے اس کا اعادہ نہیں کیا جائے گا۔
Book of Etiquette of the Judge. 121. Ashraf al-Hidayah volume... If it happens, the judge will not imprison the debtor in the first instance and in the town? And from this phrase of Jami' al-Saghir it appears that upon acknowledgment, the judge will immediately imprison the debtor. Since there was an apparent contradiction between the phrases of Quduri and Jami' al-Saghir, the author of al-Hidayah quoted the phrase of Jami' al-Saghir and explained its correct meaning. Thus he said: Imam Muhammad's intention is that the debtor had already acknowledged the debt before someone other than the judge, but then his insolvency became apparent due to non-payment. Then the creditor brought him to the judge, and as soon as he acknowledged before the judge that he had not yet paid the debt, the judge will imprison him. After this interpretation, there will be no contradiction between the phrases of Quduri and Jami' al-Saghir. The author of al-Hidayah said that since the initiation of imprisonment and its duration mentioned in Jami' al-Saghir are the same as previously explained, he will not repeat them.
Source pages p. 277

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement by the commentator resolving an apparent textual contradiction between two authoritative Hanafi works: al-Quduri's Mukhtasar and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani's Jami' al-Saghir. The contradiction concerns whether a debtor who acknowledges a debt should be imprisoned immediately. Al-Quduri's statement suggests that the judge does not imprison the debtor at the initial stage, while Jami' al-Saghir seems to say that the debtor is imprisoned upon acknowledgment. The commentator explains that the reconciliation lies in the context: the debtor had already acknowledged the debt elsewhere and subsequently failed to pay, revealing his insolvency. When he then comes before the judge and acknowledges the debt again (or confirms non-payment), the judge may imprison him. Thus, imprisonment is not based on the bare acknowledgment in court, but on the prior evidence of insolvency. The commentator notes that the details of the imprisonment procedure are not repeated as they were already covered earlier in the text. This ruling falls under the judge's authority to detain a debtor who is able to pay but refuses (imprisonment for zahir al-riwayah), but here the focus is on the timing of imprisonment relative to acknowledgment.

Key Terms
قرضدار (qarzdār): A person who owes a debt.
حبس (habs): Imprisonment by the judge as a coercive measure or penalty.
تاويل (ta'wīl): Interpretation that reconciles seemingly conflicting texts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the reconciliation provided in this passage, when does the judge imprison the debtor?
A) Immediately upon the debtor's acknowledgment of the debt in court.
B) Only after the debtor's insolvency becomes apparent due to non-payment after a prior acknowledgment elsewhere.
C) Only if the debtor fails to produce witnesses.
D) The debtor is never imprisoned for debt.

Key Takeaway
The apparent contradiction between Quduri and Jami' al-Saghir is resolved by understanding that the imprisonment in Jami' al-Saghir presupposes prior acknowledgment outside court and subsequent insolvency, making the two rulings consistent.

Imprisoning the Husband for Wife's Maintenance
Ruling on imprisoning husband for wife's nafaqah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that a husband is imprisoned for refusing to pay his wife's maintenance, and explain the reasoning based on his injustice.

Core Idea
A husband's refusal to pay nafaqah is an act of injustice; imprisonment is the judge's remedy.

This passage from al-Hidayah addresses the judge's authority to imprison a husband who withholds his wife's maintenance. The ruling is clear: imprisonment is permitted because the husband's refusal is a form of injustice (zulm). This lesson explains the basis for this ruling and its conditions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
What is the situation that triggers imprisonment? The husband has been ordered by a judge or has agreed to pay maintenance for his wife but refuses to do so despite being able.
The text assumes the husband is capable of paying (able) but refuses.
2
State the ruling
The ruling is that the judge must imprison the husband until he pays or until the debt is settled. This is a wajib measure.
Imprisonment is a discretionary penalty (ta'zir) for the injustice of withholding a wajib right.
3
Identify the proof
The proof is the husband's injustice. The text says 'because he is unjust by withholding.' Injustice (zulm) is prohibited and punishable.
The proof is rational (istihsan) based on the principle that the judge must prevent harm and enforce rights.
4
Note exceptions and conditions
The imprisonment is conditional on the husband being able to pay. If he is poor, he is not imprisoned. The wife must have a valid claim (maintenance fixed by judge or agreement).
The text does not mention these conditions explicitly, but they are standard Hanafi rules.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيوي کے نفقہ میں شوہر کو قید کرنے کا حکم ، بچہ کے دین کے عوض والد کو قید میں نہ ڈالے
قال ويحبس الرجل في نفقة زوجته لانه ظالم بالامتناع ولا يحبس الوالد في دين ولده لانه نوع عقوبة فلا يستحقه الولد على الوالد كالحدود القصاص الا اذا امتنع عن الانفاق عليه لان فيه احياء لولده ولانه لا تدارک لسقوطه ـــــزمـــان والله اعلم
ـضى

ہاں اگر باپ اپنے بیٹے کا نفقہ دینے سے انکار کرے تو اس کو قید کر لیا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ نفقہ دینے میں اس کے بچے کی زندگی اور پرورش ہے۔ اور نفقہ نہ دینے میں اس کو ہلاک کرنے کی سعی کرنا ہے۔ پس بچہ کو ہلاک کرنے کے ارادے رونے کے سنے اس توقیہ بیان کی
دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ زمانے کے گزرنے سے چونکہ نفقہ ساقط ہو جاتا ہے۔ اس لئے اس کا مدار کر ممکن نہیں ہے۔ اور دوسرے دیون زمانے کے گزرنے سے چونکہ ساقط نہیں ہوتے اس لئے اس کا تدارک ممکن ہے۔ پس اس فرق کی وجہ سے اولاد کے نفقہ کو دوسرے دیون پر قیاس نہیں کیا جا سکتا ہے۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب۔
Ruling on imprisoning the husband for wife's maintenance, and not imprisoning the father for son's debt. He said: The man is imprisoned for his wife's maintenance because he is unjust by withholding. And the father is not imprisoned for his son's debt because it is a type of punishment, so the son does not deserve it against the father, like the prescribed punishments (hudud) and retaliation (qisas). Except when he refuses to spend on him (the son's maintenance) because in it is the preservation of his son's life, and because it cannot be compensated after its lapse due to time. And Allah knows best. Translation: And the man will be imprisoned for his wife's maintenance because he is unjust by refusal. And the father will not be imprisoned for his son's debt because imprisonment is a type of punishment, so the son does not deserve such punishment against the father, like hudud and qisas. But when the father refuses to spend on his son, then he will be imprisoned because in that is the life of his son, and because it cannot be compensated as it lapses with time. And Allah knows best. Explanation: The scenario is that if the judge has fixed the wife's maintenance upon a man, or the spouses have agreed on an amount, and then the husband does not pay, and the wife files a case, the judge will imprison the husband because his injustice becomes apparent, and the punishment for the unjust is imprisonment. The father will not be imprisoned for his son's debt: if the son has a debt upon the father and the father does not pay, and the son petitions the judge, the judge will not imprison the father because imprisonment is a punishment and the son does not deserve such punishment against the father. Indeed, if the father intentionally kills the son, no retaliation is taken; if the father slanders the son, the hadd penalty for false accusation is not applied. Similarly, if the father does not pay the son's debt, the son does not have the right to have him imprisoned. How can he have this right when Allah says: 'Do not say to them 'Uff' and lower to them the wing of humility out of mercy.' (Quran 17:23) Yes, if the father refuses to pay his son's maintenance, he will be imprisoned because in maintenance is the life and upbringing of the child, and in withholding it he endeavors to destroy him. So to prevent destruction... The second reason is that because maintenance lapses with the passage of time, it cannot be compensated, while other debts do not lapse with time and can be compensated. Due to this difference, maintenance of children cannot be analogized to other debts. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 277

Commentary
This passage presents two distinct rulings in the chapter of the judge's etiquette. The first ruling: A husband who refuses to pay his wife's maintenance (nafaqah) after it has been fixed by the judge or agreed upon is imprisoned. The reason given is that he is unjust (zalim) by withholding what is obligatory. Imprisonment is a discretionary penalty for injustice. The second ruling: A father is not imprisoned for a debt owed to his son. The reason is that imprisonment is a punishment, and a son does not have the right to subject his father to punishment. This is analogous to hudud (fixed punishments) and qisas (retaliation), which are not applied between parent and child. For example, if a father kills his son intentionally, qisas is not imposed; if he falsely accuses his son of zina, the hadd of qadhf is not applied. Similarly, imprisonment for debt is a form of punishment, so it is not permitted against the father. However, there is an exception: if the father refuses to pay maintenance (nafaqah) for his son (i.e., a child whom he is obliged to support), then he is imprisoned. The reasoning is twofold: first, maintenance is essential for the child's survival; withholding it is equivalent to attempting to destroy the child. Second, maintenance lapses with time (i.e., if not paid daily, it cannot be made up later), whereas other debts (like loan debts) remain and can be enforced later. Thus, for the child's maintenance, imprisonment is a preventive measure to save the child's life, not a punishment per se. This distinction is based on istihsan (juristic preference) rather than strict qiyas, because analogy to other debts would lead to hardship. The Hanafi school relies on the Quranic command of kindness to parents (Quran 17:23) and on the principle that punishment is not due from child to parent, while maintenance of a child is a duty akin to preservation of life.

Key Terms
نفقہ (nafaqah): Maintenance: food, clothing, shelter, and other necessities that a person is obliged to provide for dependents (wife, children, parents).
ظالم (zalim): Unjust, oppressor; here referring to the husband who withholds maintenance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is a husband imprisoned for refusing to pay his wife's maintenance?
A) Because he is in debt.
B) Because he is unjust (zalim) by withholding.
C) Because the wife requested it.
D) Because the judge has no other option.

Key Takeaway
A husband's refusal to pay wajib maintenance is an act of injustice, justifying imprisonment as a coercive measure to enforce the wife's right.

Father Not Imprisoned for Son's Debt: The Hanafi Exception
Ruling on not imprisoning father for son's debt and imprisoning for son's maintenance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why a father is not imprisoned for a debt owed to his son, but is imprisoned for refusing to pay his son's maintenance, using the Hanafi distinction between punishment and preservation of life.

Core Idea
Imprisonment is a punishment; a son cannot punish his father, but maintenance is a life-preserving obligation.

This passage continues with a second, more nuanced ruling: a father is not imprisoned for a debt he owes his son, even if he refuses to pay. The reason is that imprisonment is a form of punishment, and a son does not have the right to punish his father. However, an exception is made for maintenance: if the father refuses to pay his son's maintenance, he is imprisoned. This lesson examines the reasoning, including the analogy to hudud and qisas, and the distinction between debts that lapse and those that do not.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
There are two separate cases: (1) father owes son a debt (loan) and refuses to pay; (2) father refuses to pay son's maintenance (nafaqah). The rulings differ.
The passage contrasts these two to highlight the exception.
2
State the ruling for the debt case
The father is NOT imprisoned for his son's debt. The text explicitly says: 'the father is not imprisoned for his son's debt.'
This is the general rule.
3
Identify the proof for the debt case
The proof is that imprisonment is a type of punishment (uqubah), and the son does not deserve to inflict punishment on his father. This is analogized to hudud and qisas, which are also not applied between parent and child.
The analogy (qiyas) is to the established rulings of hudud and qisas.
4
State the ruling for the maintenance case
The father IS imprisoned if he refuses to pay his son's maintenance. The text says: 'except when he refuses to spend on him, then he is imprisoned.'
This is an exception to the general rule.
5
Analyze the distinction
The distinction is based on two reasons: (a) Maintenance is essential for the child's life; withholding it is an attempt to destroy the child. (b) Maintenance lapses with time, so if not paid daily, it cannot be compensated later. Debt, on the other hand, remains and can be collected later without harm to life.
Thus, imprisonment for maintenance is a coercive measure to preserve life, not a punishment.

قال ويحبس الرجل في نفقة زوجته لانه ظالم بالامتناع ولا يحبس الوالد في دين ولده لانه نوع عقوبة فلا يستحقه الولد على الوالد كالحدود القصاص الا اذا امتنع عن الانفاق عليه لان فيه احياء لولده ولانه لا تدارک لسقوطه ـــــزمـــان والله اعلم
ـضى

عقوبت (uqubah): Punishment, penalty; here referring to imprisonment as a punitive measure.
حدود (hudud): Fixed punishments prescribed by Shariah (e.g., for theft, zina, false accusation).
قصاص (qisas): Retaliation in kind for homicide or bodily injury.

The Judge's Letter: Validity Despite Contradicting Analogy
Explains why a judge's letter is valid despite being against analogy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the validity of a judge's letter to another judge, identify the proofs (ijma and hadith), and explain the condition that makes it acceptable despite the risk of forgery.

Core Idea
A judge's letter is valid proof despite being against analogy, upheld by consensus and Prophetic practice.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah addresses the legal status of a judge's written communication to another judge. Although such a letter contradicts analogical reasoning (qiyas), the Hanafi school accepts it as valid proof based on the consensus (ijma) of the Companions and the practical necessity (hajat) of litigants who cannot bring witnesses and defendants from different cities. The suspicion of forgery is removed by requiring two witnesses to authenticate the letter and seal.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its exceptional nature
The ruling is that a judge's letter to another judge is valid legal proof (sahih), even though it contradicts qiyas. Understand why qiyas would reject it: a judge's oral statement has no force outside his jurisdiction, so a written letter should have even less force.
This ruling is an exception, not the general rule.
2
Recognize the proofs from ijma and hadith
The primary proof is the consensus (ijma) of the Companions and Successors that such letters are permissible. Additionally, the hadith of Duhak bin Sufyan provides direct Prophetic precedent: the Prophet wrote a letter instructing that a wife inherit from her husband's blood money.
The hadith shows that the Prophet himself used written correspondence as legal proof.
3
Analyze the objection and its answer
The objection is that letters and seals can be forged, creating suspicion. The answer is that the letter is accepted only when two witnesses testify that it is from the sending judge and that he affixed his seal.
This condition removes the shubhah (doubt) of forgery.
4
Determine the scope of applicability
The validity of the judge's letter applies to financial rights and similar claims, but not to hadd punishments or qisas (retaliation). Those require stricter proof and are not established in cases of doubt.
This distinction is crucial for understanding the limits of the ruling.

Source Text

بابُ كتاب القاضى الى القاضى

قبول کیا ہے تو اس خبر پر دوسرے قاضی کو عمل کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ قاضی کا خبر دینا اپنی ولایت کے علاوہ دوسرے مقام پر حجت نہیں ہوتا ہے تو اس کا خط بدرجہ اولی حجت نہ ہونا ہے لیکن صحابہ اور تابعین ع کے اجماع سے ایک قاضی کا خط دوسرے قاضی کے نام جائز ہے اور لوگوں کو اس کی حاجت بھی ہے کیونکہ آدمی کو کبھی یہ قدرت نہیں ہوتی کہ وہ اپنے شہود اور مدعی علیہ کو جمع کرہے۔ مثلاً گواہ ایک شہر میں ہے اور مدعی
