8 min
Acceptance of Judge's Letter in Marriage Contracts
Ruling and proof via qiyas with debt

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a judge's letter (kitab al-qadi) is accepted for marriage contracts and explain the qiyas with debt.

Core Idea
The marriage contract itself does not require pointing; therefore a judge's letter is accepted just as for a debt.

This passage from al-Hidayah raises a question: if pointing (isharah) is required from the spouses in marriage, how can a judge's letter (kitab al-qadi) be accepted? The author resolves this by distinguishing between the spouses' identification and the marriage contract itself, drawing an analogy to debt. This reasoning establishes the permissibility of the letter for marriage and extends to similar claims like lineage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
Pointing (isharah) from the man and woman is a condition for marriage. Since kitab al-qadi is impermissible for things requiring pointing, it seems it should be impermissible for marriage as well.
2
Distinguish the subject of the claim
The claim is about the marriage contract (nikah) itself, not about the spouses as individuals. The contract is an action (fi'l), and actions do not require pointing.
Actions are established by description, not pointing.
3
Draw the analogy with debt
Debt requires pointing from the debtor, but the debt itself (obligation in the dhimmah) does not require pointing. Despite the condition, kitab al-qadi is accepted for debt. Similarly, marriage requires pointing from spouses, but the marriage contract itself does not, so kitab al-qadi is also accepted.
The marriage contract is like the debt itself, not the debtor.
4
State the ruling and extension
Therefore, kitab al-qadi is accepted for marriage. The same logic applies to other claims such as lineage (nasab) and similar matters.

PAF The book of the etiquette of the judge. Ashraf al-Hidayah volume nine and mudarabah is that: a man claimed: 'I gave so-and-so one thousand rupees for mudarabah, but the mudarib denies the mudarabah.' Here a question: In marriage, pointing is a condition; thus pointing from the man and woman is necessary. And things that need pointing, in them kitab al-qadi ila al-qadi is impermissible. Therefore, in marriage, kitab al-qadi ila al-qadi should be impermissible? The answer: In marriage, pointing from the man and woman is a condition, while the subject of the claim is the marriage itself, not the man and woman. And the marriage itself is of the category of actions, and actions do not need pointing. Thus, the marriage itself became like a debt: just as in a debt, pointing from the debtor is a condition, but the debt itself which is obligatory in the dhimmah does not need pointing. So just as in a debt, despite pointing from the debtor being a condition, kitab al-qadi ila al-qadi is permissible, similarly in marriage, kitab al-qadi ila al-qadi is permissible. This same question and answer will apply to lineage and other things. The author of al-Hidayah says: In real estate, i.e., land, house, etc., kitab al-qadi ila al-qadi is also accepted. Because the identification of land is achieved by describing its boundaries; there is no need for pointing. And it has passed before that a thing that does not need pointing, in it the judge's letter is accepted. Therefore, in land also the judge's letter will be accepted. As for movable property like animals, slave, slave-girl, in them the judge's letter is not accepted, because movable property needs pointing. However, it is narrated from Imam Abu Yusuf that the judge's letter regarding a slave will be accepted, but regarding a slave-girl it will not be accepted, because the slave, serving outside the house, is more capable of running away, and the slave-girl, serving inside the house, does not have much ability to run away. Since the possibility of running away is stronger in the slave, the need for the judge's letter will arise regarding the slave. And since the possibility of running away is not strong in the slave-girl, the need for the judge's letter will not arise regarding her. So where there is need for the judge's letter, it will be accepted; where there is no need, it will not be accepted. And the second narration of Imam Abu Yusuf is that the judge's letter regarding both slave and slave-girl will be accepted, but with the conditions mentioned in al-Mabsut etc. From Imam Abu Yusuf it is narrated that all things that are movable and transferable, in all of them the judge's letter is accepted. On this is the fatwa of the later scholars. This is also the position of Imam Malik, Imam al-Shafi'i, and Imam Ahmad.
Source pages p. 284

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning the acceptance of a judge's letter (kitab al-qadi) in marriage and various types of property. The text starts with a specific case: a mudarabah claim is denied. Then it poses a question: if pointing (isharah) is required from the man and woman in a marriage contract, and things that require pointing cannot be established by a judge's letter, then how can a judge's letter be accepted in marriage? The answer explains that the pointing is required from the spouses, but the subject of the claim is the marriage itself (the contract), not the spouses. The marriage contract is an act, and acts do not require pointing. So it is analogous to a debt: the debtor's identity requires pointing, but the debt itself does not. Hence, a judge's letter is permissible for marriage. This same logic extends to lineage and similar matters. Then the text presents the ruling of al-Hidayah: for real estate (land, house), a judge's letter is accepted because the property can be identified by describing boundaries; no physical pointing is needed. For movable property (animals, slaves), a judge's letter is generally not accepted because identification requires pointing. However, Imam Abu Yusuf has two narrations: one differentiates between a male slave (who might run away) and a slave-girl (who is less likely to run away) — the letter is accepted for a slave but not a slave-girl. The second narration (also from Imam Abu Yusuf) accepts the letter for both but with conditions. The latter is the basis of the fatwa of the later Hanafi scholars, and it also agrees with the other three imams (Malik, Shafi'i, Ahmad). This passage combines several rulings and intra-Hanafi disputes, all centered on the principle that a judge's letter is accepted when the subject matter can be identified without physical pointing.

Key Terms
کتاب القاضی الی القاضی (kitab al-qadi ila al-qadi): A written letter from one judge to another judge regarding a legal claim or evidence.
اشارہ (isharah): Physical identification through pointing or demonstration, required for certain claims like identifying individuals or specific items.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is kitab al-qadi accepted for marriage according to the passage?
A) Because marriage is more important than other contracts.
B) Because the marriage contract is an action that does not require pointing, analogous to debt.
C) Because the judge's letter is always accepted for all claims.
D) Because the spouses are not required to be identified.

Key Takeaway
Kitab al-qadi is accepted for marriage because the contract itself, being an action, does not require physical pointing.

Qada — Judiciary
intermediate
10 min
Acceptance of Judge's Letter in Immovable and Movable Property
Ruling with proof and intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on kitab al-qadi for real estate (accepted) and movable property (accepted per later fatwa), and identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf of Imam Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
A judge's letter is accepted for real estate (identifiable by boundaries) but not for movable property without necessity; later fatwa accepts for movables due to need.

After establishing the ruling for marriage, the author of al-Hidayah turns to property. He rules that kitab al-qadi is accepted for real estate because the property can be identified by boundary descriptions, removing the need for pointing. For movable property, the general rule is non-acceptance due to the need for physical pointing. However, Imam Abu Yusuf provides two narrations, and the later fatwa (mufta bihi) accepts the letter for all movables, aligning with the other schools. This lesson unpacks the conditions, the ikhtilaf, and the practical result.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling for real estate
Real estate (aqar: land, house) can be identified by describing its boundaries; no physical pointing is required. Therefore, kitab al-qadi is accepted for real estate.
This follows the general principle: matters not needing pointing are proven by letter.
2
Identify the general ruling for movable property
Movable property (manqul: animals, slaves) requires physical pointing to identify the specific item. Since a letter cannot provide this, kitab al-qadi is not accepted in the general case.
The default rule: for a'yan (physical objects) that need isharah, the letter is rejected.
3
Examine the first narration of Imam Abu Yusuf
Imam Abu Yusuf's first narration differentiates between a male slave (ghulam) who might run away and a slave-girl (jariyah) who serves inside. Due to the higher risk of flight, the letter is accepted for the slave but not for the slave-girl.
The basis is necessity (darurah): when need arises due to risk of flight, the letter is accepted.
4
Examine the second narration and the later fatwa
Imam Abu Yusuf's second narration accepts the letter for both slave and slave-girl with conditions. This narration is adopted by the later scholars (muta'akhkhirin) as the mufta bihi, extending to all movable property. This also agrees with the views of Imam Malik, al-Shafi'i, and Ahmad.
The ruling is based on general need and practical ease.

Evidence Required for Accepting a Judge's Letter
Condition of bayyinah for accepting a judge's letter

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition for accepting a judge's letter and explain why the Shafi'i qiyas is rejected.

Core Idea
A judge's letter imposes obligations, so it requires bayyinah—unlike optional letters or messengers.

In judicial administration, a judge may send a letter to another judge to enforce a ruling. But how is that letter authenticated? The Hanafi school demands evidence (bayyinah) just like any other claim, while the Shafi'i school allows recognition of handwriting. This passage from Al-Hidayah explains the reasoning through a qiyas refutation.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The receiving judge accepts the letter only with testimony of two men or one man and two women.
This is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) view.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i (and one riwayah from Malik and Abu Yusuf) allows acceptance without bayyinah if the receiving judge recognizes the sender's handwriting and seal.
The opposite view is based on qiyas.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
They analogize the judge's letter to a letter of aman from dar al-harb (accepted without bayyinah) and to messengers between judge and muzakki (accepted without bayyinah).
Both of those do not impose legal obligations.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The letter of aman is not binding; the Imam has discretion. The tazkiyah messenger does not impose; the imposition comes from the witnesses' testimony. The judge's letter directly imposes a right on the defendant, thus requiring solid evidence.
The key distinction is 'ilzam' (imposition).
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
In practice, a Hanafi judge will not act on a letter without witness testimony; a Shafi'i judge may act based on handwriting recognition.
This affects the reliability of judicial correspondence.

مکتوب الیہ قاضی کا تب قاضی کا خط کب قبول کرے گا
قال ولا يقبل الكتاب الابشهادة رجلين او رجل وامرأتين لان الكتاب يشبه الكتاب فلا يثبت الابحجة تامة وهذا لا نه ملزم فلا بد من الحجة بخلاف كتاب الاستيمان من اهل الحرب لانه ليس بملزم و بخلاف رسول القاضى الى المزكى و رسوله الى القاضى لان الالزام بالشهادة لا بالتزكية
ترجمہ اور قاضی مکتوب الیہ، قاضی کا تب کا خط قبول نہیں کرے گا مگر دو مردوں یا ایک مرد اور دو عورتوں کی گواہی کے ساتھ اس لئے کہ تحریر تحریر کے مشابہ ہوتی ہے۔ لہذا بغیر حجت تامہ کے ثابت نہ ہوگا۔ اور یہ اس لئے کہ یہ لازم کرنے والا ہے۔ لہذا حجت ضروری ہے۔

كتاب الادب القاضي اشرف الهدایہ جلد نهم برخلاف اس خط کے جو اہل حرب کی طرف سے امن چاہنے کے لئے لکھا گیا ہو۔ کیونکہ وہ لازم کرنے والا نہیں ہے۔ اور برخلاف قاضی کے فرستادہ کے مزکی کی طرف۔ اور مزکی کے ایچی کے قاضی کی طرف۔ کیونکہ لازم کرنا گواہی سے ہوتا ہے نہ کہ تزکیہ ہے۔ تشریح صاحب قدوری نے فرمایا کہ قاضی مکتوب الیہ ، قاضی کا تب کا خط اس وقت قبول کرے گا جب اُس پر سینہ موجود ہو، یعنی دو عادل مرد یا ایک مرد اور دو عورتیں گواہی دیں کہ یہ قاضی کا تب کا خط اور اس کی مہر ہے اور اس نے ہم کو گواہ مقرر کیا ہے۔ اور امام شعمی نے فرمایا کہ بغیر بینہ کے خط قاضی کو قبول کرنا جائز ہے۔ یہی ایک روایت امام مالک کی ہے۔ اور یہی ایک روایت امام ابو یوسف کی ہے لیکن ان حضرات کے نزدیک یہ شرط ہے کہ قاضی مکتوب الیہ ، قاضی کا تب کا خط اور اس کی مہر پہچانتا ہو ۔ ان کی دلیل قیاس ہے۔ یعنی اگر دارالحرب کے بادشاہ نے امان حاصل کرنے کے لئے دارالاسلام کے بادشاہ کے پاس خط بھیجا تو مملکت اسلامیہ کا بادشاہ بغیر بینہ کے اس خط کو قبول کر سکتا ہے۔ اور یہ شرعاً جائز ہے۔ اور اسی طرح اگر قاضی نے گواہوں کا تزکیہ کرنے والے مزکی کے پاس اپنا قاصد بھیجا تو اس کا بغیر گواہوں کے قبول کرنا جائز ہے کہ یہ قاضی کا آدمی ہے۔ اور اگر مزگی نے اپنا قاصد قاضی کے پاس بھیجا تو قاضی کے واسطے بغیر ہینہ کے اس کو قبول کرنا جائز ہے کہ یہ مرگی کا آدمی ہے۔ پس جس طرح دارالحرب کے بادشاہ کا خطہ امان دار الاسلام کے بادشاہ کے لئے بغیر ہینہ کے قبول کرنا جائز ہے اور قاضی کا قاصد مزگی کی طرف اور مزگی کا قاصد قاضی کی طرف بغیر بینہ کے قبول کر لیا جاتا ہے۔ اسی طرح قاضی مکتوب الیہ کے واسطے قاضی کا تب کا خط بھی بغیر بینہ کے قبول کرنا جائز ہے۔
جمہور فقہا کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ ایک خطر چونکہ دوسرے خط کے مشابہ ہوتا ہے۔ اس لئے قاضی کا تب کا خط ہونا بغیر محبت تامہ کے ثابت نہ ہوگا اور حجت اور بینہ کا ہونا اس لئے شرط ہے۔ کہ خط قاضی کے ذریعہ مدعی علیہ پر اُس چیز کو لازم کیا جاتا ہے جو خط کے اندر تحریر کی گئی ہے اور کسی پر کسی چیز کو لانے م کرنا بغیر بینہ کے نہیں ہوتا۔ اس لئے خط قاضی قبول کرنے کے لئے بینہ اور محبت تامہ کا ہونا ضروری ہے۔ اور ایک مرد اور دو عورتوں کی شہادت کا قبول کرنا اس لئے جائز ہے کہ سابق میں گذر چکا کہ خط قاضی ایسے حقوق میں قبول کیا جاتا ہے جو حقوق شبہات سے ساقط نہ ہوتے ہوں اور جو حقوق شبہات سے ساقط نہیں ہوتے ان میں مردوں کے ساتھ عورتوں کی شہادت بھی قبول کی جاتی ہے اس لئے خط قاضی قبول ہونے کے واسطے ایک مرد اور دو عورتوں کی شہادت بھی کافی ہے۔ بخلاف كتاب الاستيمان من اهل الحرب سے امام شعمی کے قیاس کا جواب ہے۔ جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ دارالحرب کے بادشاہ کا خط امان امام المسلمین پر کسی چیز کو لازم نہیں کرتا بلکہ امام مسلمین کو اختیار ہے جی چاہے اس خط کو قبول کر کے اہلِ حرب کو امان دے۔ اور جی چاہے امان نہ دے اور جو چیز ملزم ( لازم کرنے والی) نہ ہو وہ چونکہ بینہ اور محبت کی محتاج نہیں ہوتی ۔ اس لئے امان طلب کرنے کا خط بغیر بینہ کے قبول کیا جائے گا۔ اس طرح اگر قاضی نے مزکی (گواہوں کا تزکیہ اور تعدیل کرنے والے) کے پاس اپنا قاصد بھیجایا مزگی نے قاضی کے پاس اپنا قاصد بھیجا تو یہ تزکیہ ملزم نہیں ہے۔ بلکہ گواہوں کی گواہی ملزم ہے اور جب تزکیہ ملزم نہیں ہے تو اسکو قبول کرنے کے واسطے بینہ اور حجت کا پایا جانا بھی شرط نہ ہو گا۔ یعنی مدعی علیہ پر قاصد کی وجہ سے حق لازم نہیں کیا گیا۔ بلکہ ان گواہوں کے ذریعہ لازم کیا گیا جو گواہ قاصد کے ذریعہ عادل قرار پائے ہیں۔ اور جب قاصد کے ذریعہ حق لازم نہیں کیا گیا تو قاصد کا پیغام قبول کرنے کے واسطے اس پر حجت کا ہونا بھی شرط نہ ہوگا۔ یہ واضح رہے کہ اگر ایک قاضی نے دوسرے قاضی کے پاس بجائے خط کے اپنا قاصد بھیجا تو
When will the receiving judge accept the sending judge's letter? He said: The letter is not accepted except with the testimony of two men or one man and two women, because a letter resembles a letter, so it is not established except with complete evidence. And this is because it imposes an obligation, so evidence is necessary. Unlike the letter of seeking aman from the people of war, because it does not impose an obligation. And unlike the messenger of the judge to the muzakki and his messenger to the judge, because the imposition is by the testimony, not by tazkiyah. Translation: The judge to whom the letter is sent will not accept the sending judge's letter except with the testimony of two men or one man and two women, because writing resembles writing, so it is not established without complete proof. And because this letter imposes an obligation, so proof is necessary. Unlike the letter written by the people of war seeking aman, because it does not impose. And unlike the judge's messenger to the muzakki and the muzakki's messenger to the judge, because imposition is by testimony, not by tazkiyah. Explanation: Sahib al-Quduri said: The receiving judge will accept the sending judge's letter when there is bayyinah upon it, i.e., two just men or one man and two women testify that this is the sending judge's letter and his seal, and he appointed us as witnesses. And Imam al-Shafi'i said: Accepting the judge's letter without bayyinah is permissible. This is also one narration from Imam Malik, and one narration from Imam Abu Yusuf. But according to these scholars, there is a condition that the receiving judge recognizes the sending judge's letter and his seal. Their proof is qiyas: If the king of dar al-harb sent a letter of aman to the king of dar al-Islam, the king of the Islamic state can accept that letter without bayyinah, and this is legally permissible. Similarly, if the judge sent his messenger to the muzakki (who verifies witnesses), accepting him without witnesses is permissible because he is the judge's man. And if the muzakki sent his messenger to the judge, it is permissible for the judge to accept him without bayyinah because he is the muzakki's man. Just as the king of dar al-harb's letter of aman is accepted by the king of dar al-Islam without bayyinah, and the judge's messenger to the muzakki and the muzakki's messenger to the judge are accepted without bayyinah, similarly, for the receiving judge, the sending judge's letter should be permissible to accept without bayyinah. The evidence of the majority of fuqaha is that because a letter resembles another letter, the fact that it is the sending judge's letter is not established without complete proof. And the presence of proof and bayyinah is a condition because through the judge's letter, a right is imposed upon the defendant, and imposing something upon someone is not done without bayyinah. Therefore, for accepting the judge's letter, the presence of bayyinah and complete proof is necessary. And accepting the testimony of one man and two women is permissible because it has passed before that the judge's letter is accepted in rights that are not invalidated by doubts, and in rights not invalidated by doubts, the testimony of women along with men is accepted. Therefore, for the acceptance of the judge's letter, the testimony of one man and two women is sufficient. This is a response to the qiyas of Imam al-Shafi'i from the letter of seeking aman. The essence of the response is that the letter of aman from the king of dar al-harb does not impose anything upon the Imam of the Muslims; rather, the Imam has the option: if he wishes, he may accept the letter and grant aman to the people of war; if he wishes, he may not grant aman. And a thing that is not imposing does not need bayyinah and proof. Therefore, the letter seeking aman will be accepted without bayyinah. Similarly, if the judge sent his messenger to the muzakki, and the muzakki sent his messenger to the judge, this tazkiyah is not imposing; rather, the testimony of the witnesses is imposing. And since tazkiyah is not imposing, the existence of bayyinah and proof is not a condition for accepting it. That is, a right is not imposed upon the defendant because of the messenger; rather, it is imposed through those witnesses who are declared reliable by the messenger. And since a right is not imposed through the messenger, the condition of proof is not required for accepting the messenger's message.
Source pages p. 284

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning the evidence required to accept a judge's letter (kitab al-qadi). The text begins with a general ruling: the receiving judge does not accept the letter except with the testimony of two men or one man and two women. This is because a letter resembles another letter, so without complete evidence (hujjah tammah) it is not established. Also, the letter imposes an obligation, so evidence is necessary. Exceptions are given: the letter of aman from the people of war does not impose anything, so it is accepted without evidence; and the messenger sent by the judge to the tazkiyah official (muzakki) or vice versa is also accepted without bayyinah, because the imposition is through the eventual testimony, not through the messenger. Then the text cites al-Quduri's explanation: the condition is that two just men or one man and two women testify that this is the sending judge's letter and seal, and that he appointed them as witnesses. Then it presents the opposing view of Imam al-Shafi'i (and one narration from Imam Malik and one from Imam Abu Yusuf): the letter can be accepted without bayyinah if the receiving judge recognizes the sender's handwriting and seal. Their proof is qiyas: the letter of aman from a non-Muslim king to the Muslim ruler is accepted without bayyinah; similarly, messengers between judge and tazkiyah official are accepted without bayyinah. The Hanafi majority respond by distinguishing the cases: the aman letter does not impose obligation; it is discretionary. The tazkiyah messenger also does not impose; the actual imposition is by the witnesses' testimony. The judge's letter, however, imposes a legal obligation on the defendant, so it requires solid evidence. Furthermore, the acceptance of one man and two women is justified because the rights involved are not invalidated by doubts (shubuhat), where female testimony is accepted alongside males. This passage clearly defends the Hanafi position that a judge's letter requires bayyinah, contrasting with the Shafi'i leniency.

Key Terms
بینہ (bayyinah): Legal evidence, here specifically the testimony of two men or one man and two women.
تزکیہ (tazkiyah): Verification of witnesses' reliability, usually done by a specialized person (muzakki).
کتاب الاستیمان من اہل الحرب (kitab al-isti'man min ahl al-harb): A letter from the people of war (non-Muslims) seeking aman (safe conduct) from the Muslim ruler.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view, why is a judge's letter not accepted without bayyinah?
A) Because the judge might be biased.
B) Because letters are easily forged and the letter imposes a legal obligation.
C) Because the judge's letter is not a valid form of evidence.
D) Because the receiving judge is not qualified.

Key Takeaway
A judge's letter, because it imposes a legal obligation, requires bayyinah (two men or one man and two women) for acceptance, unlike non-binding letters or messengers.

Qada — Judiciary
intermediate
8 min
Conditions for Accepting a Judge's Letter: The Bayyinah Requirement
Explains conditions and disputes for accepting a judge's written judgment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition for accepting a judge's letter, explain the opposing school's qiyas, and evaluate the Hanafi response using the distinction between binding and non-binding communications.

Core Idea
A judge's letter requires witness testimony because it imposes a binding ruling; an enemy's letter or a messenger does not.

This passage from Al-Hidayah presents a classic dispute between the Hanafi school and other madhhabs regarding the acceptance of a written judgment from one judge to another. The core issue is whether the letter must be authenticated by witnesses (bayyinah) or whether recognition of the seal suffices. Understanding this ruling reveals important principles about legal proof (hujjiyyah) and the distinction between binding and non-binding communications in Islamic law.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi condition
Identify the ruling: The judge's letter is accepted only with bayyinah — two just men or one man and two women testify that it is the writing judge's letter and seal, and that they were appointed as witnesses.
This is the position of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani, based on ijma of the Tabi'in.
2
Examine the opposing proof
The Shafi'i/Maliki view (and one narration from Abu Yusuf) uses qiyas: the enemy's letter seeking amnesty is accepted without evidence, and a messenger from the judge is accepted without evidence, so the judge's letter should also be accepted without evidence if the seal is recognized.
This qiyas is rejected by the Hanafis because it ignores the binding nature of the judge's letter.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
The enemy's letter is not binding — the Muslim leader has discretion. The messenger does not impose a right; the right is imposed later by witnesses. The judge's letter directly imposes a ruling on the defendant, so it requires proof.
The key distinction: binding vs. non-binding communications.
4
Distinguish letter from messenger
A messenger (rasul) sent instead of a letter is never acceptable, even with witnesses, because the messenger does not impose anything — only the written letter, supported by practice and consensus, is accepted with witnesses.
This is a unique Hanafi rule: the messenger is analogous to a request, not a ruling.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: bayyinah is required. The thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) is that in Hanafi courts, a judge's letter must be accompanied by witnesses; in Shafi'i/Maliki courts, recognition of the seal suffices.
This ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah and is supported by ijma and athar.

Source Text

اشرف الهدایہ جلد نهم برخلاف اس خط کے جو اہل حرب کی طرف سے امن چاہنے کے لئے لکھا گیا ہو۔ کیونکہ وہ لازم کرنے والا نہیں ہے۔ اور برخلاف قاضی کے فرستادہ کے مزکی کی طرف۔ اور مزکی کے قاصد قاضی کی طرف۔ کیونکہ لازم کرنا گواہی سے ہوتا ہے نہ کہ تزکیہ ہے۔ تشریح صاحب قدوری نے فرمایا کہ قاضی مکتوب الیہ، قاضی کا تب کا خط اس وقت قبول کرے گا جب اس پر بینہ موجود ہو، یعنی دو عادل مرد یا ایک مرد اور دو عورتیں گواہی دیں کہ یہ قاضی کا تب کا خط اور اس کی مہر ہے اور اس نے ہم کو گواہ مقرر کیا ہے۔ اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ بغیر بینہ کے خط قاضی کو قبول کرنا جائز ہے۔ یہی ایک روایت امام مالک کی ہے۔ اور یہی ایک روایت امام ابو یوسف کی ہے لیکن ان حضرات کے نزدیک یہ شرط ہے کہ قاضی مکتوب الیہ، قاضی کا تب کا خط اور اس کی مہر پہچانتا ہو۔ ان کی دلیل قیاس ہے۔ یعنی اگر دارالحرب کے بادشاہ نے امان حاصل کرنے کے لئے دارالاسلام کے بادشاہ کے پاس خط بھیجا تو مملکت اسلامیہ کا بادشاہ بغیر بینہ کے اس خط کو قبول کر سکتا ہے۔ اور یہ شرعاً جائز ہے۔ اور اسی طرح اگر قاضی نے گواہوں کا تزکیہ کرنے والے مزکی کے پاس اپنا قاصد بھیجا تو اس کا بغیر گواہوں کے قبول کرنا جائز ہے کہ یہ قاضی کا آدمی ہے۔ اور اگر مزکی نے اپنا قاصد قاضی کے پاس بھیجا تو قاضی کے واسطے بغیر بینہ کے اس کو قبول کرنا جائز ہے کہ یہ مزکی کا آدمی ہے۔ پس جس طرح دارالحرب کے بادشاہ کا خط امان دارالاسلام کے بادشاہ کے لئے بغیر بینہ کے قبول کرنا جائز ہے اور قاضی کا قاصد مزکی کی طرف اور مزکی کا قاصد قاضی کی طرف بغیر بینہ کے قبول کر لیا جاتا ہے، اسی طرح قاضی مکتوب الیہ کے واسطے قاضی کا تب کا خط بھی بغیر بینہ کے قبول کرنا جائز ہے۔
جمہور فقہا کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ ایک خط چونکہ دوسرے خط کے مشابہ ہوتا ہے، اس لئے قاضی کا تب کا خط ہونا بغیر حجت تامہ کے ثابت نہ ہوگا اور حجت اور بینہ کا ہونا اس لئے شرط ہے کہ خط قاضی کے ذریعہ مدعی علیہ پر اس چیز کو لازم کیا جاتا ہے جو خط کے اندر تحریر کی گئی ہے اور کسی پر کسی چیز کو لازم کرنا بغیر بینہ کے نہیں ہوتا۔ اس لئے خط قاضی قبول کرنے کے لئے بینہ اور حجت تامہ کا ہونا ضروری ہے۔ اور ایک مرد اور دو عورتوں کی شہادت کا قبول کرنا اس لئے جائز ہے کہ سابق میں گذر چکا کہ خط قاضی ایسے حقوق میں قبول کیا جاتا ہے جو حقوق شبہات سے ساقط نہ ہوتے ہوں اور جو حقوق شبہات سے ساقط نہیں ہوتے ان میں مردوں کے ساتھ عورتوں کی شہادت بھی قبول کی جاتی ہے، اس لئے خط قاضی قبول ہونے کے واسطے ایک مرد اور دو عورتوں کی شہادت بھی کافی ہے۔ بخلاف كتاب الاستيمان من اهل الحرب سے امام شافعی کے قیاس کا جواب ہے۔ جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ دارالحرب کے بادشاہ کا خط امان امام المسلمین پر کسی چیز کو لازم نہیں کرتا بلکہ امام مسلمین کو اختیار ہے جی چاہے اس خط کو قبول کر کے اہل حرب کو امان دے اور جی چاہے امان نہ دے اور جو چیز ملزم (لازم کرنے والی) نہ ہو وہ چونکہ بینہ اور حجت کی محتاج نہیں ہوتی، اس لئے امان طلب کرنے کا خط بغیر بینہ کے قبول کیا جائے گا۔ اس طرح اگر قاضی نے مزکی (گواہوں کا تزکیہ اور تعدیل کرنے والے) کے پاس اپنا قاصد بھیجا، مزکی نے قاضی کے پاس اپنا قاصد بھیجا تو یہ تزکیہ ملزم نہیں ہے بلکہ گواہوں کی گواہی ملزم ہے اور جب تزکیہ ملزم نہیں ہے تو اس کو قبول کرنے کے واسطے بینہ اور حجت کا پایا جانا بھی شرط نہ ہوگا۔ یعنی مدعی علیہ پر قاصد کی وجہ سے حق لازم نہیں کیا گیا بلکہ ان گواہوں کے ذریعہ لازم کیا گیا جو قاصد کے ذریعہ عادل قرار پائے ہیں۔ اور جب قاصد کے ذریعہ حق لازم نہیں کیا گیا تو قاصد کا پیغام قبول کرنے کے واسطے اس پر حجت کا ہونا بھی شرط نہ ہوگا۔ یہ واضح رہے کہ اگر ایک قاضی نے دوسرے قاضی کے پاس بجائے خط کے اپنا قاصد بھیجا تو قاصد کے پیغام کی وجہ سے مدعی علیہ پر کوئی فیصلہ نہیں تھوپا جائے گا، خواہ اس بات پر کہ یہ فلاں قاضی کا قاصد ہے بینہ ہو یا نہ ہو۔ حاصل یہ کہ کتاب القاضی الی القاضی کو بینہ کے ساتھ قبول کر لیا جاتا ہے مگر رسول القاضی الی القاضی کو بینہ کے ساتھ بھی قبول نہیں کیا جائے گا۔ اور وجہ فرق یہ ہے کہ کتاب القاضی الی القاضی کے جواز پر خلاف قیاس اثر اور تابعین کا اجماع وارد ہوا ہے اس لئے کتاب القاضی الی القاضی جائز ہوگا۔ اور رسول القاضی الی القاضی کے جواز پر چونکہ نہ اثر وارد ہوا اور نہ اجماع، اس لئے رسول القاضی الی القاضی قیاس کے مطابق نا جائز رہے گا۔
Book of the Conduct of the Judge. Ashraf al-Hidayah Volume 9. Contrary to the letter written by the people of war seeking amnesty, because that is not binding. And contrary to the judge's messenger to the one who seeks character certification (muzakki), and the muzakki's messenger to the judge, because binding occurs through testimony, not through certification. Explanation: Sahib al-Quduri said: The judge to whom the letter is written will accept the writing judge's letter only when there is evidence upon it, i.e., two just men or one man and two women testify that this is the writing judge's letter and his seal, and that he appointed us as witnesses. And Imam al-Shafi'i said: Accepting the judge's letter without evidence is permissible. This is also a narration from Imam Malik, and a narration from Imam Abu Yusuf, but according to them, the condition is that the judge to whom the letter is written recognizes the writing judge's letter and his seal. Their proof is analogy (qiyas): If the king of the war territory sent a letter to the king of the Islamic territory seeking amnesty, the king of the Islamic state can accept that letter without evidence, and this is legally permissible. Similarly, if the judge sent his messenger to the muzakki (who certifies witnesses), accepting him without witnesses is permissible because he is the judge's man. And if the muzakki sent his messenger to the judge, accepting him without evidence is permissible because he is the muzakki's man. Just as the war king's letter of amnesty is permissible to accept without evidence for the Islamic king, and the judge's messenger to the muzakki and the muzakki's messenger to the judge are accepted without evidence, similarly, for the judge to whom the letter is written, the writing judge's letter is also permissible to accept without evidence. The proof of the majority of jurists is that one letter resembles another letter; therefore, that it is the writing judge's letter cannot be established without complete proof. The presence of proof and evidence is a condition because through the judge's letter, the matter written in it is imposed upon the defendant, and imposing something upon someone does not occur without evidence. Therefore, for accepting the judge's letter, evidence and complete proof are necessary. Accepting the testimony of one man and two women is permissible because it has passed earlier that the judge's letter is accepted in such rights that are not dropped by doubts, and in rights that are not dropped by doubts, women's testimony alongside men is also accepted; therefore, for the judge's letter to be accepted, the testimony of one man and two women is sufficient. This is the answer to Imam al-Shafi'i's analogy from the book of seeking amnesty from the people of war. The essence of the answer is that the war king's letter of amnesty does not impose anything upon the leader of the Muslims; rather, the leader of the Muslims has the choice: if he wishes, he may accept the letter and grant amnesty to the warring people; if he wishes, he may not grant amnesty. And whatever is not binding, since it does not need evidence and proof, therefore the letter seeking amnesty will be accepted without evidence. Similarly, if the judge sent his messenger to the muzakki, and the muzakki sent his messenger to the judge, this certification is not binding; rather, the witnesses' testimony is binding. When the certification is not binding, then for accepting it, the presence of evidence and proof is not a condition. That is, the right is not imposed on the defendant through the messenger; rather, it is imposed through those witnesses who were declared just through the messenger. And when the right is not imposed through the messenger, then for accepting the messenger's message, having proof upon it is not a condition. Be it known that if one judge sent his messenger instead of a letter to another judge, no decision will be imposed upon the defendant due to the messenger's message, whether or not there is evidence that this messenger is from such-and-such judge. The conclusion is that the writing judge to judge letter is accepted with evidence, but the messenger of a judge to another judge is not accepted even with evidence. And the reason for the difference is that permission of the judge's letter to a judge is established by a practice (athar) and consensus of the Followers (Tabi'in) contrary to analogy, so the judge's letter to a judge will be permissible. As for the judge's messenger to a judge, since neither a practice nor consensus came for its permission, the messenger of a judge to a judge remains impermissible according to analogy.
Source pages p. 285

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute on the conditions for accepting a letter from one judge to another. The Hanafi position, following Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani, is that such a letter is only acceptable when witnessed by two just men or one man and two women who testify that it is the judge's letter and seal, and that they were appointed as witnesses. This is based on consensus (ijma) of the Tabi'in and the practice of the early Muslims, which overrides analogy. The opposing view, attributed to Imam Shafi'i, Imam Malik, and a narration from Imam Abu Yusuf, holds that no witnesses are needed if the recipient judge recognizes the letter and seal; this is supported by analogy to letters of amnesty from enemy rulers and to acceptance of messengers, which do not require evidence. The Hanafi refutation distinguishes: the enemy's letter is not binding (it is a request), and a messenger does not impose a right (the right is imposed by the witnesses' testimony later). Therefore, since the judge's letter directly imposes a ruling, it requires proof. The passage also clarifies that a messenger (rasul) sent instead of a letter is never admissible, even with witnesses, because it lacks the consensus and practice that justify the letter's acceptance. This ruling is a Zahir al-Riwayah position (from the six core books of Imam Muhammad) and is mufta bihi. The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) is that in Hanafi courts, a judge's letter must be accompanied by witnesses, whereas in Shafi'i practice, recognition of the seal suffices.

Key Terms
كتاب القاضي إلى القاضي (kitab al-qadi ila al-qadi): A written judgment or communication from one judge to another judge regarding a case or legal matter.
بينة (bayyinah): Legal evidence, specifically witness testimony in this context, required to authenticate the judge's letter.
مزكي (muzakki): A person who investigates and certifies the character (tazkiyah) of witnesses for the court.
رسول القاضي (rasul al-qadi): A messenger sent by the judge to convey a message or ruling, as opposed to a written letter.
اجماع التابعين (ijma' al-tabi'in): Consensus of the Followers (the generation after the Companions) as a legal proof for the permissibility of accepting the judge's letter.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority of Hanafi scholars (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), what is required for a judge's letter to be accepted by another judge?
A) Only the recipient judge's recognition of the seal.
B) Testimony of two just men or one man and two women.
C) No conditions; the letter is accepted on its own.
D) A messenger sent with the letter.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a judge's letter is accepted only with witness testimony because it imposes a binding ruling; this is based on the practice and consensus of the Tabi'in, overriding analogy.

Procedure for Writing a Judge's Letter: Reading, Sealing, and Intra-Hanafi Disagreement
Intra-Hanafi dispute on judge's letter conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the procedural obligations of a writing judge according to the Hanafi school and evaluate the intra-Hanafi disagreement regarding their necessity.

Core Idea
A judge's letter requires witness knowledge and sealing, but Abu Yusuf relaxed this for practical necessity.

When a judge writes a letter to another judge, the Hanafi school debated the procedural steps required to ensure the letter's authenticity and the witnesses' testimony. The majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) mandated reading the letter to witnesses, sealing it in their presence, and providing an unsealed copy. However, Imam Abu Yusuf, drawing from his experience as a judge, later held that only certifying the letter and seal suffices. This passage explores the dispute and the preferred view in the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the wajib procedures according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad
The passage states that it is wajib for the writing judge to read the letter to the witnesses or inform them of its contents, seal it in their presence, and hand it over with an unsealed copy. Note that these are considered conditions (shurut) for validity.
These procedures aim to ensure witnesses have knowledge and the letter is protected from tampering.
2
Understand the rationale: witnesses must have knowledge
The majority derive this from Quran 43:86, which implies that testimony requires knowledge ('ilm). Reading the letter ensures the witnesses know what they are testifying to.
The verse is used as dalil for the necessity of knowledge.
3
Note Abu Yusuf's opposing view
Abu Yusuf later held that none of the above are conditions; the only condition is that the judge makes the witnesses testify that this is his letter and seal. In one narration, even the seal is not required.
His position is based on practical experience as a judge (khabar ≠ mu'ayanah).
4
Understand the tarjih (preferred view)
Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi chose Abu Yusuf's view, making it the mufta bihi (operative position) due to ease and practicality.
The authority weight for this view is nawadir (rare transmissions) but adopted by later scholars.
5
Apply to modern scenario
In contemporary practice, a judge's letter is validated by official seals and witness signatures; strict reading of contents is not mandated.
The mufta bihi view avoids over-formalization that could delay justice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قاضی کا تب خط پڑھ کر سنادے تا کہ گواہ مضمون سے واقف ہوں
قال ويجب ان يقرأ الكتاب عليهم ليعرفوا ما فيه او يعلّمهم به لانه لا شهادة بدون العلم ثم يختمه بحضرتهم و يسلمه اليهم كيلا يتوهم التغيير وهذا عند ابي حنيفة ومحمد لان علم ما في الكتاب والختم بحضرتهم شرط وكذا حفظ ما فى الكتاب عندهما ولهذا يدفع اليهم كتاباً اخر غير مختوم ليكون معهم معاونة على حفظهم وقال ابويوسف اخراً شئى من ذلك ليس بشرط والشرط ان يشهدهم ان لهذا كتابه و خاتمه وعن ابى يوسف ان الختم ليس بشرط ايضاً فسهل فى ذلك لما ابتلى بالقضا و ليس الخبر كالمعاينة و اختار شمس الائمة السرخسى قول ابي يوسف
ترجمہ اور قاضی کا تب کے لئے واجب ہے کہ وہ گواہوں کو خط پڑھ کر سنا دے تا کہ وہ اس کے مضمون سے واقف ہو جائیں یا خود ان کو مضمون سے آگاہ کر دے۔ کیونکہ بغیر علم کے گواہی نہیں ہوتی پھر ان کی موجودگی میں مہر لگا کر اُس خط کو ان کے سپرد کر دے تا کہ اس میں تغیر کا وہم نہ ہو۔ اور یہ طرفین کے نزدیک ہے۔ اس لئے کہ خط کے مضمون کا علم اور گواہوں کی موجودگی میں مہر لگانا شرط ہے۔ اور اسی طرح طرفین کے نزدیک خط کے مضمون کا محفوظ ہونا شرط ہے۔ اور اسی وجہ سے قاضی کا تب گواہوں کو دوسرا خط بغیر مہر کا دے تا کہ ان کے ساتھ ان کی یاداشت پر معاونت ہو۔ اور امام ابو یوسف نے آخر میں فرمایا کہ ان میں سے کوئی چیز شرط نہیں ہے۔ بلکہ شرط یہ ہے کہ ان کو اس بات پر گواہ کر لے کہ یہ اس کا خط اور اس کی مہر ہے اور امام ابو یوسف سے مروی ہے کہ قاضی کا تب کی مہر بھی شرط نہیں ہے پس امام ابو یوسف نے اس بارے میں آسانی اس وقت پیدا کی جب خود عہدہ قضا کے ساتھ مبتلا ہوئے اور ”خبر“ مشاہدہ کے مانند نہیں ہوتی ۔ اور شمس الائمہ سرخسی نے امام ابو یوسف کے قول کو اختیار کیا ہے۔
تشریح صاحب قدوری نے فرمایا کہ شہادت وغیرہ جو کچھ قاضی کا تب نے اپنے خط میں تحریر کیا ہے قاضی کا تب خط کا پورا مضمون گواہوں کو پڑھ کر سنا دے یا بغیر پڑھے ان کو اُس مضمون سے باخبر کر دے کیونکہ اگر گواہوں کو خط کا مضمون معلوم نہ ہو تو ان کی گواہی بغیر علم کے ہوگی ۔ اور بغیر علم، گواہی دینا باطل ہے۔ چنانچہ باری تعالیٰ کا ارشاد ہے الا من شهد با لحق وهم يعلمون" مگر جس نے گواہی دی کچی اور ان کو خبر تھی ۔ یعنی اگر کسی نے اپنے علم کے مطابق کچی گواہی دی تو وہ معتبر ہے۔ اس آیت سے معلوم ہوا کہ گواہ کو اس چیز کا علم ضروری ہے جس کے بارے میں گواہی دینا چاہتا ہے۔ بہر حال قاضی کا تب نے جب گواہوں کے سامنے خط پڑھ کر سنا دیا یا اُن کو اُس کے مضمون سے باخبر کر دیا تو ان کی موجودگی میں مہر لگا کر سیل کر کے طرفین کے نزدیک اس خط کو گواہوں کے حوالہ
The writing judge reads the letter so that the witnesses become familiar with its contents. He said: It is obligatory that he reads the letter to them so they know what is in it, or he informs them of it, because there is no testimony without knowledge. Then he seals it in their presence and hands it over to them so that alteration is not suspected. This is according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, because knowledge of what is in the letter and sealing in their presence is a condition, and similarly preserving what is in the letter according to them. For this reason, he gives them another letter unsealed to assist their memory. Abu Yusuf later said that none of this is a condition; rather, the condition is that he makes them witness that this is his letter and seal. And from Abu Yusuf it is narrated that the seal is also not a condition. So he made it easy in this matter because he was afflicted with the office of judge, and news is not like direct observation. Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi chose the statement of Abu Yusuf. Translation: It is obligatory for the writing judge that he reads the letter to the witnesses so they become aware of its contents, or he informs them of the contents himself, because there is no testimony without knowledge. Then he seals it in their presence and hands it over to them so that alteration is not suspected. This is according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad). Because knowledge of the letter's contents and sealing in their presence is a condition, and similarly preserving the letter's contents is a condition according to them. For this reason, the writing judge gives them another unsealed letter to assist their memory. Imam Abu Yusuf later said that none of this is a condition; rather, the condition is that he makes them witness that this is his letter and seal. And from Imam Abu Yusuf it is narrated that the seal is also not a condition. Thus Imam Abu Yusuf made it easy in this matter when he himself was afflicted with the office of judge, and news is not like direct observation. Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi chose the statement of Imam Abu Yusuf. Explanation: Sahib al-Quduri said: Whatever the writing judge has written in his letter regarding testimony etc., he should read the entire contents of the letter to the witnesses or inform them of the contents without reading, because if the witnesses do not know the contents of the letter, their testimony would be without knowledge, and giving testimony without knowledge is invalid. As Allah Almighty says: 'Except those who bear witness to the truth while they know' (Quran 43:86). Meaning if someone gives true testimony according to his knowledge, it is reliable. From this verse it is understood that the witness must have knowledge of the matter about which he wishes to testify. In any case, when the writing judge reads the letter in front of the witnesses or informs them of its contents, then seals and closes it in their presence, according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) he hands this letter over to the witnesses...
Source pages p. 286

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the procedural obligations of a judge when writing a letter to another judge. According to the majority (Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad), it is wajib for the writing judge to: (1) read the letter to the witnesses or inform them of its contents so they have knowledge (shart), (2) seal it in their presence to prevent suspicion of tampering, and (3) give them an unsealed copy to aid memory. These are conditions (shurut) for the validity of the letter's acceptance. Imam Abu Yusuf, however, later held that none of these are conditions; the only condition is that the judge makes the witnesses testify that this is his letter and seal. In one narration from Abu Yusuf, even the seal is not a condition. He relaxed the requirements due to his practical experience as a judge, reasoning that hearsay (khabar) is not equivalent to direct observation (mu'ayanah) — i.e., the witnesses do not need to memorize the contents; their certification of the letter's authenticity suffices. Imam al-Sarakhsi preferred Abu Yusuf's view, which is considered the more practical position. The commentary (Tashrih) supports the majority view by citing Quduri and the Quranic verse 'except those who bear witness to the truth while they know' to emphasize that knowledge is essential for valid testimony. The passage ends mid-sentence, but the main ruling is clear. This is a Nawadir-level transmission (since Abu Yusuf's personal practice is not from the Zahir al-Riwayah) but was adopted by later scholars like Sarakhsi.

Key Terms
وَيَجِبُ (yajibu): It is obligatory; here referring to the procedures that the writing judge must follow according to the majority.
يَخْتِمُهُ (yakhtimuhu): He seals it; the act of putting a seal on the letter in the presence of witnesses to prevent tampering.
شَرْط (shart): Condition; something whose absence renders the act invalid. Here, the majority consider knowledge of contents and sealing as shurut for the letter's acceptability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) He must read the letter to the witnesses.
B) He must seal the letter in their presence.
C) He must make the witnesses testify that this is his letter and seal.
D) He must give them an unsealed copy.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's practical position on judge letters is the one easiest on the judge, as chosen by Sarakhsi, requiring only certification.

Acceptance of a Judge's Letter vs Messenger
Distinguishing between a judge's written letter and oral messenger

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on accepting a judge's letter versus a messenger and explain the role of ijma in overriding qiyas.

Core Idea
A judge's letter is accepted with evidence but a messenger is not — because consensus (ijma) overrides analogy only for the letter.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah clarifies a crucial distinction in judicial procedure. Although qiyas (analogy) would reject both written and oral transmissions from a judge, the Hanafi school accepts the written letter based on the consensus (ijma) of the Tabi'un and an athar (tradition). The messenger remains impermissible. Understanding this distinction reveals how consensus can override the default method of qiyas in Hanafi jurisprudence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two cases
The passage discusses two methods by which a judge may communicate to another judge: a written letter (kitab) and an oral message delivered by a messenger (rasul). Recognize that both involve a transmission from one judge to another in a legal context.
The key is the medium of communication: written vs oral.
2
State the ruling for each
For the letter: it is accepted (ja'iz) provided there is evidence (bayyinah) proving it is from the judge. For the messenger: it is not accepted, even if there is evidence that the messenger is indeed the judge's messenger.
The ruling is absolute: the messenger is never accepted.
3
Identify the default legal method
By default, qiyas (analogical reasoning) would reject both the letter and the messenger. This is the baseline ruling before considering any overriding evidence.
Qiyas would treat both as unverified hearsay.
4
Identify the proof that overrides qiyas for the letter
The passage cites an athar (a narration from early authorities) and the consensus (ijma) of the Tabi'un as evidence that the letter is permissible contrary to qiyas. This consensus is what makes the letter an exception.
No such proof exists for the messenger, so qiyas remains.
5
Conclude the distinction
Thus, the Hanafi position is a specific exception to qiyas based on consensus. The letter is accepted; the messenger is not. This demonstrates how ijma can override qiyas in legal rulings.
This is a classic example of istihsan (juristic preference) based on consensus.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اشرف الہدایہ جلد نهم قاصد کے پیغام کی وجہ سے مدعی علیہ پر کوئی فیصلہ نہیں تھوپا جائے گا۔ خواہ اس بات پر کہ یہ فلاں قاضی کا قاصد ہے بینہ ہو یا نہ ہو۔ حاصل یہ کہ کتاب القاضی الی القاضی کو بینہ کے ساتھ قبول کر لیا جاتا ہے مگر رسول القاضی الی القاضی کو بینہ کے ساتھ بھی قبول نہیں کیا جائے گا۔ اور وجہ فرق یہ ہے کہ کتاب القاضی الی القاضی کے جواز پر خلاف قیاس اثر اور تابعین کا اجماع وارد ہوا ہے اس لئے کتاب القاضی الی القاضی جائز ہوگا۔ اور رسول القاضی الی القاضی کے جواز پر چونکہ نہ اثر وارد ہوا اور نہ اجماع ۔ اس لئے رسول القاضی الی القاضی قیاس کے مطابق نا جائز رہے گا۔
Ashraf al-Hidayah Volume Nine: No ruling shall be imposed upon the defendant due to the messenger's message, whether there is evidence that this is a certain judge's messenger or not. The conclusion is that a letter from a judge to a judge is accepted with evidence, but a messenger from a judge to a judge is not accepted even with evidence. The reason for the difference is that for the permissibility of a letter from a judge to a judge, contrary to analogy, an athar (narration) and the consensus of the Tabi'un have occurred, so a letter from a judge to a judge will be permissible. As for the permissibility of a messenger from a judge to a judge, since neither an athar nor consensus has occurred, the messenger from a judge to a judge remains impermissible according to analogy.
Source pages p. 286

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on judicial correspondence. It states that when a judge sends a messenger (qasid) to another judge with a message, the receiving judge cannot pass a judgment based on that message alone, regardless of whether there is evidence that the messenger is indeed the judge's messenger. However, if the judge sends a written letter (kitab), it can be accepted provided there is evidence (bayyinah) that it is from the judge. The basis for this distinction is that the acceptance of a written letter is established by an athar (a tradition from the Companions or early authorities) and the consensus (ijma) of the Tabi'un (the generation after the Companions), which overrides the default ruling of qiyas (analogy). By default, qiyas would reject both, but the letter is accepted due to this special evidence. The messenger, lacking such evidence, remains impermissible by qiyas. The key point: the Hanafi school gives weight to consensus and precedent over mere analogy in judicial practice.

Key Terms
کتاب القاضی الی القاضی (kitab al-qadi ila al-qadi): A written letter from one judge to another judge concerning a legal case.
رسول القاضی الی القاضی (rasul al-qadi ila al-qadi): A messenger sent by a judge to another judge to convey a message orally.
قیاس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning in Islamic law; here it is the default method that would reject both letter and messenger.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on accepting a messenger sent from a judge to another judge?
A) Accepted if there is evidence the messenger is from the judge.
B) Not accepted, regardless of evidence.
C) Accepted only if the messenger is a known trusted person.
D) Accepted with or without evidence.

Key Takeaway
A judge's written letter is accepted with evidence because of consensus (ijma) overriding qiyas, but a messenger's oral message is not accepted even with evidence.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on the Scribe's Duty: Necessity of Witness Knowledge vs. Simplicity
Intra-Hanafi dispute on conditions for valid witness testimony on a letter from a judge's scribe.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions required by Abu Hanifa and Muhammad for a scribe's letter, explain Abu Yusuf's later view, and identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) of the dispute.

Core Idea
Abu Yusuf's practical experience as a judge led him to relax strict conditions for witness testimony on a scribe's letter.

This passage from al-Hidayah presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on the procedure for a judge's scribe when sending a letter containing testimony. The dispute centres on what conditions must be met for the witnesses' testimony to be valid before the receiving judge. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani require detailed conditions, while Imam Abu Yusuf later adopted a more lenient view based on his own judicial experience. This lesson will examine the proofs and practical consequences of both positions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is the scribe's duty to inform witnesses of the letter's content and seal it. The ruling is that these actions are obligatory (wajib) according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, but the dispute is about which specific conditions are necessary for the witnesses' testimony to be valid.
The text begins 'قال ويجب أن يقرأ الكتاب عليهم' – He said: It is obligatory for the scribe to read the letter to them.
2
State the position of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad
They require: (1) the scribe must read the letter to the witnesses or inform them of its content; (2) seal it in their presence; (3) the witnesses must memorize the content; and (4) the scribe gives them an extra unsealed copy to aid memory.
The reason is that testimony requires knowledge (Quran 43:86) and sealing prevents suspicion of alteration.
3
State Abu Yusuf's later opinion
Abu Yusuf later said that none of the above are conditions. The only condition is that the scribe makes the witnesses testify that this is his letter and his seal. Even the seal itself may not be required.
Abu Yusuf's change came from his own experience as a judge; he found strict conditions impractical.
4
Analyse the evidence
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad rely on the Quranic verse requiring knowledge for testimony. Abu Yusuf's view is based on practical necessity (istihsan) and the fact that news of the seal is sufficient, though not equivalent to direct observation.
The text mentions 'ليس الخبر كالمعاينة' – news is not like direct observation, but Abu Yusuf allowed it for ease.
5
Determine the practical consequence
Under the strict view, if the witnesses forget any detail of the letter at the time of testimony, the receiving judge rejects the letter. Under the lenient view, the letter is accepted if the witnesses simply swear that it is the scribe's authentic letter and seal.
Al-Sarakhsi chose Abu Yusuf's view for ease (taisir), making it the mufta bihi position.

مہر لگا کر سیل کرنا بھی شرط نہیں ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا کہ امام ابو یوسف نے یہ آسانیاں اس وقت پیدا فرما ئیں جب امام موصوف بذات خود منصب قضاء پر فائز ہوئے۔ پس امام ابو یوسف نے تجر بہ اور مشاہدہ کے بعد جو کچھ فرمایا ہے وہ زیادہ صحیح ہے۔ کیونکہ خبر ، مشاہدہ کے مانند کبھی نہیں ہو سکتی اور لوگوں پر آسانی پیدا کرنے کے لئے شمس الائمہ سری نے بھی حضرت امام ابو یوسف کے قول کو اختیار کیا ہے۔
He said: It is obligatory for the scribe to read the letter to them so that they know what is in it, or to inform them of it, because there is no testimony without knowledge. Then he should seal it in their presence and hand it over to them so that no alteration is suspected. This is according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, because knowledge of the content of the letter and sealing in their presence is a condition, and similarly preserving the content of the letter is a condition according to them. For this reason, the scribe gives them another unsealed letter to assist their memory. Abu Yusuf later said that none of this is a condition; the condition is that he makes them witness that this is his letter and his seal. And it is narrated from Abu Yusuf that sealing is also not a condition. He made things easy in this matter when he was afflicted with the office of judge, and news is not like direct observation. Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi chose the opinion of Abu Yusuf. Translation: It is obligatory for the scribe to read the letter to the witnesses so that they become aware of its content, or to inform them of the content himself, because testimony without knowledge is not valid. Then in their presence he should affix a seal and hand over that letter to them so that there is no suspicion of alteration. This is according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) because knowledge of the content of the letter and sealing in the presence of the witnesses are conditions, and similarly preserving the content of the letter is a condition according to them. For this reason, the scribe gives them another unsealed letter to assist their memory. Imam Abu Yusuf later stated that none of these things are conditions; rather the condition is that he makes them witness that this is his letter and his seal. And it is narrated from Imam Abu Yusuf that sealing is also not a condition. So Imam Abu Yusuf made ease in this matter when he himself was afflicted with the office of judge. And news is not like direct observation. Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi chose the opinion of Imam Abu Yusuf. Explanation: Sahib al-Quduri said: Whatever testimony and such the scribe wrote in his letter, the scribe should read the entire content of the letter to the witnesses or inform them of the content without reading, because if the witnesses are not aware of the content, their testimony will be without knowledge, and testifying without knowledge is void. As Allah Almighty says: 'Except those who bear witness to the truth while they know' (Quran 43:86). This verse indicates that knowledge is necessary for the witness regarding what he testifies about. In any case, when the scribe reads the letter before the witnesses or informs them of its content, then in their presence he seals it and according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) hands over this letter to the witnesses. According to Imam Abu Yusuf, he hands it over to the plaintiff. Sealing is so that there is no doubt of alteration or change in the content. Sahib al-Hidayah says: Informing the witnesses of the content of the letter, sealing it in their presence, and the witnesses bearing the content from the time of testimony to the time of performance is a condition according to the two. Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Ahmad are also of this view, and one narration from Imam Malik is also the same. Since it is a condition that the witnesses remember the content of the judge's letter, it is said that the scribe should give them another unsealed letter so that they can look at it and remember the content. Accordingly, if any of the matters mentioned in the letter is forgotten by the witnesses at the time of testimony, according to the two, the judge to whom the letter is written will not accept that letter. The first opinion of Imam Abu Yusuf is like that of the two. But Imam Abu Yusuf's later opinion is that it is not a condition that the witnesses be aware of the content or that they remember the content; rather the only condition is that he makes them witness that this is his letter and his seal. This is also one narration from Imam Malik. So if the witnesses testify before the receiving judge that this is the scribe's letter and his seal, it will be sufficient. And one narration from Imam Abu Yusuf is that sealing is also not a condition. Sahib al-Hidayah said: Imam Abu Yusuf made these easings when he himself assumed the office of qada. So what Imam Abu Yusuf said after experience and observation is more correct, because news can never be like direct observation, and to create ease for people, Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi also chose the opinion of Imam Abu Yusuf.
Source pages p. 286

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute on the procedure for a judge's scribe (katib) when sending a letter with testimony to another judge. The core ruling: The scribe must ensure the witnesses know the content of the letter and see it sealed to prevent tampering. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (al-Shaybani) require that the scribe read the letter to the witnesses or inform them of its content, then seal it in their presence, and hand it over to them. They also require the witnesses to memorize the content, so the scribe gives them an extra copy (unsealed) to help memory. Abu Yusuf initially agreed but later simplified: only the witnesses' testimony that the letter and seal are the scribe's is sufficient; no need for them to know the content or seal in their presence, and sealing itself may not be required. The reason for Abu Yusuf's change: his experience as a judge showed that strict conditions cause hardship, and news (khabar) from witnesses about the seal is not the same as direct observation (mu'ayana) – but easier. The text quotes the Quranic verse (43:86) to emphasize knowledge is necessary for testimony. The commentary explains that all conditions are to prevent suspicion of alteration. Al-Sarakhsi preferred Abu Yusuf's final view for ease. The practical effect: under the stricter view (Abu Hanifa & Muhammad), if witnesses forget any detail, the letter is rejected; under Abu Yusuf's view, the letter is accepted if witnesses simply confirm the letter and seal are authentic, without needing to recall content.

Key Terms
ختم (khatm): The act of sealing a letter to prevent tampering; a disputed condition.
شهادة (shahada): Testimony; here it refers to witnesses testifying about the scribe's letter and seal.
قاضی کا تب (qadi ka katib): The scribe of the judge who writes the letter to another judge.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) The witnesses must testify that this is the scribe's letter and seal.
D) The witnesses must memorize the content of the letter.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school offers a stricter and a lenient view on witness testimony for a scribe's letter; the mufta bihi opinion is the lenient one for ease.

Qada — Judiciary
intermediate

Conditions for Witnesses of a Judge's Letter: Abu Hanifa vs. Abu Yusuf
Explains conditions for witnesses of a judge's letter and Abu Yusuf's relaxed view

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the positions of the two (Abu Hanifa & Muhammad) and Abu Yusuf regarding the conditions for witnesses of a judge's letter, and state the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Abu Yusuf's experience as a judge led him to relax the conditions: only witnessing the letter and seal suffices.

This passage from the Hidayah addresses a practical problem in judicial administration: what conditions must witnesses fulfill when they carry a judge's letter (khatt al-qadi) to another judge? The answer affects the ease of enforcing judgments across jurisdictions. The text presents a split within the Hanafi school between the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) and Abu Yusuf, with the latter's later opinion gaining preference for its practicality.

Guided Path
1
State the positions of the two and Abu Yusuf
Identify the conditions required by Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (the 'two') versus the conditions in Abu Yusuf's later opinion. The two require witnesses to know the content, be present at sealing, and retain the content until testimony. Abu Yusuf only requires witnessing the letter and seal.
Abu Yusuf's first opinion agreed with the two, but his final opinion was relaxed.
2
Identify the opposing schools and their view
Note that Imam al-Shafi'i, Imam Ahmad, and one narration of Imam Malik agree with the two (requiring knowledge of content). Another narration of Malik agrees with Abu Yusuf.
This shows the dispute crosses school boundaries.
3
Examine the evidence for each position
The two rely on analogy to testimony upon testimony (shahada 'ala al-shahada) to prevent fraud. Abu Yusuf relies on practical experience: the seal is a sufficient guarantee, and requiring content knowledge causes hardship.
Al-Hidayah notes that news can never equal observation.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The author of al-Hidayah and Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi adopt Abu Yusuf's later opinion because it is based on direct judicial experience and facilitates the process for people.
This preference is the mufta bihi position.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Under the two's view, witnesses must remember the content; if they forget any part, the letter is rejected. Under Abu Yusuf's view, they only need to testify that the letter and seal belong to the judge, making the process simpler.
Practical impact: easier enforcement of judgments across jurisdictions.

The Book of the Etiquette of the Judge. Ashraf al-Hidayah volume... And according to Imam Abu Yusuf, he should hand it over to the plaintiff. And putting a seal and stamping it is so that there remains no doubt of alteration and change in the content. The author of al-Hidayah states: Informing the witnesses of the content of the letter, sealing it in their presence, and the witnesses' retention of the content of the letter from the time of bearing witness until the time of testimony is a condition according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad). Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Ahmad are also of this view, and one narration from Imam Malik is the same. Since the witnesses remembering the content of the judge's letter is a condition, it is said that the writing judge should give another unsealed letter to the witnesses so that they may repeatedly look at it and remember the content. Thus, if any of the matters mentioned in the letter is forgotten by the witnesses at the time of testimony, according to the two, the receiving judge will not accept this letter. Abu Hanifa's first opinion is also like the two. However, Abu Yusuf's final opinion is that the witnesses' knowledge of the letter's content and their remembering it are not conditions. Rather, the only condition is that he makes them witness that this is my letter and my seal. This is also one narration from Imam Malik. Thus, if the witnesses testify before the receiving judge that this is the writing judge's letter and his seal, it will be sufficient. And from Abu Yusuf there is one narration that sealing and stamping is also not a condition. The author of al-Hidayah said: Abu Yusuf made these concessions when he himself assumed the office of judgeship. So what Abu Yusuf said after experience and observation is more correct, because news can never be like observation. And for making things easy for people, Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi also adopted the opinion of Abu Yusuf.
Source pages p. 287

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the conditions for witnesses who witness a judge's letter (khatt al-qadi). The text presents the ruling from the Hidayah and then explains the differences. The author of Hidayah (Al-Marghinani) states that according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani), the witnesses must be informed of the content of the letter, be present at its sealing, and retain the content from the time of bearing testimony until the time of delivering testimony. This is also the position of Imam al-Shafi'i, Imam Ahmad, and one narration from Imam Malik. To ensure retention, it is recommended that the writing judge give the witnesses an unsealed copy to review. If a witness forgets part of the content, the letter is not accepted. However, Abu Yusuf's final view, based on his practical experience as a judge, relaxes these conditions: only witnessing that the letter and seal belong to the judge is required; knowledge of the content is unnecessary. One narration also dispenses with the seal. The Hidayah comments that Abu Yusuf's view is more correct because it is based on direct experience, and Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi also adopted it for ease.

Key Terms
خط (khatt): A written judgment or letter from one judge to another.
مہر (mohr): Seal of the judge, used to authenticate the letter.
شہادت علی الشہادہ (shahada 'ala al-shahada): Testimony upon testimony, where a secondary witness (shahid al-far') transmits the testimony of the primary witness (shahid al-asl).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Yusuf's later opinion, what is the only condition for witnesses of a judge's letter?
A) They must know the entire content of the letter.
B) They must be present when the letter is sealed.
C) They must witness that the letter and seal belong to the judge.
D) They must memorize the letter word for word.

Key Takeaway
Abu Yusuf's later opinion, adopted by al-Hidayah and Sarakhsi for ease, only requires witnesses to testify that the letter and seal are the judge's.

Qada — Judiciary
intermediate
8 min
Procedure for the Receiving Judge: Accepting the Letter and Checking the Seal
Explains the procedure for the receiving judge to accept and open the letter in the presence of the defendant and witnesses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the procedure for the receiving judge to accept a judge's letter, explain the requirement of defendant's presence using qiyas, and distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa/Muhammad and Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
Accepting a judge's letter is like performing testimony – the defendant must be present, unless you follow Abu Yusuf.

This passage from Al-Hidayah explains the detailed procedure when a judge receives a written testimony from another judge. The central ruling is that the receiving judge must not accept the letter except in the presence of the defendant (khasm). The text provides two strong analogical proofs and also records a difference of opinion within the Hanafi school. Understanding this procedure is essential for grasping how judicial correspondence works in Hanafi law and the importance of the presence of the litigant at key procedural steps.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the receiving judge accepting the letter. The ruling: he must not accept it except in the presence of the defendant, because it is equivalent to ada' al-shahada (performance of testimony).
2
Examine the first proof: qiyas to ada' al-shahada
The acceptance of the letter is likened to the performance of testimony. Just as a defendant must be present when witnesses testify, so must he be present when the letter is presented.
Asl: ada' al-shahada; Far': qabul al-kitab; Illa: both involve making testimony count against the defendant.
3
Examine the second proof: qiyas to shahada 'ala al-shahada
The letter is analogous to testimony upon testimony, where the defendant must be present when the secondary testimony is heard. Here, the writing judge transmits witness statements via the letter.
The writing judge acts like a secondary witness (shahid far').
4
Contrast with the writing judge's hearing
The writing judge hears witnesses without the defendant because his role is only transmission (naql), not judgment (hukm). This distinction reinforces the rule for the receiving judge, whose role is judgment.
The writing judge's hearing is like tahammul al-shahada (bearing testimony), which does not require the opponent's presence.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Yusuf holds that the defendant's presence is not required at acceptance, only at judgment. Understand the thamarah al-khilaf: practical difference in procedure.
Under Abu Yusuf, the judge can accept the letter privately and summon the defendant later for judgment.
