When will the receiving judge accept the letter? He said: When it reaches the judge, he shall not accept it except in the presence of the opponent, because it is equivalent to the performance of testimony, so his presence is necessary. Unlike the hearing of the writing judge, because it is for transmission, not for judgment. Translation: Then when this letter reaches the receiving judge, he shall not accept it except in the presence of the defendant, because this letter is in the rank of performing testimony. Therefore, the presence of the defendant is necessary. Unlike the writing judge's hearing, because this testimony is for transmission, not for judgment. Explanation: The author of al-Quduri says: When the writing judge's letter reaches the receiving judge, the receiving judge should accept the letter in the presence of the defendant. That is, upon the defendant's presence, he takes the letter from the plaintiff or the witnesses. The proof is that this letter is in the rank of performing testimony before the receiving judge. And at the time of performing testimony, the presence of the defendant is necessary. Therefore, at the time of accepting this letter, the presence of the defendant will also be necessary. A second proof is that this letter of the writing judge is in the rank of testimony upon testimony. Because the writing judge, through his letter, transmits the words of the witnesses to the receiving judge, just as a secondary witness transmits the words of the primary witness's testimony. And for hearing testimony upon testimony, the presence of the defendant is necessary. Therefore, here too, at the time of accepting the judge's letter, the presence of the defendant will be necessary. On the contrary, when the writing judge hears testimony from the witnesses, at the time of his hearing, the presence of the defendant is not a condition. Thus, if the writing judge hears the testimony of the plaintiff's witnesses in the absence of the defendant, it is permissible, because the writing judge's hearing is not for giving judgment, but rather for transmitting the words of the testimony. So the writing judge's hearing of the plaintiff's witnesses is like the secondary witness's hearing of the primary witness's testimony and his action to transmit it. And at the time of the secondary witness's bearing testimony, the presence of the defendant is not a condition. Therefore, here too, when the writing judge heard the plaintiff's witnesses, the presence of the defendant will not be a condition. In the commentary of al-Quduri by Aqta', it is stated that according to Imam Abu Yusuf, the receiving judge can accept the writing judge's letter even in the absence of the defendant. That is, according to Imam Abu Yusuf, the presence of the defendant at the time of accepting the letter is not a condition, because the letter pertains to the receiving judge. Therefore, the receiving judge will not need anyone's presence to accept it. However, afterwards when he gives judgment based on the letter, then the presence of the defendant is necessary so that judgment against an absent person does not occur. The receiving judge should check the seal of the letter in the presence of the witnesses. He said: Then when the witnesses hand it over to him, he looks at its seal. Then when they testify that it is the letter of so-and-so judge, he handed it to us in his court of judgment and ruling, and read it to us, and sealed it, then the judge opens it and reads it to the opponent and makes binding what is in it. This is according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf said: When they testify that it is his letter and his seal, he accepts it as has passed. And for opening the letter, the appearance of the witnesses' probity is not made a condition. And the correct view is that he opens the letter after establishing probity, as mentioned by al-Khassaf, because he may need additional witnesses, and they can only perform testimony after the seal is broken. And he only accepts it if the writer is in the position of a judge. So if he dies, is removed, or is no longer qualified for judgeship before the letter arrives, he does not accept it, because he has become one of the subjects. For this reason, he does not accept another judge's letter in a matter outside his jurisdiction or outside both jurisdictions. Likewise, if the recipient dies, unless he wrote to so-and-so son of so-and-so, the judge of such city, and to every Muslim judge who receives it, because the others are his followers and he is known. Unlike what is written to his heir, because he stands in his place. If he writes initially to everyone who receives it, according to our scholars, because he is not known. And if the opponent dies, it is executed. Then, (in the presence of the defendant) when the witnesses hand over this letter to the receiving judge, the receiving judge checks its seal. Then when the witnesses testify that this letter is of such judge, he gave it to us in his court of judgment and ruling, and read it to us, and sealed it, then the receiving judge opens it and reads it to the defendant and makes binding what is in it. This is according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf said: When they testify that it is his letter and his seal, he accepts it as has passed. And for opening the letter, the appearance of the witnesses' probity is not made a condition. And the correct view is that...
Source pages p. 287

Commentary
This passage details the procedure for the receiving judge (al-qadi al-maktub ilayhi) when he receives a letter from another judge. The ruling is that he must not accept the letter except in the presence of the defendant (khasm), because accepting the letter is equivalent to the performance of testimony (ada' al-shahada). Just as in a normal trial, the defendant must be present when witnesses testify, so too here the defendant must be present when the letter is presented. The text provides two proofs: (1) The letter is like performing testimony, so the defendant must be present. (2) The letter is analogous to testimony upon testimony (shahada 'ala al-shahada), where the defendant must be present when the secondary testimony is heard. However, the writing judge (al-qadi al-katib) does not need the defendant's presence when he first hears the witnesses, because his role is only transmission, not judgment. The text also notes that according to Abu Yusuf, the receiving judge may accept the letter even without the defendant's presence at the time of acceptance, but the defendant must be present when judgment is later pronounced. Then the text discusses the procedure for opening the letter. The witnesses hand over the letter to the receiving judge, who checks the seal. Then the witnesses testify that it is the letter of a specific judge, that he gave it in his court, read it to them, and sealed it. At that point, according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, the judge opens it and reads it to the defendant, making the contents binding. Abu Yusuf simplifies: if the witnesses testify that it is the judge's letter and seal, that suffices. The text also addresses conditions: the writing judge must have been a judge at the time of writing; if he dies or is removed before the letter arrives, it is not accepted. Similarly, if the recipient judge dies, the letter is not accepted unless it was addressed to him generically. The opponent's death does not prevent execution.

Key Terms
مکتوب الیہ (al-maktub ilayhi): The judge to whom the letter is written; the receiving judge.
اداء الشہادہ (ada' al-shahada): The performance of testimony before a judge, as opposed to bearing testimony (tahammul al-shahada).
شہادۃ علی الشہادۃ (shahada 'ala al-shahada): Testimony upon testimony, where a secondary witness transmits the testimony of the primary witness.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary analogy used to require the defendant's presence when the receiving judge accepts the letter?
A) Analogy to a contract (aqd)
B) Analogy to performance of testimony (ada' al-shahada)
C) Analogy to an oath (yamin)
D) Analogy to a sale (bay')

Key Takeaway
The receiving judge must accept the judge's letter in the presence of the defendant, because it is equivalent to the performance of testimony; this rule is derived by qiyas and is subject to an intra-Hanafi difference.

Qada — Judiciary
intermediate
10 min
Acceptance of a Judge's Letter: Procedure and Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Explains conditions for accepting a judge's letter and intra-Hanafi disputes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for accepting a judge's letter in Hanafi fiqh and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the required testimony and witnesses' justice.

Core Idea
A judge's letter is accepted only if its authenticity is verified; Hanafi imams differ on whether detailed testimony or mere seal suffices.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah explains the procedure for a judge to accept a letter from another judge, focusing on the conditions and the dispute between Abu Hanifa/Muhammad and Abu Yusuf on the sufficiency of testimony and the necessity of witnesses' justice. The ruling impacts how judicial correspondence is handled in practice, balancing authenticity and efficiency.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what legal act is being discussed — accepting a judge's letter (kitab al-qadi) — and its permissibility under conditions.
The ruling is not simply 'valid' but depends on fulfilling specific conditions.
2
Distinguish between hearing testimony and accepting the letter
Note that the passage first discusses the deputy judge's hearing of testimony: defendant presence is not required for mere transmission. Then apply this to the letter: Abu Yusuf extends this to letter acceptance.
The analogy of secondary witness (shahid far') is key.
3
State the procedure according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad
List the detailed requirements: witnesses must testify that the letter is from the specific judge, was handed in his court, recited, and sealed.
This is the more stringent position.
4
State Abu Yusuf's position
Abu Yusuf requires only testimony that the letter and seal belong to the sender; no further details needed.
He views the seal as sufficient authentication.
5
Identify the second dispute: witnesses' justice
Al-Quduri did not require investigation of witnesses' justice before opening, but al-Hidayah and al-Khassaf require it to prevent need for additional witnesses later.
The mufta bihi is to open after establishing justice.
6
Determine the mufta bihi
The preferred (sahih) view is that of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: detailed testimony and verification of witnesses' justice before opening.
This is supported by al-Hidayah and al-Khassaf.

Book of the Judge. For hearing testimony, the presence of the defendant is necessary. Therefore, here too, when accepting the judge's letter, the presence of the defendant is required. In contrast, when the deputy judge hears testimony from witnesses, the presence of the defendant at the time of hearing is not a condition. Thus, if the deputy judge hears the plaintiff's witnesses in the absence of the defendant, it is permissible. Because the deputy judge's hearing is not to give a verdict, but rather to transmit the words of testimony. So the deputy judge hearing the plaintiff's witnesses is like a secondary witness hearing the testimony of the primary witness and acting upon it, i.e., to transmit it. And for the secondary witness to bear testimony, the presence of the defendant is not a condition. Hence here too, when the deputy judge hears the plaintiff's witnesses, the defendant's presence is not a condition. In the commentary of Quduri, it is stated that according to Imam Abu Yusuf, the judge to whom the letter is written (maktub ilayh) can accept the letter of the deputy judge even in the absence of the defendant. That is, according to Imam Abu Yusuf, the presence of the defendant at the time of accepting the letter is not a condition. Because the letter pertains to the judge maktub ilayh. Therefore, the judge maktub ilayh does not need anyone's presence to accept it. Yes, later when he gives a verdict based on the letter, then the presence of the defendant is necessary so that judgment against an absent person does not occur. The judge maktub ilayh shall examine the seal of the letter in the presence of witnesses. He said: So when the witnesses hand it over to him, he looks at its seal. So when they testify that it is the letter of such-and-such a judge, he handed it to us in his court of judgment and adjudication, recited it to us, and sealed it, then the judge opens it and reads it to the opponent and enforces what is in it. This is according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. And Abu Yusuf said: When they testify that it is his letter and his seal, he accepts it as previously mentioned. And he did not stipulate the appearance of justice (of witnesses) for opening. And the correct view is that he opens the letter after the establishment of justice. Thus al-Khassaf mentioned it. Because sometimes there is need for additional witnesses, and they can only perform testimony after the seal is intact. And the maktub ilayh only accepts it if the writer (the original judge) is in his office of judgment. So if he died, was dismissed, or was no longer fit for judgment before the letter arrived, he does not accept it, because he has become one of the subjects. Hence, another judge does not accept his information outside his jurisdiction or outside both jurisdictions. Similarly, if the maktub ilayh dies, except when he wrote to such-and-such, the judge of such town, and to every judge of the Muslims who receives it, because the other became a follower of him, and he is known. In contrast to when he wrote initially to everyone who receives it, according to our scholars, because he is not known. And if the opponent dies, it is executed upon his heir because the heir stands in his place. Then when the witnesses handed the letter to the judge maktub ilayh, he examines its seal. Then when the witnesses testify that this is the letter of such-and-such a judge, he handed it to us in his court of judgment and adjudication, recited it to us, affixed it and sealed it, then the judge maktub ilayh opens it, reads it to the defendant, and enforces whatever is in it upon him. This is according to Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad. And Imam Abu Yusuf said that when the witnesses testify that this is his letter and his seal, he accepts it, as previously mentioned. And for opening the letter, the appearance of the witnesses' justice is not stipulated. But the correct view is that he opens after the appearance of justice. Thus Imam al-Khassaf mentioned it. Because sometimes there is need for additional witnesses, and to perform testimony is only possible when the seal is intact. And the judge maktub ilayh accepts this letter only when the judge (the writer) is in his office. Even if he died, was dismissed, or was no longer fit for judgment before the letter arrived, the judge maktub ilayh will not accept it. Because he became one of the subjects. For this reason, another judge will not accept his report outside his jurisdiction or outside both jurisdictions. Similarly, if the judge maktub ilayh died, except when he wrote: To so-and-so son of so-and-so, the judge of such town, and to every judge of the Muslims who receives it, because the other becomes his follower, and he is known. Contrary to the case when he wrote initially to every judge who receives it, according to what our scholars hold. Because he is not known. And if the defendant died, the judge maktub ilayh will execute the letter on his heir because the heir stands in his place. Sahib al-Quduri explained that when in the presence of the defendant, the witnesses or the plaintiff gave this letter of the judge to the judge maktub ilayh, then the judge maktub ilayh first examines its seal. Then when the witnesses testify that this is the letter of such-and-such a judge of such town, he gave us this letter in his court, read it to us, sealed it with a seal in our presence, then the judge maktub ilayh opens that letter, reads it to the defendant, and enforces what is written in it upon the defendant, provided that in the opinion of the judge maktub ilayh, the written judgment and testimony of the judge (the writer) are in accordance with the Islamic law. And the defendant has no proof against it. Sahib al-Hidayah says that all the mentioned matters are the madhhab of the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad). Otherwise, the madhhab of Imam Abu Yusuf has passed earlier that testimony only that this is the letter of such judge and this is his seal is sufficient. After such testimony, it is permissible for the judge maktub ilayh to accept the letter. The rest of the mentioned matters are not conditions. Thus it was said earlier: Abu Yusuf said: 'None of that is a condition; the condition is that they testify that this is his letter and his seal.' Handed over. Sahib al-Hidayah says that Shaykh Abul Hasan al-Quduri in his book Mukhtasar al-Quduri did not mention the condition of establishing the witnesses' justice for opening the letter. That is, he did not say: 'The judge maktub ilayh investigates the justice of the witnesses and then opens the letter.' Rather, he only said: 'When the witnesses testify that this is the letter of such judge, he gave it to us in the court, read it to us, and sealed it with his seal in our presence, then the judge maktub ilayh opens it.' This indicates that according to Sahib al-Quduri, for opening the letter, investigating the witnesses' justice and its appearance is not a condition. Rather, without the appearance of justice, the judge maktub ilayh may open the letter. Sahib al-Hidayah says: 'Not so. Rather, the correct view is that the judge maktub ilayh opens after the appearance of the witnesses' justice.' That is, for opening the letter, the appearance of the witnesses' justice is a condition. Thus Imam al-Khassaf mentioned it. Because the witnesses who saw the letter, due to the non-appearance of their justice, sometimes the plaintiff needs additional witnesses. In such a way that the defendant...

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah is an expansion of the rulings from al-Hidayah regarding the acceptance of a judge's letter (kitab al-qadi). The passage begins by establishing a general principle: for hearing testimony, the presence of the defendant is required. However, when a deputy judge (qadi na'ib) hears testimony merely to transmit it to the main judge, the defendant's presence is not needed, analogous to a secondary witness (shahid far') hearing testimony from a primary witness (shahid asl). The author then applies this to the letter: when the deputy judge writes a letter to the main judge (maktub ilayh), the defendant's presence at the time of the letter's acceptance is not required according to Imam Abu Yusuf, because the letter belongs to the maktub ilayh; but when the verdict is given based on the letter, the defendant must be present to avoid judgment against an absent person (qada' 'ala al-gha'ib). The passage then details the procedure: the maktub ilayh examines the seal, requires witnesses to testify that it is the letter of the specific judge and was given in his court, etc. A key intra-Hanafi dispute is presented: Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad require detailed testimony (including that the letter was recited and sealed in the witnesses' presence), while Abu Yusuf holds that testimony that it is the judge's letter and his seal is sufficient. Furthermore, there is disagreement on whether the justice ('adalah) of the witnesses must be established before opening the letter. Al-Quduri seemingly did not require it, but al-Hidayah and al-Khassaf insist it is necessary, because the plaintiff may need additional witnesses if the original witnesses' justice is questionable. The passage also covers scenarios where the original judge dies or is dismissed before the letter arrives (letter is invalid), and if the recipient judge dies (unless the letter is addressed generally to all judges). If the defendant dies, the letter is executed on his heir.

Key Terms
مکتوب الیہ (maktub ilayh): The judge to whom a letter is written by another judge.
قاضی کاتب (qadi katib): The judge who writes the letter (the original judge).
عدالت ('adalah): Justice; the quality of being upright and trustworthy, necessary for witnesses.
تحمل شہادت (tahammul al-shahada): Bearing/undertaking testimony; the act of receiving testimony to transmit it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Hidayah, what is the correct condition for opening a judge's letter?
A) The letter can be opened immediately upon receipt.
B) The letter can be opened only after the witnesses' justice is established.
C) The letter can be opened only if the defendant is present.
D) The letter can be opened only if the original judge is alive.

Key Takeaway
A judge's letter is authenticated through witnesses; the Hanafi school's preferred view requires their justice to be verified before opening.

Conditions for Accepting a Judge's Letter: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Witness Integrity
Intra-Hanafi dispute on witnessing conditions for judicial letters

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the majority Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) and Abu Yusuf's alternative, and explain the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) of their disagreement.

Core Idea
The receiving judge must verify both the seal and the witnesses' integrity; Abu Yusuf only requires testimony about the seal.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah addresses a crucial procedural question in Islamic judicial administration: when one judge sends a written decision to another judge, what conditions must be met for the receiving judge to accept and enforce it? The text presents a detailed procedure from al-Quduri and then reveals a significant intra-Hanafi disagreement. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to analyse how different juristic priorities – caution vs. efficiency – shape legal procedures.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
What is the core procedural act being discussed? The acceptance of a letter (kitab) from one judge by another. What conditions are required for that acceptance?
2
State the majority Hanafi position
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, describe the conditions that must be fulfilled: detailed testimony, witnesses' probity, seal intact, etc.
These are outlined in Quduri's description and affirmed by al-Hidayah.
3
Identify Abu Yusuf's opposing view
Abu Yusuf holds that only testimony that 'this is the letter and seal of the judge' is sufficient; no further conditions are needed.
This is a more lenient and efficient position.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response to Abu Yusuf
Why do the majority insist on witness integrity? The text gives a practical reason: if the defendant challenges the witnesses, additional witnesses may be needed, and their testimony requires the seal to be intact. Thus, the seal must be preserved, which is only possible if the witnesses are trustworthy.
This is a form of defensive procedural design.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Under the majority view, the receiving judge must investigate the witnesses' probity before opening the letter, delaying acceptance. Under Abu Yusuf's view, acceptance is quicker but the ability to later challenge the witnesses is compromised.
The mufta bihi is the majority view for its caution.

[The letter] should be opened after [the witnesses'] integrity becomes apparent. Similarly, Imam Khasaf mentioned it. Because sometimes additional witnesses are needed; the testimony of the additional witnesses will be possible only when the seal is intact. And the addressee judge will accept this letter only when the writing judge is present in his office of qada. So much so that if before the letter arrives he dies or is dismissed or is no longer qualified for qada, the addressee judge will not accept his letter. Because he becomes one of the subjects, and for that reason another judge will not accept his notification in a territory outside his jurisdiction or outside both jurisdictions. Similarly, if the addressee judge dies, unless he wrote: 'To the judge of such city, so-and-so son of so-and-so, and to every person among Muslim judges whom this letter reaches', because the addressee becomes subordinate to the non-addressee even though the non-addressee is known. Contrary to the case when he initially wrote: 'To every judge whom this letter reaches' on the basis on which our shuyukh are, because it is not well-known. And if the defendant dies, the addressee judge will enforce this letter against his inheritor because his inheritor stands in his place. Explanation: Sahib al-Quduri said: When in the presence of the defendant the witnesses or the plaintiff bring this letter of the judge to the addressee judge, then the addressee judge should first examine its seal. Then when the witnesses testify that 'This is the letter of so-and-so son of so-and-so, the judge of such city; he handed this letter to us in his court, read it out to us, put his seal on it in our presence and sealed it', then the addressee judge should open the letter, read it to the defendant, and enforce whatever is written in the letter against the defendant, provided that in the opinion of the addressee judge the writing judge's decision and testimony conform to Islamic law, and the defendant has no proof against it. Sahib al-Hidayah says: All the mentioned matters are the madhhab of the two sides (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad). Otherwise, the madhhab of Qadi Abu Yusuf has passed earlier that only the testimony that 'This is the letter of such judge and this is his seal' is sufficient. After such testimony, it is permissible for the addressee judge to accept the letter. None of the mentioned matters are conditions. Thus it was said earlier: Abu Yusuf said, 'Lastly, none of that is a condition; the condition is that they testify that this is his letter and his seal.' Handed over. Sahib al-Hidayah says: Shaykh Abu al-Hasan al-Quduri in his book Mukhtasar al-Quduri did not mention the condition of the witnesses' integrity for opening the letter; that is, he did not say: 'The addressee judge should investigate the witnesses' integrity and then open the letter.' Rather he only said: 'When the witnesses testify that this is the letter of such judge, he handed it to us in his court, read it to us, and put his seal on it in our presence, then the addressee judge should open the letter.' From this it appears that in the view of Sahib al-Quduri, investigating the witnesses' integrity and having their probity become apparent is not a condition for opening the letter. Rather, without probity becoming apparent, the addressee judge may open the letter. Sahib al-Hidayah says: This is not so. Rather the correct view is that the addressee judge [opens] after the witnesses' probity becomes apparent; that is, for opening the letter, the witnesses' probity becoming apparent is a condition. Similarly, Imam Khasaf mentioned it. Because the witnesses who testified to the letter, if their probity is not apparent, sometimes the plaintiff needs additional witnesses. For example, the defendant casts aspersions and objections on these witnesses and says: 'Bring additional other witnesses.' Then for these additional witnesses, giving testimony will be possible only when the seal is present. Because the additional witnesses will testify that 'This is the letter of such judge and his seal.' And this testimony can be given only when the seal is present; otherwise, if the seal is broken, how can they testify that this is the seal of such judge?
Source pages p. 289

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah discusses the procedure and conditions for a judge (qadi maktub ilayhi) to accept a letter from another judge (qadi katib). The text begins mid-discussion, stating that the letter should be opened only after the witnesses' integrity (adalah) becomes apparent, a point attributed to Imam al-Khasaf. The reason given is practical: if additional witnesses are needed later, their testimony requires the seal to be intact. The writing judge must still be in office when the letter arrives; if he dies, is dismissed, or loses qualification before the letter reaches, the letter is not accepted because he becomes an ordinary subject. Exceptions are made if the letter is addressed to multiple judges or if the defendant dies (then it is enforced against the heir). The core of this lesson is the detailed procedure from Sahib al-Quduri's Mukhtasar: the receiving judge first checks the seal, then witnesses testify that the writing judge gave them the letter in his court and sealed it in their presence. The receiving judge then opens the letter, reads it to the defendant, and enforces its contents, provided the decision conforms to Islamic law and the defendant has no counterevidence. Al-Hidayah notes that this entire procedure is the madhhab of 'the two sides' (tarafayn), meaning Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani. Abu Yusuf holds a more lenient view: only testimony that 'this is the letter and seal of the judge' is sufficient; the additional conditions regarding witnesses' integrity and detailed witness statements are not required. Al-Hidayah then clarifies an apparent conflict: Sahib al-Quduri did not explicitly mention the condition of investigating the witnesses' integrity. Some might think he deems it unnecessary. But al-Hidayah insists that the correct position is that the witnesses' integrity must be known, as stated by al-Khasaf. The reason is that if the defendant challenges the witnesses, the plaintiff may need to bring additional witnesses. Those additional witnesses can only testify about the seal if it is still intact. Therefore, opening the letter without verifying the witnesses' integrity could undermine the ability to bring further proof. This passage thus presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Yusuf and the majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), with the latter requiring additional safeguards.

Key Terms
کتاب القاضی الی القاضی (kitab al-qadi ila al-qadi): A written judgment or notification sent by one judge to another judge concerning a legal case.
عدالت (adala): The probity or moral integrity of a witness, necessary for their testimony to be accepted.
طرفین (tarafayn): Here it refers to Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani (the two sides).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), what must be established before the receiving judge can accept a letter from another judge?
A) Only that the letter is sealed
B) That the witnesses testify in detail and their probity (adala) is known
C) That the writing judge is present in court
D) That the defendant admits the claim

Key Takeaway
The receiving judge must verify both the witnesses' probity and the seal before opening the letter, per the majority Hanafi view.

Qada — Judiciary

Death of the Writing Judge and the Validity of Kitab al-Qadi
Inter-madhhab dispute on acceptance of a judge's letter after the writer's death

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the validity of a judge's letter when the writing judge dies before it is read, and evaluate the opposing argument based on the analogy to shahada 'ala al-shahada.

Core Idea
A judge's letter is void if the writer dies before it is read—authority is not transferable by writing alone.

This passage from al-Hidayah addresses a critical procedural issue in Islamic judiciary: what happens to a written judgment if the judge who wrote it dies or becomes disqualified before the receiving judge can read it in court? The Hanafi school, represented by Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani, holds that the letter becomes void (batil). Abu Yusuf, however, agrees with the Shafi'i and Hanbali schools that the letter remains valid. Understanding this dispute reveals how different schools determine the moment when a judicial act is considered complete and binding, a matter with significant practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling from al-Hidayah: the addressee judge only accepts the letter if the writing judge is still in office at the time of reading. Death, dismissal, or loss of capacity before that renders the letter void.
2
Identify the opposing view and its basis
Note that Abu Yusuf (within the Hanafi school), Imam al-Shafi'i, and Imam Ahmad hold that the letter remains valid. Their key proof: kitab al-qadi is analogous to shahada 'ala al-shahada (testimony upon testimony).
3
Follow the opponent's proof (qiyas)
Understand the analogy: in shahada 'ala al-shahada, secondary witnesses testify before the writing judge, who records it. The transfer of testimony is completed by writing. If the secondary witnesses die after testifying but before judgment, the judge can still decide. Similarly, if the writing judge dies after writing, the letter should be valid.
This is a qiyas jaliy, so a qiyas panel will be constructed below.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response refutes the analogy: writing alone does not complete the transfer. The transfer is only complete when the letter reaches the receiving judge and is read to the defendant. Death before that is like death of secondary witnesses before they testify—no judgment can be given.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: under the Hanafi view, if the writing judge dies, many letters become void, potentially delaying justice. Under the opposing view, the letter remains executable, providing continuity.

صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا کہ قاضی مکتوب الیہ مذکورہ خط اس وقت قبول کرے گا جب کہ قاضی کا تب، منصب قضاء پر فائز ہو ۔ چنانچہ اگر قاضی کا تب مر گیا یا معزول کر دیا گیا یا جنون یا بیہوشی یا مرتد ہونے یا دار الحرب میں چلے جانے یا بعض حضرات کے نزدیک فسق کی وجہ سے اہمیت قضا سے خارج ہو گیا۔ حالانکہ ابھی تک خط قاضی مکتوب الیہ کے پاس نہیں پہنچا یا خط پہنچ تو گیا مگر قاضی مکتوب الیہ مدعی الیہ کو پڑھ کر نہیں سنایا تو یہ خط باطل ہو جائے گا۔ اور قاضی مکتوب الیہ اس کو قبول نہیں کرے گا۔ اور اس کے مطابق مدعی علیہ کے خلاف کوئی فیصلہ نہیں کرے گا حضرت امام ابو یوسف امام شافعی اور امام احمد نے فرمایا کہ قاضی مکتوب الیہ اس حال میں بھی خط کو قبول کر کے اُسی کے مطابق عمل کرے گا۔
ان حضرات کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ کتاب القاضی الی القاضی ، شہادت علی الشہادت کے مانند ہے۔ کیونکہ کتاب القاضی کے ذریعہ مکتوب الیہ کی طرف اُن گواہوں کی شہادت کو منتقل کیا جاتا ہے جن گواہوں نے قاضی کا تب کے پاس گواہی دی ہے اور گواہی نقل کرنا، کتاب لیے لکھنے سے مکمل ہو گیا ہے۔ پس خط پہنچنے سے پہلے قاضی کا تب کا مرنا یا اہمیت قضاء سے خارج ہونا ایسا ہے جیسے شہود فرع ادائے شہادت کے بعد فیصلہ سے پہلے مر گئے ہوں اور شہود فرع کا ادائے شہادت کے بعد قاضی کے فیصلہ دینے سے پہلے مر جانا قضائے قاضی کے لئے مانع نہیں ہوتا ، بلکہ قاضی ان کے مرنے کے بعد بھی ان کی شہادت علی الشہادت کی بنیاد پر فیصلہ دے گا۔ اسی طرح خط تحریر کر کے مہر وغیرہ لگانے کے بعد اگر قاضی کا تب مر گیا تو بھی قاضی مکتوب الیہ اس خط کو قبول کرے گا اور اس پر عمل کرے گا۔ لیکن ہماری طرف سے اس دلیل کا جواب یہ ہے کہ محض کتابت اور تحریر سے شہادت کو نقل کر نا مکمل نہیں ہوتا۔ بلکہ نقل شہادت اس وقت پورا ہوگا جب خط قاضی مکتوب الیہ کے پاس پہنچ جائے گا ۔ اور قاضی مکتوب الیہ اس کو مدعی علیہ کے سامنے پڑھ کر سنا دے ہیں قاضی مکتوب الیہ کے خط کو پڑھ کر سنانے سے پہلے قاضی کا تب کا مرجانا ایسا ہے جیسے شہود فرع ادائے شہادت سے پہلے مرجائیں۔ اور شہود فرع اگر ادائے شہادت سے پہلے مرجائیں تو قاضی کوئی فیصلہ نہیں دے گا۔ پس اسی طرح قاضی مکتوب الیہ کے خط پڑھ کر سنانے سے پہلے قاضی کا تب مر گیا یا قضاء کا اہل نہ رہا تو بھی قاضی مکتوب الیہ اس خط پر عمل نہیں کرے گا اور کوئی فیصلہ نہ دے گا۔
خط قبول نہ ہونے پر طرفین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ قاضی مکتوب الیہ کے خط پڑھ کر سنانے سے پہلے اگر قاضی کا تب مر گیا یا معزول ہو گیا یا جنون وغیرہ کی وجہ سے اہلیت قضاء سے خارج ہو گیا تو وہ رعایا میں سے ایک شخص ہو گیا یعنی عام آدمی کی طرح ہو گیا اور جب قاضی کا تب حاکم نہ رہا بلکہ عام آدمی ہو گیا تو خط کے ذریعہ اس کا فیصلہ اور حکم بھی نافذ نہ ہوگا کیونکہ عام آدمی کا کوئی فیصلہ نافذ نہیں ہوتا۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ اگر ایک قاضی نے دوسرے قاضی کو اپنے ولایت قضاء کے علاوہ دوسرے شہر میں کوئی خبر دی مثلاً یہ کہا کہ فلاں شخص کا فلاں شخص پر حق ثابت ہے تو اُس دوسرے شہر کا قاضی محض اس خبر پر فیصلہ نہ دے گا۔ کیونکہ خبر دینے والا قاضی اپنی ولایت قضاء کے علاوہ دوسرے شہر میں ایک عام آدمی کی طرح ہے اور محض ایک عام آدمی کی خبر پر فیصلہ نہیں دیا جا تا۔ لہذ امذ کورہ قاضی کی خبر پر بھی فیصلہ نہ دیا جائے گا۔ اسی طرح اگر دو قاضی ایسے شہر میں جمع ہو گئے جو دونوں کی ولایت قضاء سے باہر ہے اور ان میں سے ایک
Sahib al-Hidayah said: The addressee judge will accept the mentioned letter only when the writing judge is still holding the office of qada. So if the writing judge dies, or is dismissed, or loses qualification for qada due to insanity, unconsciousness, apostasy, going to dar al-harb, or according to some, fisq, while the letter has not yet reached the addressee judge, or it has reached but the addressee judge has not read it to the defendant, then this letter becomes void. The addressee judge will not accept it and will not pass judgment against the defendant accordingly. Hadrat Imam Abu Yusuf, Imam al-Shafi'i, and Imam Ahmad said: The addressee judge will accept the letter even in this situation and act accordingly. Their proof is that kitab al-qadi ila al-qadi is like shahada 'ala al-shahada (testimony upon testimony). Because by means of kitab al-qadi, the testimony of the witnesses who testified before the writing judge is transferred to the addressee. And the transfer of testimony is completed by writing the book. So the writing judge's death before the letter arrives or his becoming disqualified is like the secondary witnesses dying after their testimony but before the judge's decision. The death of secondary witnesses after giving testimony but before the judge's decision does not prevent the judge from judging; rather, the judge will give judgment based on their shahada 'ala al-shahada even after their death. Similarly, after writing the letter and putting the seal etc., if the writing judge dies, the addressee judge will accept the letter and act upon it. But our (Hanafi) response to this proof is that merely writing and composition does not complete the transfer of testimony. Rather, the transfer of testimony is completed only when the letter reaches the addressee judge and he reads it to the defendant. The writing judge's death before the addressee judge reads the letter is like the secondary witnesses dying before giving testimony. If the secondary witnesses die before giving testimony, the judge will not give judgment. So similarly, if before the addressee judge reads the letter, the writing judge dies or becomes unqualified for qada, the addressee judge will not act upon this letter and will not give judgment. The proof of the two sides (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) for not accepting the letter is that if before the addressee judge reads the letter, the writing judge dies or is disqualified due to insanity etc., he becomes one of the subjects, i.e., an ordinary person. When the writing judge is no longer a ruler but an ordinary person, his judgment and order through the letter will not be enforceable because an ordinary person's judgment is not enforceable. This is why if a judge gives information to another judge about a matter outside his own jurisdiction, e.g., he says that such person has a right against such person, the judge of the other city will not decide based on that information alone. Because the informing judge, outside his jurisdiction, is like an ordinary person, and judgment is not given based solely on an ordinary person's information. Therefore, judgment will not be given on the information of the mentioned judge. Similarly, if two judges gather in a city that is outside both their jurisdictions, and one of them...

Commentary
This passage addresses the crucial question: what happens if the writing judge (al-qadi al-katib) dies or loses his judicial capacity after writing the letter but before the receiving judge (al-qadi al-maktub ilayhi) reads it to the defendant? Al-Hidayah states the Hanafi position: the letter becomes void (batil) and is not accepted. The writing judge must still be in office when the letter is actually read out in court. If he dies, is dismissed, becomes insane, unconscious, apostate, goes to dar al-harb, or even (according to some) becomes a fasiq (sinner), the letter is nullified. This applies whether the letter never reached the receiving judge or reached but was not yet read. The receiving judge cannot act on it. Opposing this are Imam Abu Yusuf (within the Hanafi school), Imam al-Shafi'i, and Imam Ahmad. They argue that kitab al-qadi is analogous to shahada 'ala al-shahada (testimony upon testimony). In the latter, the original witnesses testify before the writing judge, who then records it. The transfer of testimony is completed by the writing of the letter. Thus, if the secondary witnesses (shuhud al-far') testify and then die before the judge gives judgment, the judgment can still be given based on their testimony. Similarly, if the writing judge dies after writing the letter, the letter is still valid because the testimony transfer was complete when he wrote it. The Hanafi response (from Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) refutes this analogy. They argue that the transfer of testimony is not completed by mere writing; it is completed only when the receiving judge reads the letter to the defendant (or at least when the letter reaches the receiving judge). The writing judge's death before that point is like the death of the secondary witnesses before they give testimony. If secondary witnesses die before testifying, no judgment is given. Therefore, the letter is not valid until it is actually read in court. The Hanafi position is further supported by a rational argument: once the writing judge ceases to be a judge (through death or disqualification), he becomes an ordinary subject (min al-ra'aya). An ordinary person's judgment or written decision has no authority. Just as a judge's verbal statement outside his jurisdiction is not binding (because he is like a common man there), so too his written judgment becomes non-binding once he loses judicial capacity. The text concludes with a partial example about two judges meeting in a city outside their jurisdictions, which is cut off. This lesson clearly shows the inter-madhhab disagreement (Hanafi vs. Shafi'i and Ahmad) and even an intra-Hanafi difference (Abu Yusuf siding with the opposing schools).

Key Terms
کتاب القاضی الی القاضی (kitab al-qadi ila al-qadi): A letter from one judge to another conveying a judgment or testimony.
شہادت علی الشہادت (shahada 'ala al-shahada): Testimony upon testimony: secondary witnesses testify to the fact that primary witnesses gave testimony.
اہلیت قضاء (ahliyyat al-qada): The legal capacity to serve as a judge, including being Muslim, free, sane, etc.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), why does a judge's letter become void if the writing judge dies before the receiving judge reads it?
A) Because the seal might be broken.
B) Because the writing judge becomes an ordinary person whose judgment has no authority.
C) Because the letter must be returned to the deceased judge's heirs.
D) Because the witnesses must testify again.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, a judge's letter is only valid if the writing judge remains alive and qualified until the moment it is read to the defendant; otherwise, it becomes void.
